# BUILD: model-benchmark-harness

**Purpose:** Scientifically compare Codex 5.4 vs Claude Opus 4.7 on BuildRunner3 phase work. Produce a trustworthy default-runtime recommendation backed by ~300 task-level observations across 30 phases × 2 models × 3 replications × 2 sub-studies = 360 runs, with context-poisoning defenses and a third-party judge.

**Target Users:** Byron Hudson (BR3 maintainer). Secondary: anyone evaluating coding models on their own codebase.

**Tech Stack:** Python 3.11+ (`core/benchmark/` package), shell (`dispatch-to-node.sh`), BR3 cluster (Muddy, Otis, Lomax, Walter, Below, Lockwood), OpenRouter (third-party judge + paraphraser).

---

followed by existing `app.add_typer(spec_app, ...)`, `app.add_typer(tasks_app, ...)`, `app.add_typer(build_app, ...)`, `app.add_typer(quality_app, ...)`, etc. Phase 1 appends one more: `app.add_typer(benchmark_app, name="benchmark")`.

**`tests/__init__.py` — present.** `tests/integration/` subdir exists. **Phase 1 creates `tests/benchmark/__init__.py` (NEW)** as the empty package marker so pytest discovers Phase 1's own test modules (`test_models.py`, `test_registry.py`, `test_session_state.py`, `test_cli_skeleton.py`); the Files-list entries for these are in Phase 1's Files list. Phase 2 onwards adds additional test modules into the same directory without re-creating the init.

**`ui/package.json` — present and verified on 2026-04-16.** `python3 -c "import json; p=json.load(open('ui/package.json')); print(p['name'], p['scripts']['test'])"` returns `buildrunner-ui vitest`. Specifically: the file exists at `/Users/byronhudson/Projects/BuildRunner3/ui/package.json`, the top-level `"name"` key is `"buildrunner-ui"`, and `"scripts"."test"` is `"vitest"`. Phase 5's `run_local_tests(handle, runner)` gates its Node test surface on `<handle.clone_path>/ui/package.json` existing _in the contestant's clone_ (a contestant could delete or edit this file), so the verification here is that the **pre-phase** tree includes it; post-phase existence is checked per-run.

**`.buildrunner/builds/BUILD_*.md` — 34 files present**, for example `BUILD_1A_PRD_WIZARD.md`, `BUILD_cluster-build-orchestration.md`, `BUILD_walter-auto-provision.md`. This is the benchmark corpus.

**`.buildrunner/benchmarks/` — directory present** in the repo (as of 2026-04-16). Phase 1's `deps.py` startup calls `mkdir -p .buildrunner/benchmarks .buildrunner/benchmarks/prompts .buildrunner/benchmarks/results .buildrunner/benchmarks/reports .buildrunner/benchmarks/sessions` idempotently (a no-op when any directory already exists) and writes the initial `benchmark_registry.jsonl` + `sessions/index.json` into the top-level `.buildrunner/benchmarks/`. **Session state is stored per-session** under `.buildrunner/benchmarks/sessions/<session_id>.json` (see Phase 1's `session_state.py` deliverable for the canonical layout) — there is **NO** top-level `session-state.json`; earlier drafts that named such a file are superseded by the per-session layout, which is the single on-disk contract across the whole plan. The `prompts/` subdirectory is where Phase 3 writes per-run audit-trail prompt files (outside any worktree, so `git add -A` inside a worktree cannot sweep them into a scored commit). The `exclusions.jsonl` file at the top level is shared across Phase 2 (stratum violations) and Phase 4 (paraphrase/equivalence failures). Later phases only write into these directories; they never recreate them.

**Shared lock-resolution helper**: `core/benchmark/lockres.py` is created in Phase 2 and consumed by both the Phase 2 selector and the Phase 3 runner. Phase 3 therefore has Phase 2 in its Blocked-By list (see matrix).

**`~/.buildrunner/scripts/cluster-check.sh` — verified present** at `/Users/byronhudson/.buildrunner/scripts/cluster-check.sh` (executable, 9.9 KB, last modified 2026-04-15). This script lives in the user's global BuildRunner install (not in this repo's tree), which is why it isn't listed in the repo file layout. `deps.py` preflight asserts `[ -x ~/.buildrunner/scripts/cluster-check.sh ]` at startup, so a broken install fails fast. **Verified CLI contract (resolves R36 W2 — the script's own shebang-comment header documents this surface, and `deps.py` / `probe_node_pool()` consume only these invocations)**: (a) **Primary usage** — `NODE_URL=$(~/.buildrunner/scripts/cluster-check.sh <role>)` where `<role>` is a node role name drawn from the set `{otis, lomax, walter, muddy, below, lockwood, semantic-search, test-runner, parallel-builder, staging-server, inference, command, memory, sentinel, second-builder, forge, workhorse}` (role keys resolved against `~/.buildrunner/cluster.json`). **Output contract**: stdout is a single URL string (e.g. `http://10.0.1.103:8000`) when the role resolves to an online node whose 1-second health ping succeeds, OR an empty string when the role is unknown, the node is offline, or `BR3_CLUSTER=off` disables the check. **Exit code** is always `0` for primary-usage invocations — offline is signalled by empty stdout, not by a non-zero exit. `deps.probe_node_pool()` therefore treats `len(stdout.strip()) > 0` as the online signal, not the exit code. (b) **Structured mode** — `~/.buildrunner/scripts/cluster-check.sh --health-json <node_name>` returns a JSON object on stdout with fields `{node, ip, online, cpu_load, memory_pct, gpu_memory_pct?, gpu_temp?, ac_power, running_builds, via}` for local/remote machines; exit code `0` on success, `1` on malformed invocation (missing `<node_name>`). The harness only consumes primary-usage mode (`probe_node_pool()` calls `cluster-check.sh otis` / `cluster-check.sh lomax`); the structured mode is documented here for completeness but is not on any harness call path. (c) **No positional-argument interpretation beyond the role/--health-json switch** — the script rejects unknown flags silently by returning empty stdout. Unit test `test_deps.py::test_probe_node_pool_parses_cluster_check_stdout` mocks `subprocess.run(["cluster-check.sh", "otis"])` to return `("http://10.0.1.103:8000\n", 0)` and asserts the node is reported online; a second case returns `("", 0)` and asserts offline. This is the single verified surface the harness relies on; any future `cluster-check.sh` rewrite that changes the exit-code-vs-empty-stdout signal or the role-name set must land a companion update to `deps.py`'s preflight.

## Design Invariants (from research)

1. **N ≈ 300 checklist items** across 30 phases, 3 replications, 2 models, 2 sub-studies → 360 runs total.
2. **Third-party judge** (GPT-5 or Gemini via OpenRouter) — never Claude or Codex.
3. **Paraphraser is a third model** — Llama-3.1-405B via OpenRouter (not in contestant or judge pools). Local Below `Qwen-2.5-Coder` is fallback.
4. **Semantic-equivalence validator is a fourth system** — Below `/api/classify` NLI call. Not overlapping with paraphraser, judge, or contestants. **Known limitation (disclosed in methods section and caveats)**: Below's `/api/classify` is a general-purpose text classifier, not a purpose-built NLI model. Its ability to reliably discriminate "semantic equivalence" vs "partial" vs "diverged" between two BUILD-spec paraphrases is validated by the 20-pair human calibration (Phase 4) — Below is only accepted as primary validator when its observed agreement with Byron's labels is ≥ 80%; otherwise DeepSeek (a stronger LLM) is promoted. The methods section of the final report explicitly flags that a general-purpose classifier is an imperfect substitute for a dedicated NLI model, describes the calibration procedure, and reports the observed agreement rate as a first-class caveat.
5. **Training-cutoff stratification** — pre-cutoff vs post-cutoff phases reported separately; cutoffs read by `core/benchmark/training_cutoffs.py` from `.buildrunner/benchmarks/config.yaml:contestants.*_training_cutoff_utc` via `config.load_config()`. There is **no hardcoded date in `training_cutoffs.py`** — the module is a thin accessor that returns the values from `BenchmarkConfig.contestants`. Phase 2's selector calls into this accessor (the "constants" wording elsewhere in the plan refers to the values being frozen-per-study via config.yaml, not Python-level literals).
6. **Spec paraphrasing + recognition probe** defeat token-level memorization.
7. **Dual sub-study** — native prompts (each model's own skill) + neutral prompt (shared minimal).
8. **Double-pass judging with A/B swap** — position bias controlled, unstable pairs excluded.
9. **Format normalization** — Prettier (TS/JS) and Black (Python) applied to pre- and post-edit source files, then diff regenerated. Erases model-identity style tells.
10. **Judge-human calibration** — Byron scores 60 items (floor: 30) to validate judge agreement.
11. **Bradley-Terry pairwise ratings** + **Benjamini-Hochberg correction** on a pre-registered hypothesis list.
12. **Clustered bootstrap CIs** — items nested in phases, cluster on phase not item, 10k iterations.
13. **Chen 2021 pass@k** unbiased estimator for test-pass across replications.
14. **Node randomization** — each run's node assignment is randomized so that model × node is not confounded. `dispatch-to-node.sh` accepts any `(runtime, node)` combination (verified in the dependency table), so any model can run on any parallel-builder node. Pool: `{Otis, Lomax}` — both are M2 parallel-builder-tagged nodes in `cluster.json`. Allocation: each `(phase, model, replication, sub_study)` tuple draws a node such that every `model × node` cell has equal count within each phase (balanced incomplete block within phase). Lomax's staging-server role is served via its API endpoints (`/api/projects/{p}/build`) — those endpoints read a committed ref and are not contended by concurrent benchmark runs executing on the same machine; the benchmark run checks out into `/tmp/br3-bench-<uuid>/` worktrees that are distinct from Lomax's staging workspace. **Contention-measurement rule (precise)**: during the Phase 9 pilot only, the runner measures per-run wall-clock on both Otis and Lomax separately, groups by model × node, and computes the ratio `max(median_lomax, median_otis) / min(median_lomax, median_otis)`. If that ratio exceeds the threshold loaded from `.buildrunner/benchmarks/config.yaml:pilot.contention_ratio_threshold` (canonical default **1.10**, tunable via config without code change — `pilot_contention.py` reads this value via `load_config()` and never hardcodes the literal) after the per-bucket minimum has landed on each node (`config.yaml:pilot.contention_min_samples_per_bucket`, canonical default **8**, also config-loaded — sufficient for a stable median), Lomax is dropped from the pool for Phase 10 — specifically, the Phase 9 pilot writes its verdict to `.buildrunner/benchmarks/pilot_contention.json` (schema: `{drop_lomax: bool, ratio: Optional[float], otis_median_ms: Optional[int], lomax_median_ms: Optional[int], measured_at_utc: str}` — the three `Optional` fields are all-null together on the insufficient-sample fallback path; see Phase 9 Files list for the pydantic-level definition), and Phase 10's **own preflight in `deps.py`** reads that artifact and is the sole writer of `preflight_single_node` — so the "Phase 1 `deps.py` only" writer invariant holds. `deps.py` at Phase 10 preflight decides the flag as `preflight_single_node = (live_node_count == 1) OR (pilot_contention.json exists AND drop_lomax)`. If the pilot never ran `pilot_contention.json` is absent and the rule falls back to live node count only. The `node_name` regression covariate is auto-dropped per Phase 7's single-level-factor rule when `preflight_single_node=true`. The pilot-side check runs once at end-of-pilot, not continuously — this is the simplest rule that avoids mid-run pool flapping. Outcome is also logged human-readably to `.buildrunner/benchmarks/reports/pilot_contention.md`; the machine-readable `.json` is what `deps.py` consumes.
15. **Recognition probe is non-priming** — run in a fresh OS process _after_ the scored run, never before. Probe process has no access to prior run state.
16. **Paraphrase-fail = phase-fail (balanced)** — if the paraphraser or equivalence validator fails after 3 retries with different seeds, the entire **phase** (not just one replication) is dropped from both models and both sub-studies so that cell balance is preserved. The phase is re-drawn from the candidate pool. Never fall back to the original spec (that would violate Invariant 6). This keeps pass@k denominators and model × node cells balanced across the analysis. Excluded phases are logged in the report.
17. **Pre-registered decision rule** — `runtime.json` default is changed iff the _lower bound_ of the 95% clustered-bootstrap CI on the Bradley-Terry rating gap favors the challenger on **both** sub-studies and a tie-breaker cost metric does not veto. Rule written to `.buildrunner/benchmarks/decision-rule.md` before Phase 10 runs.
18. **Atomic artifact writes** — full-file artifacts (`config.yaml`, reports, exports) are written via `tmp + fsync + rename`. The JSONL registry is an **append-log**, written with `O_APPEND` + `fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX)` per append (see Phase 1). **Resume is keyed on `cell_key`, not `run_id`** (retries mint new `run_id`s per Invariant 6/claim-dedup contract, so `run_id`-keyed skip would re-run cells). `runner.resume()` scans `benchmark_registry.jsonl`, reduces rows by `cell_key` using the two-level reducer defined in Phase 1, and skips cells whose reduced row has `stage in {"scored","judged"}` or a live non-expired lease; cells with only expired/superseded rows are eligible for a fresh attempt with a newly-minted `run_id`.
19. **Single harness caveat** — results apply to BR3 dispatch only, disclosed in report header.

---

## Phases

### Phase 1: Foundation + Data Models + Registry

**Goal:** `br benchmark --help` prints full subcommand list. All dataclasses defined. Registry file initialized. External dependency paths asserted at startup.

**Files:**

- `core/benchmark/__init__.py` (NEW)
- `core/benchmark/models.py` (NEW)
- `core/benchmark/cli.py` (NEW — Typer app that imports 12 command-implementation modules listed below and calls each module's `register(app)` hook. **CLI export-name contract (resolves R29 B1)**: `cli.py`'s module-level Typer instance is the single symbol `benchmark_app = typer.Typer(name="benchmark", help="BR3 model-benchmark harness")`. That same object is re-exported under the alias `app = benchmark_app` at module scope so both the `python -m core.benchmark.cli` entrypoint and the `core/benchmark/__main__.py` wrapper (`from .cli import app; app()`) resolve to the identical Typer instance — there is no second Typer object anywhere in the package. BR3's top-level `cli/main.py` imports `benchmark_app` (the canonical name) and calls `app.add_typer(benchmark_app, name="benchmark")`; `__main__.py` imports `app` (the alias) for terseness. `cli.py`'s `__all__ = ["app", "benchmark_app"]` makes both names part of the public surface. `cli.py` itself is **only modified by Phase 1**; every later phase that implements a subcommand does so by **replacing the contents of its own `cli_<cmd>.py`** module without touching `cli.py`. This avoids MODIFY conflicts on `cli.py` across phases and keeps the build order's file-conflict matrix clean.)
- `core/benchmark/cli_run.py`, `cli_select.py`, `cli_score.py`, `cli_judge.py`, `cli_paraphrase.py`, `cli_probe.py`, `cli_validate.py`, `cli_report.py`, `cli_resume.py`, `cli_status.py`, `cli_gc_anchors.py`, `cli_record_contracts.py` (NEW — **12 stub modules**, one per subcommand. Each defines `def register(app: typer.Typer) -> None:` with a `--help`-only Typer command body. Later phases **replace the contents** of their own stub (MODIFY in that phase's Files list) with the real implementation — Phase 2 fills in `cli_select.py` + `cli_record_contracts.py`; Phase 3 fills `cli_run.py` + `cli_resume.py` + `cli_status.py` + `cli_gc_anchors.py`; Phase 4 fills `cli_paraphrase.py` + `cli_probe.py`; Phase 5 fills `cli_score.py`; Phase 6 fills `cli_judge.py`; Phase 8 fills `cli_validate.py` + `cli_report.py`. Phase 5's `cli_gc_anchors.py` update also adds the `--reset-venv` flag that triggers end-of-session venv recreation. Phase 7 has no dedicated CLI command (aggregator runs inside `report`), so it does not modify any `cli_*.py`.)
- `core/benchmark/registry.py` (NEW — atomic JSONL writer/reader for `benchmark_registry.jsonl`)
- `core/benchmark/__main__.py` (NEW — one-line module entrypoint `from .cli import app; app()` so `python -m core.benchmark --help` works as a convenience alias alongside `python -m core.benchmark.cli --help`.)
- `tests/benchmark/__init__.py` (NEW — empty package marker so pytest discovers every Phase-1-through-Phase-8 `tests/benchmark/*.py` module. Created here in Phase 1 so Phase 1's success criteria — which include unit tests for dataclasses, registry round-trip, and CLI skeleton — can actually be satisfied in the stated build order.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_models.py` (NEW — pydantic round-trip tests for `PhaseSpec`, every `RegistryRow` variant, `LocalTestResult`, `SessionState`.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_registry.py` (NEW — write+read+reduce tests including progressive-fill stage precedence and cell-key-keyed claim dedup.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_session_state.py` (NEW — atomic write, set_flag validation, dict-write helper for `redraw_map`.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_cli_skeleton.py` (NEW — asserts `python -m core.benchmark --help` and `python -m core.benchmark.cli --help` both return 0 and list every subcommand.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_config.py` (NEW — asserts `load_config()` parses `.buildrunner/benchmarks/config.yaml` into every declared `BenchmarkConfig` field.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_deps.py` (NEW — **resolves R36 B5**. Unit tests for `core/benchmark/deps.py`'s preflight surface. - `tests/benchmark/test_installer_order.py` (NEW — **resolves R30 B2 + R35 B3**. Asserts that after `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh` runs against a synthetic repo containing both `requirements-benchmark.txt` (pinning `pytest>=7.4,<9.0`) and a second `requirements-example.txt` (pinning `pytest>=7.0` — a broader range that **overlaps** the harness pin), the installed `pytest` version falls inside the harness's narrower `[7.4, 9.0)` window — proving the two-pass install order correctly makes `requirements-benchmark.txt`'s pins win on overlap. **The pins are deliberately compatible** (the broader `>=7.0` contains the harness's `>=7.4,<9.0`), because the test's purpose is to prove **ordering-wins-on-overlap**, not to exercise the `ResolutionImpossible` → `install_failed` path (which is the separate contradictory-pins scenario documented in Phase 5's `runner._detect_venv_drift` contract where a contestant pins `pytest>=9.0` against the harness's `<9.0`). Using contradictory pins here would trip pip's resolver and `set -euo pipefail` would abort the installer before the assertion could run — that is a legitimate runtime behavior but it does not validate the two-pass ordering contract this test covers. The test uses a `tmp_path` synthetic repo, subprocess-invokes the installer, and parses `.venv-benchmark/bin/pip show pytest` output; it asserts the parsed `Version:` line satisfies the harness pin `>=7.4,<9.0` via `packaging.version.Version`.)
- `core/benchmark/config.py` (NEW — `load_config()` helper that parses `.buildrunner/benchmarks/config.yaml` into a Pydantic `BenchmarkConfig` model. **Phase 1 declares the full Pydantic schema up-front, locking every field every later phase will ever need so no subsequent phase has to modify this file.** The complete `BenchmarkConfig` fields declared in Phase 1: `openrouter: OpenRouterConfig { paraphraser_primary: str, paraphraser_secondary: str, judge_primary: str, judge_secondary: str, equivalence_fallback: str }` — **these five role-specific fields are the single source of truth for every OpenRouter model identifier the harness consumes.** Phase 4's paraphraser reads `config.openrouter.paraphraser_primary` / `paraphraser_secondary` directly; Phase 4's equivalence fallback reads `config.openrouter.equivalence_fallback`; Phase 6's judge reads `config.openrouter.judge_primary` / `judge_secondary`. **There is no `required_models: list[str]` field** — `deps.py`'s preflight computes the list of IDs to verify against OpenRouter's `/v1/models` response from the five role-specific fields at preflight time via `required = [c.openrouter.paraphraser_primary, c.openrouter.paraphraser_secondary, c.openrouter.judge_primary, c.openrouter.judge_secondary, c.openrouter.equivalence_fallback]` (de-duplicated). This keeps the role-to-model mapping explicit and typed: a misconfigured `judge_primary` surfaces as a role-specific remediation message, not a lost role-assignment in a flat list; `pool: PoolConfig { nodes: list[str], single_node_retry_backoff_seconds: int }`; `registry: RegistryConfig { lease_seconds: int, judge_lease_seconds: int }` (canonical defaults: `lease_seconds=1800` for `ClaimRow`/`HeartbeatRow` run-scoped leases, `judge_lease_seconds=900` for `JudgeClaimRow` pair-scoped leases — both tunable via config without code change; Phase 6's `registry.claim_judge()` reads `judge_lease_seconds` and Phase 3's `runner.dispatch_run` reads `lease_seconds`); `blinding: BlindingConfig { blind_salt: str }`; `selector: SelectorConfig { target_phases: int, buffer_phases: int, replications: int, sub_studies: list[Literal["native","neutral"]] }` (canonical default: `sub_studies=["native","neutral"]` per Invariant 7 dual-sub-study design; declared here in Phase 1 so Phase 6's `run_session` can compute `expected_cell_count = len(config.selector.sub_studies) * config.selector.replications` from a declared field rather than a hardcoded literal, and so Phase 7's regression can iterate `config.selector.sub_studies` for the per-sub-study stratification — **resolves R37 B1**); `scorer: ScorerConfig { python_test_timeout_seconds: int, node_test_timeout_seconds: int, install_timeout_seconds: int, venv_lock_timeout_seconds: int }`; `judge: JudgeConfig { position_swap_enabled: bool, rater_disagreement_dim_threshold: int }`; `pilot: PilotConfig { sample_size_gate_floor: int, human_agreement_gate: float, contention_ratio_threshold: float, contention_min_samples_per_bucket: int }`; `contestants: ContestantsConfig { claude_runtime_flag: str, claude_model_version: str, claude_training_cutoff_utc: str, codex_runtime_flag: str, codex_model_version: str, codex_training_cutoff_utc: str }` — **the single source of truth for the `(model_version → dispatch-to-node.sh --runtime flag)` mapping so the study is reproducible against a specific model version**. Canonical values for the current study, frozen before Phase 10 launches: `claude_runtime_flag="claude"`, `claude_model_version="claude-opus-4-7"`, `claude_training_cutoff_utc="2026-01-31T00:00:00Z"`, `codex_runtime_flag="codex"`, `codex_model_version="codex-5-4"`, `codex_training_cutoff_utc="2025-11-01T00:00:00Z"`. Phase 3's `runner.dispatch_run` reads `config.contestants.<model>_runtime_flag` to populate the `--runtime <flag>` argv; `training_cutoffs.py` (Phase 2) reads the `_training_cutoff_utc` fields; the report (Phase 8) prints the `_model_version` fields in the methods section so readers know exactly which versions were benchmarked. Any later-session comparison against a newer Codex or Claude version must bump these config values and re-run the full study — the model-version → runtime-flag mapping is not re-inferred anywhere else in the codebase. This list covers every configurable knob the 10 phases introduce; **Phase 1 is the sole writer of `config.py` and no later phase modifies it** — any later-phase knob that needs a config value must use one of the fields above (or a runtime-loaded literal), not add a new schema field. If a genuinely-new knob is discovered during implementation, the plan requires a re-spec pass rather than a silent cross-phase edit. Single source of truth for every phase that reads config.)

Canonical contents (Phase 1 owns the initial write; later phases may only append entries, never remove): `benchmarks/layer-cache.json`, `benchmarks/api-status.json`, `benchmarks/layer_provenance.json`, `benchmarks/sessions/`, `benchmarks/results/`, `benchmarks/prompts/`, `benchmarks/pilot_contention.json`, `benchmarks/benchmark_registry.jsonl`, `benchmarks/exclusions.jsonl`, `benchmarks/previews/`, `benchmarks/.git-gc-config-backup.json` (**resolves R54 Codex W1** — the append-only registry/exclusions JSONL files, preview-session directories, and the gc.auto backup file are all harness runtime artifacts that must never be committed; earlier drafts omitted these and a fresh `git add -A` could have committed them. The gc-backup entry additionally protects against a kill-mid-session leak where the backup file persists across a process crash; adding it to `.gitignore` guarantees the recovery path is not polluted by the backup file accidentally landing in a commit). The file is created by `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh` on first run (idempotent: re-runs assert content matches and append any new entries introduced by later phases). Listed here so the owning phase is explicit and Phase 2's layer-cache reference has a real on-disk ignore rule.)
- `cli/main.py` (MODIFY — add `from core.benchmark.cli import benchmark_app` and `app.add_typer(benchmark_app, name="benchmark")`)
- `requirements-benchmark.txt` (NEW — **Phase 1 owns the full pin list** so Phase 2+ can rely on `pydantic`, `responses`, `vcrpy` from the start. The canonical list is: `typer>=0.9.0` (CLI framework — **resolves R36 B1** + **resolves R54 Claude B1**: the upper bound `<1.0` was removed because the project's root `pyproject.toml` pins `typer>=0.9.0` without an upper bound, so a contestant edit that pulls the project's pyproject into the shared venv via pass-1 install would resolve typer to a newer major (e.g. `1.x`). Pass-2's install of `requirements-benchmark.txt` would then see a conflicting pin (`<1.0` vs `>=0.9.0`), emit `ResolutionImpossible`, trigger `runner._detect_venv_drift`, recreate `.venv-benchmark/`, re-run pass 1 (which re-introduces typer `1.x`), and loop. Removing the upper bound makes the harness pin a strict subset of the project pin — pip's resolver picks a single compatible version on both passes, no drift is detected, and the recreate loop cannot start. The harness's `import typer` surfaces are first-party (`core/benchmark/cli*.py` command bodies) and use only the stable `app.add_typer(...)` / `@app.command()` decorator surface that predates 0.9, so the upper-bound cap did not guard against any real API break: the `.venv-benchmark/` venv is isolated from the project's root install, so `typer` must be pinned here so `core/benchmark/cli.py` and every `cli_*.py` module can `import typer` inside the benchmark venv; the project's `requirements-api.txt` does not list typer, so without this pin `python -m core.benchmark.cli --help` would `ImportError` immediately), `PyYAML>=6.0,<7.0` (config.yaml loader dep — `core/benchmark/config.py:load_config()` calls `yaml.safe_load()`; required in the benchmark venv for the same isolation reason as typer), `requests>=2.31,<3.0` (used by `deps.py`'s OpenRouter/Below/Walter/Lomax HTTP probes and by Phase 2's `api_clients.py`; harness-only dep so it ships in the benchmark venv), `pytest>=7.4,<9.0`, `pytest-timeout>=2.2,<3.0`, `statsmodels>=0.14,<0.15`, `scipy>=1.11,<2.0`, `numpy>=1.26`, `pandas>=2.1,<3.0`, `scikit-learn>=1.4,<2.0`, `pydantic>=2.5,<3.0`, `responses>=0.24`, `vcrpy>=5.1`, `black>=24.3,<25.0`, `ruff>=0.4,<1.0`, `lizard>=1.17,<2.0`, `packaging>=23.0,<26.0` (used by Phase 5's `runner._detect_venv_drift` for PEP 440 `Version` comparison — `from packaging.version import Version` is imported there; on modern pip `packaging` is already a pip transitive dep but the harness pins it explicitly so `import packaging.version` in the drift detector never fails in a minimal venv). `pytest` + `pytest-timeout` are in Phase 1's venv because (a) Phase 2+ unit tests run from `.venv-benchmark/` and (b) Phase 5's `run_local_tests(handle, runner)` invokes `.venv-benchmark/bin/pytest` against each contestant's clone. Phase 5 does **not** modify this file; it only adds the Node toolchain installer. **pytest upper-bound rationale (resolves R24 N10)**: `pytest<9.0` is a deliberate reproducibility floor — pytest 9+ introduces collection-API changes that would silently break the scorer's `--tb=no --no-cov` parse if a contestant pinned `pytest>=9` in a root `requirements*.txt` edit mid-study. The shared venv is **monotonically widened** by contestant edits (not replaced), so pinning `pytest<9` here guarantees the scorer's invocation semantics stay stable across all 360 runs. If a contestant's diff pins `pytest>=9.0`, the version-drift check (cross-major-version detection described in Phase 5's `venv_version_drift` path) fires and the venv is recreated, but the recreation re-runs `pip install -r requirements-benchmark.txt` **after** the contestant's file, so the harness's `pytest<9` pin wins on the dependency resolver's last-write (pip installs `requirements-benchmark.txt` last in Phase 1's installer loop; pip's resolver picks the intersection of pins, so `pytest<9` caps the contestant's `>=9`). That produces a `ResolutionImpossible` error from pip, which the runner catches and surfaces as `status="install_failed", reason="pytest_version_conflict"` — scored as a model failure. This is intentional: a contestant's pytest-9-only plugin is not a supported scenario in the study, and the error path documents it explicitly rather than silently breaking the scorer's parse.)
- `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh` (NEW — **Phase 1 owns Python toolchain install** only. Starts with the canonical `#!/usr/bin/env bash` shebang and `set -euo pipefail` for fail-fast behavior. Creates `.venv-benchmark/` and installs requirements in **two ordered passes** so the harness's pins win over any contestant-introduced pin: **Pass 1** — any non-harness root `requirements*.txt` files (i.e. every file matching `requirements*.txt` EXCEPT `requirements-benchmark.txt`) installed first via `shopt -s nullglob; for req in requirements*.txt; do [ "$req" = "requirements-benchmark.txt" ] && continue; .venv-benchmark/bin/pip install -r "$req"; done`. **Pass 2** — `requirements-benchmark.txt` installed LAST via `.venv-benchmark/bin/pip install -r requirements-benchmark.txt`. pip's resolver respects the last-installed pin set as the authoritative constraint, so harness pins (e.g. `pytest<9.0`) override any earlier-loaded overlap. The two-pass order is mandatory — a single-pass loop that happens to iterate in lexicographic order would put `requirements-api.txt` after `requirements-benchmark.txt` and silently reverse the priority. Phase 5's `install-benchmark-tools.sh` delegates to this script for the Python side and only adds the `npm` install step. Idempotent: re-runs skip the venv-creation step if `.venv-benchmark/bin/python` already exists; both passes re-run `pip install -r` to pick up drift. **Parent-repo gc.auto backup/restore owner (resolves R53 B3 — Phase 3's GC-safety design references gc.auto disable/restore behavior on this installer script + the `.buildrunner/benchmarks/.git-gc-config-backup.json` backup file, but no phase previously owned adding that logic to any file. Phase 1 owns this installer and therefore Phase 1 owns the gc.auto lifecycle: the installer is the single-writer of the backup file)**: at session-start (invoked by `br benchmark run` / `br benchmark resume` via `cli_run.py`'s startup hook before any dispatching), the installer writes the session's owning `session_id` (passed in via a required `--session-id` flag newly added to this script, populated by the caller from `SessionState.session_id`) plus the current parent-repo values of `gc.auto` and `gc.autoPackLimit` into `.buildrunner/benchmarks/.git-gc-config-backup.json` via `tmp+fsync+rename` atomic-write (schema: `{"owning_session_id": str, "gc_auto": str, "gc_auto_pack_limit": str, "backup_created_at_utc": str}`), then executes `git -C <PARENT_REPO> config gc.auto 0` + `git -C <PARENT_REPO> config gc.autoPackLimit 0`. If the backup file already exists with a different `owning_session_id` and a running-pid lock file (`/tmp/br3-bench-session-<owning_session_id>.lock`) is NOT held, the installer calls `deps._recover_orphaned_gc_config()` first (Phase 1's orphan-recovery helper, declared alongside the preflight functions) to clean up the prior session's leak before writing its own backup. At session-end (invoked by `cli_run.py`'s finally-block AND by `br benchmark gc-anchors --reset-venv`), the installer's companion function `restore_gc_config()` reads the backup file, calls `git -C <PARENT_REPO> config gc.auto <backup.gc_auto>` + `git -C <PARENT_REPO> config gc.autoPackLimit <backup.gc_auto_pack_limit>`, and deletes the backup file. The `deps.execution_preflight()` / `deps.offline_preflight()` / `deps.scoring_preflight()` / `deps.analysis_preflight()` / `deps.select_preflight()` entry points all call `deps._recover_orphaned_gc_config()` at startup to catch leaks from killed sessions, as documented in Phase 3's `setup_clone` keepalive-ref deliverable. Unit test `tests/benchmark/test_installer_gc_backup.py::test_install_writes_gc_backup_with_session_id` (NEW — added to Phase 1's Files list alongside `test_installer_order.py`) asserts the installer writes the backup file with the session_id, `gc.auto=0` is applied to the parent, and `restore_gc_config` restores the prior values and deletes the backup file. Companion test `test_install_recovers_orphaned_backup_from_killed_session` seeds a backup with a stale session_id (no lock file held) and asserts the installer triggers `_recover_orphaned_gc_config` before writing its own backup. A unit-level test in `tests/benchmark/test_installer_order.py` asserts that after install, `.venv-benchmark/bin/pip show pytest` reports the version that satisfies `requirements-benchmark.txt`'s `<9.0` pin rather than whichever pytest an earlier requirements file may have pulled in.)
- `core/benchmark/session_state.py` (NEW — typed JSON session-state files under `.buildrunner/benchmarks/sessions/` — **the canonical on-disk layout is a per-session file `.buildrunner/benchmarks/sessions/<session_id>.json` plus a single session registry `.buildrunner/benchmarks/sessions/index.json`; there is NO top-level `session-state.json`**. Any earlier reference in this plan to "`.buildrunner/benchmarks/session-state.json`" is superseded by this canonical layout — that path is **not** created and is **not** read by any code path. Tests, resume logic, and preflight writers all agree on the per-session path. The read/write/flag helpers: `get_flag(session_id, key)`, `set_flag(session_id, key, value)`, `clear_flag(session_id, key)` — every helper is session-scoped and takes the `session_id` as the first argument; there is no global-session read path. Stores preflight outcomes, which Phase 7 regression code reads. Writes are atomic via `tmp + fsync + rename` **AND serialized via a per-session-file `fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX)` on `/tmp/br3-bench-session-<session_id>.lock` around the full `read-modify-write` cycle (resolves R48 W5 — two concurrent `run_cell` invocations for different phases in the same session could otherwise race on the per-session file's tmp+fsync+rename, and the phase-scoped paraphrase flock only serializes within a single phase_id, not across phases)**. Every `get_flag`/`set_flag`/`clear_flag`/`set_map_entry` helper acquires the per-session flock as its first operation, performs the read-modify-write inside the lock, and releases the flock on exit. The lock is session-scoped (not global) so two concurrent sessions' writes to their own per-session files do not serialize against each other — the lock filename includes `session_id` so `flock()` contention is isolated per session. The per-session flock contract is additive to the existing tmp+fsync+rename atomicity: tmp+fsync+rename guarantees no partial write is ever visible on disk (crash safety), and the flock guarantees no two in-flight writers produce a lost-update race (concurrency safety). Unit test `test_session_state.py::test_concurrent_set_flag_no_lost_update` spawns two threads that both call `set_flag(session_id, "redraw_map", ...)` on disjoint keys concurrently and asserts the final map contains both keys (a lost-update would drop one). Schema (pydantic `SessionState` model, declared in full in Phase 1 so no later phase adds fields; every declared field has exactly one writer phase — no stranded fields): `{"preflight_below_unreachable": bool (writer: Phase 1 deps.py), "preflight_walter_unreachable": bool (writer: Phase 1 deps.py), "preflight_lomax_unreachable": bool (writer: Phase 1 deps.py), "preflight_single_node": bool (writer: **Phase 1 deps.py only** — set at preflight from `probe*node*pool()`and never updated mid-run; Phase 3's`node_allocator`is a pure **reader** of this flag, not a writer. If a node goes offline mid-run after a two-node preflight, the allocator continues with the remaining node for subsequent cells but does NOT flip`preflight_single_node`— that is a preflight snapshot, not a live gauge. Phase 7's regression additionally falls back to observed`node_name`cardinality in the dataset when deciding whether to drop the`node_name`covariate, so a mid-run collapse is still caught by the analysis without requiring a mid-run flag write), "preflight_nodes_online": list[str] (writer: Phase 1 deps.py), "preflight_timestamp_utc": str (writer: Phase 1 deps.py), "redraw_map": dict[str, str] (writer: **Phase 2 selector ONLY** — maps `dropped_phase_id → replacement_phase_id`for idempotent phase replacement per Phase 2's`redraw`contract; default`{}`on fresh session-state; Phase 3/4 failure paths read this map via`selector.redraw`but never write session-state directly), "selected_phase_ids": list[str] (writer: **Phase 2 selector ONLY** — ordered list of `phase_id`s the selector drew into the session's buffer via `select()`/`select_with_buffer()`. Default `[]`on fresh session-state. Written atomically once per draw call via`set_flag("selected_phase_ids", [...])`; appended-to (never mutated in place) when `redraw()`mints a replacement. **Resolves R31 B6**: after a kill/resume, Phase 3's`runner.resume(session_id)`reads this list +`selector_cache`to reconstruct which phases are in scope without re-running the stratified draw — the draw is inherently non-deterministic across restarts (seed is session-scoped but the candidate pool's exclusion state can change mid-session via`benchmark_registry.jsonl`additions), so we persist the result, not the draw). "selector_cache": dict[str, dict] (writer: **Phase 2 selector ONLY** — persists the`PhaseSpec`objects the selector has drawn so far. Keyed by`phase_id`; each value is the pydantic-serialized `PhaseSpec.model_dump()`dict. Default`{}`on fresh session-state. Populated synchronously by every selector method that mints a new`PhaseSpec` (`select`, `select_with_buffer`, `redraw`) via `set_map_entry("selector_cache", phase_id, phase_spec_dict)`. **Resolves R31 B6**: Phase 3's `runner.resume()`and Phase 2's`selector.get_phase(phase_id)`both materialize a`PhaseSpec`on demand by looking up`selector_cache[phase_id]`in session-state and validating back into the`PhaseSpec`pydantic model — no in-memory-only candidate cache; the cache is disk-backed from the first draw. This is the single source of truth that binds the selector's live object-cache to the disk-persisted session so a kill/restart can rebuild`selector.get_phase`behavior by re-hydrating`selector_cache`. Size ceiling: with the target of 30 phases + worst-case `target + buffer`over-draw at ~50 entries × ~2 KB per`PhaseSpec.model_dump` (the PhaseSpec carries the phase_id, file list, and checklist items), the cache stays ≤ 100 KB — well within the atomic-file-write budget.), "resume_session_id": str (writer: **Phase 1 deps.py ONLY**; **per-session file, not a global single-writer slot — resolves R25 W4 concurrent-orchestrator clobber**. Session-state is **partitioned per-session** on disk: each active session writes to its own file`.buildrunner/benchmarks/sessions/<session_id>.json`(the generic file path`.buildrunner/benchmarks/session-state.json`named earlier is the logical schema label; the concrete on-disk path is the per-session file). A companion **session registry**`.buildrunner/benchmarks/sessions/index.json`tracks active session ids and is rewritten atomically under`/tmp/br3-bench-sessions-index.lock` (fcntl.flock, same pattern as the registry). Startup logic: **`br benchmark run`** mints a fresh `session_id = uuid4()`, acquires the sessions-index lock, reads `active_session_ids`, appends the new id, atomically rewrites the index, releases the lock, then creates the per-session file with `resume_session_id=<session_id>`, preflight flags, AND `selected_models=<cli_parsed_models_list>`(the list parsed from the operator's`--models`CLI flag after validation — the canonical short runtime_flag keys like`["claude"]`, `["codex"]`, or `["claude","codex"]`; defaults to `["claude","codex"]`when`--models`is omitted, matching the`cli_run.py`flag default. **Resolves R46 B2**: this is the single on-disk persistence point for the`--models`subset, which both the initial-draw scheduler and the resume-path scheduler later consume via`session_state.get_flag(session_id, "selected_models")`so`run_session`'s `models` parameter reflects the operator's intent across kill/resume cycles). **`br benchmark resume [--session-id <id>]`** requires `--session-id`when`len(active_session_ids) > 1`; when exactly one id is active, `--session-id` is optional and defaults to it; when zero active, the command errors with a remediation message. **`br benchmark run --session-id <existing_id>`is explicitly NOT supported** —`run`always mints a new id,`resume`is the only path that re-uses one. **Concurrent-orchestrator semantics**: two`br benchmark run`invocations on Muddy both mint unique UUIDs, both append to`index.json`under the flock (one waits for the other's write), and both write their own per-session files with zero overlap. A subsequent`br benchmark resume --session-id <A>`picks session A's file;`--session-id <B>`picks session B's. Neither orchestrator's preflight write can clobber the other's. **Session-index cleanup**: on clean`br benchmark run`/`resume`exit, the final action re-acquires the sessions-index lock and removes the session id from`active_session_ids`, leaving the per-session file on disk as an audit artifact. `br benchmark gc-anchors --reset-venv`additionally accepts`--prune-sessions`to delete per-session files older than 30 days. Phase 3's`runner.resume(session_id)` only **reads** the corresponding per-session file — it never writes session-state. This preserves the single-writer invariant **and** the concurrent-orchestrator contract.)}`. "display_label": Optional[str] (writer: **Phase 1 deps.py ONLY** — default `None`; set at session-creation time to the operator-supplied `--session-id` value if it differs from the minted `uuid4`, else `None`. This is the display-label field Phase 3's CLI flag description references; it is never read by resume logic, never used for registry filtering, and never used to route writes — it exists solely so the startup banner and report can show the operator-supplied label alongside the authoritative uuid4. Resolves R31 W1/W5 cleanly), "is_preview": bool (writer: **Phase 2 `core/benchmark/cli_select.py` preview-bootstrap path ONLY — resolves R47 W1 writer-conflict**; earlier text nominally attributed the writer to Phase 1 deps.py, but the actual logic that mints a preview session lives in Phase 2's `cli_select.py` and the single-writer invariant must match the code path that actually writes. Phase 1's `deps.py` owns only the generic preflight-flag writers (`preflight**\_unreachable`); `is_preview`is set exclusively by Phase 2's`cli_select.py`when the operator invokes`br benchmark select`standalone without an active`run`session. Default`False`; set to `True`exclusively by that preview-bootstrap path. **Resolves R46 B1** — pre-declared here in Phase 1 so Phase 2's`cli_select.py`preview-session bootstrap is pure consumer code; the frozen-schema invariant holds: no later phase adds fields to`SessionState`. Readers: (a) `br benchmark resume`filters the sessions-index disambiguation list to exclude any session whose per-session file has`is_preview==True`, so preview sessions never appear as candidates for resume; (b) Phase 3's `runner.resume(session_id)`refuses to load a preview session-state file and exits with a remediation message directing the operator to`br benchmark run`for a real session; (c) Phase 7's aggregator filters preview sessions out of the analysis dataset by joining`CompletedRow.session_id`against the set of non-preview session ids (preview sessions do not contribute to Bradley-Terry ratings or mixed-effects regression). Single-writer-per-field holds: only Phase 2's`cli_select.py`preview-bootstrap path sets`is_preview=True`via`set_flag(session_id, "is_preview", True)`at session creation; no later phase ever writes this field. **Preview-session vs`active_session_ids`contract** (resolves R46 warning): a preview session IS appended to`active_session_ids`in`sessions/index.json`(so the session-id remains globally unique and never collides with a concurrent non-preview session), but the`resume`disambiguation filter above elides it. The sessions-index cleanup path on`br benchmark select`exit additionally removes preview-session ids from`active_session_ids`so the index does not accumulate stale entries. Preview sessions' per-session files ARE written to disk (as audit artifacts) and are eligible for`br benchmark gc-anchors --prune-sessions`cleanup after the 30-day retention window), "preview_created_at_utc": Optional[str] (writer: **Phase 2 `core/benchmark/cli_select.py` preview-bootstrap path ONLY — sibling to `is_preview`, same R47 W1 writer-conflict resolution**; default `None`; set to the UTC ISO-8601 timestamp at the exact moment `br benchmark select`'s preview-bootstrap path mints the preview session, synchronously with `is_preview=True`. Non-preview sessions leave this field `None`. Sibling declaration to `is_preview`— resolves R46 B1 alongside it. Readers: the startup banner for preview sessions shows this timestamp so the operator can confirm the preview is fresh;`gc-anchors --prune-sessions`uses this timestamp (rather than file mtime) to compute the 30-day retention window for preview-session files), "selected_models": list[str] (writer: **Phase 1 deps.py ONLY** — the list of short runtime_flag model keys the operator selected via`br benchmark run --models <csv>`(canonical values:`"claude"`, `"codex"`), persisted at session-creation time so `resume`can reconstruct the exact same model subset after a kill. Default value on a fresh session-state is`["claude", "codex"]`(the full set — matches the existing`--models`default when the flag is omitted). **Resolves R46 B2** — pre-declared here in Phase 1 as part of the frozen SessionState schema so Phase 3's`run_session(selector, replications, models, sub_studies)`scheduler and Phase 6's`run_session`/`resume`body extensions can iterate the actual subset (via`for model in models:`where`models`is either the CLI-parsed list passed directly to`run_session`or, on resume, re-read from this session-state field via`session_state.get_flag(session_id, "selected_models")`) instead of the previously-hardcoded `for model in ("claude", "codex"):`tuple. Without this field, a single-model run like`--models claude`would still register codex`(phase, model)`pairs with the probe scheduler at startup, causing`\_maybe_fire`to wait for codex cell completions that will never exist, so recognition probes would never fire. Every scheduler loop site — Phase 3's initial-draw`run_session`body, Phase 3's replacement-phase scheduler extension, Phase 6's`run_session`body extension, Phase 6's`Runner.resume()`body extension, and Phase 3/Phase 6`cli_run.py`/`cli_resume.py`call sites — iterates this subset exclusively. Unit test`test_runner.py::test_run_session_respects_models_subset`constructs a session with`selected_models=["claude"]`and asserts`probe_scheduler.schedule()`is called only for`model="claude"`(never`"codex"`) across every `(phase, model)`registration path). All three`preflight\*\*\_unreachable`booleans default to`False`so a fresh session-state file is valid.`set_flag(key, value)`pydantic-validates the key against this schema AND pydantic-validates`value`against the declared type for that key (scalar for`bool`/`str`fields,`dict[str, str]`for`redraw_map`); writes of unknown keys OR type-mismatched values raise at runtime rather than being silently dropped. A companion helper **`set_map_entry(session_id: str, key: str, sub_key: str, sub_value)`** (sole-purpose: dict-valued flags like `redraw_map`/`selector_cache`; **resolves R39 B2** — `session_id`is the first argument, matching the`get_flag(session_id, key)`/`set_flag(session_id, key, value)`/`clear_flag(session_id, key)`signatures declared above; no helper takes a 2-arg form) reads the current`dict[str, Any]`value for`key`under the given`session_id`, inserts `{sub_key: sub_value}`, and atomically writes back via the same `tmp+fsync+rename`; pydantic validates the key is a dict-typed field before the write. Phase 2's selector uses `set_map_entry(session_id, "redraw_map", dropped_phase_id, replacement_phase_id)`for its idempotent redraw bookkeeping — the scalar`set_flag`call path is never used for`redraw_map`. OpenRouter reachability is **not** tracked as a soft-degrade flag because OpenRouter is a hard-fail dependency at preflight — `OPENROUTER_API_KEY`env check at line 157 plus the five role-specific 1-token`POST /api/v1/chat/completions`dry-probes (the **only** verified OpenRouter endpoint;`/v1/models`is never called by the harness — see`deps.execution_preflight()` contract) are all hard preflight checks; the harness refuses to start if any fails. GPG signing state is not stored either — the Phase 3 SSH probe for`commit.gpgsign=true` without a key is also a hard-fail preflight, handled by exit-before-start, not by a session-state flag.)

**Blocked by:** None

**Deliverables:**

- [ ] Dataclasses: `PhaseSpec` (includes `build_file: str`, `phase_number: int`, `phase_id: str`, `layer: Literal["backend","frontend","fullstack","docs","infra","testing","data-migration"]` (derived by the Phase 2 parser — see Phase 2 deliverable: the layer is inferred from the set of declared files via the path-prefix mapping documented in `selector.py` module docstring, or falls back to a Below `/api/classify` call over the phase goal+deliverables when file-path heuristics are inconclusive; the resulting label is frozen onto the `PhaseSpec` and never recomputed downstream), `layer_source: Literal["path_heuristic","below_classifier","fallback_fullstack"]` (companion provenance field recording which branch produced the `layer` value — declared up-front in Phase 1 so Phase 2 writes it, Phase 7 reads it for the layer-covariate-drop guard rule, and Phase 8 reports it in the caveats section; single-writer = Phase 2's selector), `checklist_items: list[ChecklistItem]` where each `ChecklistItem = {item_id: str (stable hash of phase_id+ordinal+text), text: str, extracted_keywords: list[str], declared_files: list[str], item_kind: Literal["standard","unscorable"]}`, `paraphrased_prompt_native: Optional[str] = None` (**resolves R38 B2** — declared here in Phase 1 as part of the frozen `PhaseSpec` schema so no later phase adds fields; single-writer = Phase 2's `selector.set_paraphrase()` method called from Phase 3's `run_cell` under the phase-scoped paraphrase flock; readers are every `run_cell` call for the phase's cells and Phase 6's judge which consumes the paraphrased prompt verbatim. Defaults `None` until the first successful paraphrase+equivalence pass; `selector_cache` serialization handles `Optional` via pydantic's default `None` round-trip.), `paraphrased_prompt_neutral: Optional[str] = None` (same contract as `_native`, holds the sub-study-specific paraphrase for `sub_study="neutral"` — the two sub-study-specific fields are sibling optional strings so the paraphrase gate can short-circuit on whichever sub-study's cell fires first without requiring both to be present)), `RunResult` (includes `replication_index: int`, `node_name: str`, `sub_study: Literal["native","neutral"]`, `token_counts: TokenCounts`, `wall_clock_ms: int`, `exit_code: int`, `no_changes: bool` (**resolves R45 B1** — pre-declared here in Phase 1 so Phase 3's `finalize_run` can set `no_changes=True` when `post_run_commit_sha == pre_run_commit_sha` AND `exit_code == 0` without amending the schema; semantics: `True` means the contestant's runtime produced no commit against the dispatched clone AND exited cleanly — a legitimate "no-op" outcome that scores at zero adherence, NOT an error. Phase 5's scorer reads this field; when `no_changes==True` the diff is empty so per-item adherence checks all resolve to `missed`, `ObjectiveMetrics.test_pass==False`, and `LocalTestResult.combined_status` reflects the unchanged contestant tree. Phase 7's aggregator surfaces `no_changes` as a categorical covariate. Pydantic default `False` so legacy `RunResult` constructions without explicit `no_changes` round-trip correctly.), `runtime_failure_no_commit: bool` (**resolves R49 W6** — pre-declared here in Phase 1 as a sibling discriminator to `no_changes` so Phase 3's `finalize_run` can distinguish a legitimate zero-adherence no-op from a runtime failure that produced no commit. Semantics: `True` means `post_run_commit_sha == pre_run_commit_sha AND exit_code != 0` — the contestant's runtime errored out before committing. Mutually exclusive with `no_changes` by construction; `finalize_run` asserts `not (no_changes and runtime_failure_no_commit)` before returning. Phase 7's aggregator excludes `runtime_failure_no_commit=True` rows from the adherence point estimate (they are not zero-adherence observations — the contestant could not finish) and routes them into a per-model failure-rate covariate instead. Phase 8's report surfaces the failure count alongside the adherence rate in separate panels. Pydantic default `False`.), `exit2_classification_reason: Optional[Literal["post_run_commit_present","stderr_validation_marker_matched","conservative_default_no_commit_no_marker"]] = None` (**resolves R49 W6 audit trail** — pre-declared here in Phase 1 so Phase 3's `_classify_exit2` helper can stamp the reason that drove the exit-2 classification decision. `None` for any run where `exit_code != 2`. Phase 7's regression can optionally model this field as a covariate to test whether conservative-default runs behave differently from explicitly-evidenced runtime-failure runs.), `pre_run_commit_sha: str`, `post_run_commit_sha: str` (pre-declared sibling fields Phase 3's `finalize_run` populates alongside `no_changes` — Phase 1 owns the full schema)), `ObjectiveMetrics` (includes `test_pass: bool`, `local_test_result: LocalTestResult`, `walter_cluster_snapshot: Optional[ClusterSnapshot]`, `lomax_cluster_snapshot: Optional[ClusterSnapshot]`, plus per-metric fields — **all frozen here in Phase 1**); `LocalTestResult` (declared in Phase 1 so no later phase adds variants — the full pydantic model is `{python_status: Literal["pass","fail","timeout","no_tests_discovered","install_failed"], node_status: Literal["pass","fail","timeout","no_tests_discovered","install_failed"], combined_status: Literal["pass","fail","timeout","no_tests_discovered","partial_pass"], python_duration_ms: int, node_duration_ms: int, python_failing_tests: list[str], node_failing_tests: list[str], python_install_log_tail: Optional[str], node_install_log_tail: Optional[str], editable_package_name: Optional[str], editable_install_leaked: bool, venv_version_drift: bool, pytest_forced_reinstall: bool, venv_drift_report: Optional[VenvDriftReport], node_runner_detected: Optional[Literal["vitest","other"]]}` (the `node_runner_detected` field is declared here in Phase 1 to resolve R31 B3 — it records whether Phase 5's Node-test invocation classified the contestant's `scripts.test` as vitest (append `--run`) or other (no positional args), and is `None` when the Node surface was absent. Phase 5 consumes this pre-declared field without amending the schema). **`VenvDriftReport` is also declared here in Phase 1** (alongside `LocalTestResult` in the same `models.py` file) — full pydantic model: `{drift: bool, classes: list[Literal["downgrade","cross_major","same_major_replacement","dependency_removal"]], affected_packages: dict[str, AffectedPackage]}` where `AffectedPackage = {pre: Optional[str], post: Optional[str], class_: Literal["downgrade","cross_major","same_major_replacement","dependency_removal"]}`. Phase 5's venv-drift detector consumes these pre-declared types without adding new schema fields. The `combined_status` Literal explicitly includes `partial_pass` in Phase 1's declaration so Phase 5 consumes that symbol without amending the schema); `ClusterSnapshot = {status: Literal["pass","fail","unknown"], captured_at_utc: str}`; `AdherenceMetrics` (includes `per_item_scores: list[ItemScore]` where each `ItemScore = {item_id, score: Literal["delivered","partial","missed"], matched_keywords: list[str], matched_files: list[str]}` — this is the per-item granularity Phase 8's raw-data export requires, declared up-front in Phase 1), `JudgeVerdict` (includes `secondary_overall_winner: Optional[Literal["A","B","tie"]]`, `secondary_per_dimension: Optional[dict[str, int]]`, `rater_disagreement: bool` — pre-declared for Phase 6's two-judge reduction rule), `CalibrationPair` (**resolves R30 B1 + R31 B2/B5 — the model is declared here in Phase 1's `models.py` as part of the single-owner invariant AND matches Phase 4's ternary validator contract byte-for-byte**; full pydantic model: `{pair_id: str, original_phase_id: str, paraphrase_phase_id: str, true_label: Literal["equivalent","divergent"], below_prediction: Optional[Literal["equivalent","partial","diverged"]], below_confidence: Optional[float], deepseek_prediction: Optional[Literal["equivalent","partial","diverged"]], deepseek_confidence: Optional[float], byron_reviewed_at_utc: str, notes: Optional[str]}`. The prediction Literals are **ternary** (`equivalent` / `partial` / `diverged`) to match exactly the `categories=["equivalent","partial","diverged"]` list Phase 4's equivalence validator sends to Below's `POST /api/classify`; the `true_label` is **binary** (`equivalent` / `divergent`) because Byron's hand-review is a 2-class ground truth (a paraphrase is either semantically-equivalent or it is not — the `partial` intermediate only exists in Below's output space, not in the ground-truth label). The 20 hand-reviewed instances (10 true-equivalent + 10 true-divergent) are written to `.buildrunner/benchmarks/equivalence-calibration.json` by Phase 4 — Phase 1's schema and Phase 4's artifact schema are now the single shared contract.), `BenchmarkConfig`. The `layer` field is the canonical stratification key consumed by Phase 2 (`redraw` stratum), Phase 7 (per-layer regression), and Phase 8 (per-layer breakdown) — nowhere does a later phase infer `layer` from anything other than `PhaseSpec.layer`.
- [ ] **Registry rows are a discriminated union, declared in full in Phase 1**. `registry.py` writes **rows**, not `RegistryEntry` objects. Each row is a JSONL record with a mandatory `row_type: Literal["claim","heartbeat","superseded","completed","dropped","skipped","recognition","probe_pending","judge_claim","judge_superseded","judge_abandoned","judge_decision"]` discriminator plus the subset of fields relevant to that type (resolves R31 B1/B4 + R34 B1: `probe_pending`, `judge_claim`, `judge_superseded`, and `judge_abandoned` are first-class discriminator values declared here in Phase 1, NOT added by a later phase). The union is declared up-front as `RegistryRow = Union[ClaimRow, HeartbeatRow, SupersededRow, CompletedRow, DroppedRow, SkippedRow, RecognitionRow, ProbePendingRow, JudgeClaimRow, JudgeSupersededRow, JudgeAbandonedRow, JudgeDecisionRow]` in `models.py` with every field on every variant named explicitly; the twelve-variant union is the single-owner frozen schema. **`ExclusionRow` is NOT a member of `RegistryRow`** — it is a separate pydantic model that lives in the same `models.py` file (for one-stop import of all benchmark row types) but is written to a **different file** (`.buildrunner/benchmarks/exclusions.jsonl`) with its own append-writer. The two sibling JSONL logs are disjoint by design: `benchmark_registry.jsonl` holds only `RegistryRow` instances, `exclusions.jsonl` holds only `ExclusionRow` instances. Readers of each file discriminate only within their own union. No later phase adds new variants or new fields to either model; any later-phase call site must use one of the pre-declared row types or fail pydantic validation.
  - **Shared run-scoped field (resolves R31 B8 + R39 W3 — registry rows must carry session provenance so pilot-only analyses can filter without inferring, AND recognition probes must be per-session so concurrent sessions don't suppress each other's probe scheduling)**: every run-scoped variant (`ClaimRow`, `HeartbeatRow`, `SupersededRow`, `CompletedRow`, `SkippedRow`, `ProbePendingRow`, `RecognitionRow`) **additionally carries `session_id: str`** (the UUID minted by `br benchmark run` at startup, per the `SessionState.resume_session_id` writer contract). The recognition-probe scheduler's dedup key is `(session_id, phase_id, model)` — not the earlier `(phase_id, model)` alone — so a `RecognitionRow` written by session A never suppresses probe scheduling or analysis joins for session B, and `br benchmark probe` backfill honors the same triple when choosing which `ProbePendingRow` entries to re-attempt. `DroppedRow` remains phase-scoped (not run-scoped) and does NOT carry `session_id` — it is shared across all sessions because phase-drop state is a property of the repo's phase pool, not of any one benchmark session. The `session_id` column lets Phase 9's `pilot_contention.py` filter `CompletedRow`s to the pilot session's rows only (avoiding contamination by any concurrent non-pilot `br benchmark run` invocation that happens to share the registry file). Unit test `test_models.py::test_registry_row_session_id` asserts the seven session-scoped variants (the six run-scoped + `RecognitionRow`) require `session_id` and the one remaining phase-scoped variant (`DroppedRow`) does not carry it.
  - **`ClaimRow`**: `row_type="claim"`, `session_id`, `run_id`, `phase_id`, `model`, `sub_study`, `replication_index`, `node_name`, `worker_id`, `claimed_at_utc`, `lease_expires_at`. **The tuple `(phase_id, model, sub_study, replication_index)` is the `cell_key`** (per-model, used for claim/lease/resume dedup). **The tuple `(phase_id, sub_study, replication_index)` is the `pair_key`** (model-agnostic, used by Phase 6's judge to write one `JudgeVerdict` per matched pair and by Phase 7's Bradley-Terry aggregator to reduce without double-counting). Both are declared as pydantic `NamedTuple` types in `models.py` (`CellKey = NamedTuple("CellKey", [("phase_id", str), ("model", str), ("sub_study", str), ("replication_index", int)])`, `PairKey = NamedTuple("PairKey", [("phase_id", str), ("sub_study", str), ("replication_index", int)])`). `run_id` is an attempt-scoped identifier that a retry re-mints, so dedup must key on `cell_key`, not `run_id`.
  - **`HeartbeatRow`**: `row_type="heartbeat"`, `session_id`, `run_id`, `phase_id`, `model`, `sub_study`, `replication_index`, `worker_id`, `lease_expires_at`, `heartbeat_at_utc`. Carries the full `cell_key` so the claim-dedup reducer can filter by `cell_key` without joining back to the original `ClaimRow`.
  - **`SupersededRow`**: `row_type="superseded"`, `session_id`, `run_id`, `phase_id`, `model`, `sub_study`, `replication_index`, `superseded_worker_id`, `superseded_at_utc`, `reason`. Also carries `cell_key` for the same reason.
  - **`CompletedRow`**: `row_type="completed"`, `session_id`, `run_id`, `phase_id`, `model`, `sub_study`, `replication_index`, `node_name`, `worker_id`, `created_at_utc`, `stage: Literal["run","scored","judged"]`, `pair_key: PairKey` (**resolves R50 B1** — populated on **every** `CompletedRow` variant (`stage="run"`, `stage="scored"`, `stage="judged"`), not just judged rows. The earlier "populated only on judged" spec was unworkable because Phase 6's `judge_pair(pair_key)` must look up both models' `stage="scored"` rows by `pair_key` before the judge runs, and those rows had `pair_key=None` under the earlier schema. `pair_key` is derivable from `(phase_id, sub_study, replication_index)` at append time for every stage — `runner.run_cell` computes it alongside `cell_key` and stamps both on every row regardless of stage. Making the field non-optional and always-populated is strictly additive: judged rows' semantics are unchanged, scored and run rows now carry the same pair identifier so pair-level queries (`is_pair_judged`, `judge_pair`, the three-row commit protocol, Phase 7's aggregator) can filter by `pair_key` without a join. Pydantic validation rejects a missing `pair_key` on any CompletedRow variant), `equivalence_validator: Literal["below","deepseek","both","na"]`, `paraphrase_model`, plus nested `RunResult`, `ObjectiveMetrics: Optional[ObjectiveMetrics]`, `AdherenceMetrics: Optional[AdherenceMetrics]`, `JudgeVerdict: Optional[JudgeVerdict]` (all frozen dataclasses declared in Phase 1). **Progressive-fill contract**: `CompletedRow` is appended **three times per run** as metrics accumulate, and the "last wins" reducer picks the most advanced stage: (1) Phase 3's `runner.run_cell()` appends a `stage="run"` row with `RunResult` populated and `ObjectiveMetrics=AdherenceMetrics=JudgeVerdict=None`; (2) Phase 5's `scorer.score_run()` reads that row, computes `ObjectiveMetrics` + `AdherenceMetrics`, and appends a `stage="scored"` row copying through `RunResult` with the two metric objects filled in (`JudgeVerdict` still `None`); (3) Phase 6's `judge.judge_pair()` reads the scored row, obtains the verdict, and appends a `stage="judged"` row with all four nested fields populated. The reducer compares `stage` via the ordering `judged > scored > run` and picks the highest. This keeps the registry strictly append-only (no mutations) while ensuring every completed run eventually carries its metrics and verdict. Each stage's writer is responsible only for appending its own stage row; no phase mutates another phase's row.
  - **`DroppedRow`**: `row_type="dropped"`, `phase_id`, `reason`, `dropped_at_utc`.
  - **`SkippedRow`**: `row_type="skipped"`, `session_id`, `run_id`, `phase_id`, `reason: Literal["phase_dropped","duplicate_completed","lease_active","dispatch_abandoned","dispatch_terminal_exit2_validation"]`, `skipped_at_utc`.
  - **`RecognitionRow`**: `row_type="recognition"`, `session_id`, `phase_id`, `model`, `recognition_score: float`, `probed_at_utc`.
  - **`ProbePendingRow`**: `row_type="probe_pending"`, `session_id`, `phase_id`, `model`, `attempt_count: int`, `last_error: str`, `last_attempted_at_utc: str`. Emitted by the recognition-probe scheduler (Phase 4) when all in-process retries fail; consumed by the `br benchmark probe` backfill subcommand which re-attempts and then appends a proper `RecognitionRow` on success (resolves R30 W6).
  - **`JudgeClaimRow`** (resolves R34 B1): `row_type="judge_claim"`, `session_id`, `pair_key: PairKey`, `worker_id`, `claimed_at_utc`, `lease_expires_at`. Written by Phase 6's `Runner.run_cell()` through `registry.claim_judge(pair_key, worker_id, session_id)` under `LOCK_EX` to reserve the single judge slot for this `pair_key` before calling `judge_pair()`. The pair-level lock prevents concurrent orchestrators from both producing `JudgeVerdict`s for the same pair. Default `lease_expires_at = claimed_at_utc + config.registry.judge_lease_seconds` (default 900 s).
  - **`JudgeSupersededRow`**: `row_type="judge_superseded"`, `session_id`, `pair_key`, `superseded_worker_id`, `superseded_at_utc`, `reason: Literal["lease_expired","abandoned_by_claimer"]`. Appended when a later orchestrator takes over an expired or abandoned judge claim.
  - **`JudgeAbandonedRow`**: `row_type="judge_abandoned"`, `session_id`, `pair_key`, `worker_id`, `abandoned_at_utc`, `reason: Literal["companion_not_scored","judge_api_error","judge_timeout"]`. Appended when the claimer holds the claim but elects to release it immediately (companion cell not yet scored) or after retry exhaustion (judge_pair() raised after all retries). A subsequent `run_cell()` (same or different orchestrator) may re-attempt the claim; `claim_judge` treats an abandoned-then-lease-expired claim as eligible for takeover (same path as `JudgeSupersededRow` with `reason="abandoned_by_claimer"`).
  - **`JudgeDecisionRow`** (resolves R47 B2 — judge-commit atomicity across two per-model judged rows): `row_type="judge_decision"`, `session_id`, `pair_key: PairKey`, `verdict: JudgeVerdict` (the full pydantic `JudgeVerdict` declared in Phase 1's `models.py` — serialized inline so the decision row carries the verdict verbatim; this is the durable record of the judging outcome), `worker_id`, `decided_at_utc`. **This is a single-JSONL-append commit point for the pair's judged state**: Phase 6's `Runner.run_cell()` protocol writes this row FIRST (single atomic append under `LOCK_EX`), then appends the two `CompletedRow{stage="judged", model="claude"}` + `CompletedRow{stage="judged", model="codex"}` convenience-view rows inside the same `LOCK_EX` acquisition. If a crash strikes between the `JudgeDecisionRow` append and either `CompletedRow{stage="judged"}` append — or between the two CompletedRow appends — the commit point survives on disk and the resume path rebuilds the missing CompletedRow rows from the stored verdict via `registry.recover_missing_judged_rows(session_id)` (declared below in Phase 1's method surface). Redefinition: **`registry.is_pair_judged(pair_key)` returns `True` iff a `JudgeDecisionRow` exists for `pair_key`** (NOT "iff a CompletedRow{stage=judged} exists") — this is the corrected atomicity contract. The two CompletedRow{stage="judged"} rows are now **derived views**, not the source of truth, so a half-written pair is self-healing via `recover_missing_judged_rows`. Declared up-front here in Phase 1 so no later phase adds new row variants; Phase 6's `run_cell` is a pure consumer of the three-append commit protocol.
  - **`ExclusionRow`** (declared in the same `models.py`, written to `.buildrunner/benchmarks/exclusions.jsonl` — a sibling file to the registry, not a row in the registry itself): `{phase_id: str, reason: Literal["paraphrase_failed","equivalence_failed","stratum_violation","pool_exhausted"], attempt_count: int, failed_at_utc: str, session_id: str, extra: dict}`. Phase 2 is the first writer; Phase 4 shares the writer. Schema is fully described here in Phase 1 so both consumers can import from `models.py` at write time.
  - **`PilotContention`** (declared in the same `models.py`, artifact written by Phase 9's `pilot_contention.py` to `.buildrunner/benchmarks/pilot_contention.json` and read by Phase 10's `deps.read_pilot_contention()`): `{drop_lomax: bool, ratio: Optional[float], otis_median_ms: Optional[int], lomax_median_ms: Optional[int], observed_scoring_serial_p95_seconds: Optional[float], p95_sample_size: Optional[int], measured_at_utc: str}` (**resolves R53 B4 — `p95_sample_size` is declared up-front in Phase 1's `PilotContention` model so producer (Phase 9), schema (Phase 1), and consumer (Phase 10) see one JSON shape. `p95_sample_size` is `None` iff `observed_scoring_serial_p95_seconds` is `None` — they are covariant nullable fields. Populated to the count of scored rows used to compute the p95 when the p95 is non-null, per Phase 9's sample-size-aware selector — single-sample degenerate path writes `1`, small-sample fallback path (<20 rows) writes the actual count, canonical path (≥20 rows) writes the actual count. Phase 10's budget revalidation reads the field and applies a small-sample widening factor when `p95_sample_size < 20`.**) — byte-for-byte identical to Phase 9's artifact schema (Invariant 14 + Phase 9 Files list). **`observed_scoring_serial_p95_seconds`** (**resolves R50 B3** — pre-declared here in Phase 1 so Phase 10's venv-lock budget-revalidation logic (see Phase 10 Budget math) can consume the p95 serialized-scoring-time measurement from the pilot without amending the schema. Phase 9's `pilot_contention.py` computes this from the pilot's `CompletedRow` rows by measuring `stage="scored"`-row-write-time minus `stage="run"`-row-write-time across the pilot session's cells and taking the 95th percentile. `None` when the pilot did not run any scored cells (e.g. an early-abort pilot). Phase 10's budget-revision gate compares this field against the 5–6 min budget; a p95 above 8 min triggers a written budget-revision note before Phase 10 starts.). Declared up-front here in Phase 1 so Phase 10's `deps.py` MODIFY is pure consumer code — no schema types are added in Phase 10.
  - Readers that want a per-run record (e.g. the aggregator) reduce the log by `run_id` using the stage-precedence rule defined on `CompletedRow` (`judged > scored > run`): among all `CompletedRow`s for a given `run_id`, the one with the highest-precedence `stage` wins; ties (multiple rows at the same stage from a concurrent writer — should not happen given single-writer-per-stage but handled defensively) are resolved by `created_at_utc` (latest wins). `DroppedRow` and `RecognitionRow` are joined in separately. Reduction contract documented at top of `registry.py`, exercised by a unit test that feeds a `run`+`scored`+`judged` sequence and asserts the reduced record has all four nested fields populated.
- [ ] Registry writer: single-writer mode uses POSIX `open(..., O_APPEND | O_WRONLY)` + `fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX)` for each append — this is the correct append-safe primitive, not `tmp+rename` (which is for full-file replacement). Atomic full-file replacement (`tmp+fsync+rename`) is used only for snapshot exports, never for `benchmark_registry.jsonl` during runs. **Concurrency scope is explicitly single-machine**: all registry writes happen from the orchestrator process (the `br benchmark run` invocation) on Muddy — the machine that owns `.buildrunner/benchmarks/benchmark_registry.jsonl`. Contestants run on Otis / Lomax via `dispatch-to-node.sh`, but **contestants never touch the registry file**; the orchestrator polls dispatch completion and writes the resulting `CompletedRow` locally on Muddy. The only `fcntl.flock` contention is between multiple orchestrator processes on Muddy (e.g. a `br benchmark run` and a concurrent `br benchmark resume`), which `fcntl.flock` handles correctly because both share the same kernel. Cross-machine concurrency is therefore not a concern and NFS / SMB shares are explicitly unsupported for the registry path. Reader is stateless (line-by-line JSONL scan). Writer contract, concurrency scope, and the "contestants never write" invariant are documented at top of `registry.py`.
- [ ] **Claim-before-run dedup keys on the LOGICAL CELL, not `run_id` (resolves the retry-minting-new-run-id dup-claim hole)**. The unit of work the benchmark analyzes is the logical **cell** `cell_key = (phase_id, model, sub_study, replication_index)`; `run_id` is an **attempt**-scoped identifier that a retry re-mints. Every row in `ClaimRow`/`HeartbeatRow`/`SupersededRow`/`CompletedRow`/`SkippedRow` therefore carries both `cell_key` fields (as their own top-level columns) and `run_id`. `registry.claim(cell_key, run_id, worker_id, session_id: str, lease_seconds=1800)` (**resolves R53 B1 — `session_id` is a required positional argument on the claim surface so every row the method appends (`ClaimRow`, `HeartbeatRow`, `SupersededRow`, `CompletedRow`, `SkippedRow`) can populate its required `session_id: str` column without the caller falling back to a global or implicit context. The caller — `Runner.run_cell`, `Runner.dispatch_run`, `runner.resume` — already holds `self.session_id` from the `SessionState` bootstrap and passes it through. Every downstream row writer in `registry.py` (the heartbeat loop, the completion writer, the skipped-row writer) threads this `session_id` into the row's `session_id` field; no row is ever appended with `session_id=None`**) reduces registry rows **filtered by `cell_key`** under the `LOCK_EX` and decides:
  - If any `CompletedRow` for this `cell_key` exists with `stage` in `{"scored","judged"}` (terminal stages per the progressive-fill contract) → claim rejected, caller skips. A `stage="run"` CompletedRow alone is **not** terminal (the run landed but was never scored — treat the cell as incomplete and permit takeover).
  - If the latest (`ClaimRow` or `HeartbeatRow`) for this `cell_key` (any `run_id`) has `lease_expires_at` in the future → active-lease conflict, claim rejected, caller skips. This is the invariant that prevents two orchestrators from launching the same `(phase_id, model, sub_study, replication_index)` concurrently even if they would mint different `run_id`s.
  - If that latest lease has expired → **takeover**: a `SupersededRow` is appended referencing the stale `(cell_key, run_id, worker_id)`, then a fresh `ClaimRow` with the new `run_id` is appended, and the claim succeeds.
  - If no prior active row exists → a `ClaimRow` with this `cell_key`, `run_id`, `worker_id`, `claimed_at_utc`, and `lease_expires_at` is appended.
- [ ] **Attempt → cell reducer (resolves the duplicate-attempts-per-cell ambiguity for Phase 7)**. The aggregator documents and enforces a **two-level reduction**: (1) the existing progressive-fill reducer per `run_id` (`stage: judged > scored > run`, ties by `created_at_utc`) picks the single canonical row per attempt; (2) a second reduction **per `cell_key`** picks one surviving attempt according to: prefer the attempt with the highest `stage` (`judged > scored > run`); tie-break by `created_at_utc` (latest wins among attempts that reached the same terminal stage); **earlier `SupersededRow`-flagged attempts are excluded** (they were explicitly taken over). If two attempts for the same cell both reach `stage="judged"` without supersession (should only happen under a clock-skew race that the lease protocol did not catch), the aggregator keeps the later `created_at_utc` and emits a `duplicate_cell_completion` warning in the report's caveats. Under normal operation — where the `cell_key` claim lock is honored — each cell has exactly one non-superseded completed attempt, so the reducer's tie-breaker is a defensive path, not the common case. The reducer is exercised by a `test_aggregator.py` unit test (**owned and created in Phase 7's Files list, not Phase 1's — resolves R30 W1**: Phase 1's success criteria do not depend on this test passing because `test_aggregator.py` is a Phase-7 artifact; the reference here is forward-pointing so readers know which phase's test suite covers the reducer contract declared in Phase 1's schema. The reducer logic itself lives in `core/benchmark/aggregator.py` (Phase 7's file), and Phase 1 only declares the schema the reducer operates on). That test feeds a synthetic `claim → superseded → claim → judged + dispatch_abandoned` sequence for one cell and asserts exactly one canonical row surfaces.
