- [ ] **Heartbeat + completion rules (same as before, but keyed on `cell_key`)**: a lightweight heartbeat thread in `runner.py` appends a `HeartbeatRow` every 60 seconds that carries both the current attempt's `run_id` and the `cell_key`, bumping `lease_expires_at`. On completion, a `CompletedRow` is appended with both fields. On crash the heartbeat stops; after `lease_seconds` of silence, the `cell_key`-scoped takeover path above runs. Default `lease_seconds = 1800` (30 min), configurable in `config.yaml`.
- [ ] **Judge-claim method surface (resolves R38 B3)**: `registry.py` exposes three explicit pair-level methods owned by Phase 1 alongside `claim`/`drop_phase`/`is_phase_dropped`: (a) **`registry.claim_judge(pair_key: PairKey, worker_id: str, session_id: str, lease_seconds: Optional[int] = None) -> Literal["claimed","rejected_active_lease","rejected_already_judged"]`** (**resolves R53 B2 — `session_id` is a required positional argument threaded from `Runner.run_cell`'s `self.session_id` so every judge-lock row the method appends — `JudgeClaimRow`, `JudgeSupersededRow`, `JudgeAbandonedRow`, `JudgeDecisionRow` — populates its required `session_id: str` field. The companion release/decision methods take the same argument; no judge-lock row is ever appended with `session_id=None`**) — acquires `fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX)` on `benchmark_registry.jsonl`, scans all `JudgeClaimRow`/`JudgeSupersededRow`/`JudgeAbandonedRow`/`JudgeDecisionRow{pair_key==target}` rows filtered by `pair_key` (**resolves R50 B2** — the "already judged" sentinel scanned here is the `JudgeDecisionRow`, the same atomic commit point checked by `is_pair_judged`, NOT the derived `CompletedRow{stage="judged"}` rows; keying both methods on the same sentinel closes the crash-between-appends window where a resuming orchestrator could re-judge a pair whose JudgeDecisionRow was durable but whose convenience CompletedRow{stage="judged"} rows were lost to a crash between appends), applies the same takeover precedence as `claim()` (JudgeDecisionRow present → rejected_already_judged; active non-superseded non-abandoned claim with `lease_expires_at` in future → rejected_active_lease; expired or abandoned claim → append `JudgeSupersededRow` then new `JudgeClaimRow` and return claimed; no prior row → append `JudgeClaimRow` and return claimed). `lease_seconds` defaults to `config.registry.judge_lease_seconds` (declared in Phase 1's `RegistryConfig`, canonical default 900). (b) **`registry.release_judge(pair_key: PairKey, worker_id: str, session_id: str, reason: Literal["companion_not_scored","judge_api_error","judge_timeout"]) -> None`** (**resolves R53 B2 — `session_id` threaded through so the `JudgeAbandonedRow` this method appends has its required `session_id: str` field populated**) — appends a `JudgeAbandonedRow` under the same lock; callers (Phase 6's `run_cell`) use this when the companion cell is not yet scored or after retry exhaustion so a subsequent `claim_judge` can take over. (c) **`registry.is_pair_judged(pair_key: PairKey) -> bool`** (redefined by R47 B2 atomicity fix) — stateless scan returning `True` iff a `JudgeDecisionRow{pair_key==target}` exists in the registry. The CompletedRow{stage="judged"} rows are no longer the commit point — they are derived views that may be missing after a crash-between-appends and are self-healed by `recover_missing_judged_rows`. Callers that want to check "is this pair fully committed as judged?" use `is_pair_judged`; callers that want "are both per-model convenience rows present?" compose `is_pair_judged` with a stateless scan for both CompletedRow{stage="judged", model=X} rows. (d) **`registry.recover_missing_judged_rows(session_id: str) -> int`** (resolves R47 B2 — single-writer recovery path; returns count of CompletedRow{stage="judged"} rows appended as recovery). Acquires `LOCK_EX`. Scans `JudgeDecisionRow` entries with matching `session_id`; for each one, counts the existing `CompletedRow{stage="judged", pair_key==decision.pair_key}` rows grouped by `model`. For each `model` in `session_state.get_flag(session_id, "selected_models")` missing a matching CompletedRow{stage="judged"} row, reconstructs the row from the stored `JudgeDecisionRow.verdict` + the most recent `CompletedRow{stage="scored", pair_key, model}` (for `RunResult` + `ObjectiveMetrics` + `AdherenceMetrics` passthrough) and appends the missing row. Releases the lock. Called exactly once by `runner.resume(session_id)` before the cell-key reducer runs, so the registry is internally consistent before resume-dispatch decisions are made. If `recover_missing_judged_rows` finds a `JudgeDecisionRow` whose matching `CompletedRow{stage="scored"}` rows are themselves missing (pathological — judge decided before scoring, impossible under the normal protocol), the helper emits a `registry_inconsistency` warning and the runner exits with a remediation message; this is a hard-fail preflight check on resume, not a silent recovery. Fully covered by `tests/benchmark/test_registry.py`: `test_recover_appends_missing_judged_rows` seeds a `JudgeDecisionRow` + one `CompletedRow{stage="judged", model="claude"}` (codex missing) + both `CompletedRow{stage="scored"}` rows, invokes `recover_missing_judged_rows`, and asserts one new `CompletedRow{stage="judged", model="codex"}` is appended with verdict payload matching the decision row; `test_recover_no_op_when_both_rows_present` seeds a complete pair and asserts the helper returns 0 and appends nothing; `test_recover_hard_fails_when_scored_missing` asserts the pathological case raises `RegistryInconsistencyError`. All three methods live in `core/benchmark/registry.py` (Phase 1's file), share the same JSONL writer + LOCK_EX path already owned by `claim()`, and are fully covered by `tests/benchmark/test_registry.py` (Phase 1's test file) with scenarios for claim+release+reclaim, expired-lease takeover, and double-judged rejection. **Phase 6's judging flow depends on this pre-declared surface** — Phase 6 adds no new registry methods, it only consumes `claim_judge` / `release_judge` / `is_pair_judged` + the existing `append(CompletedRow(stage="judged", ...))` path. This resolves R38 B3: the registry API the judge uses is wholly declared in Phase 1 alongside the twelve-variant row union, preserving the single-owner invariant.
- [ ] **Scan helpers for probe + resume paths (resolves R44 B2, extended for R49 W4)**: `registry.py` additionally exposes three stateless-scan helpers owned by Phase 1 alongside the claim methods above: (a) **`registry.scan_pending_probes(session_id: Optional[str] = None, all_sessions: bool = False) -> list[ProbePendingRow]`** — returns all `ProbePendingRow` entries that do NOT have a matching `RecognitionRow` at the `(session_id, phase_id, model)` dedup key declared by Phase 4 (R42 B2). When `session_id` is passed (default), the scan is scoped to that session id; when `all_sessions=True`, the scan covers every session present in the registry. Stateless single-pass JSONL read under `fcntl.flock(LOCK_SH)`; matches Phase 6's `br benchmark probe` backfill and `ProbeScheduler.run_pending()` consumers. (b) **`registry.scan_for_judged_rows(session_id: str) -> list[CompletedRow]`** — returns every `CompletedRow{stage="judged", session_id==target}` entry grouped by the caller (Phase 6's `_resume_scheduler_counters_from_registry` iterates the returned list and rebuilds the `ProbeScheduler` `completed` counters per `(phase_id, model)` in two-model sessions). Stateless single-pass JSONL read under `LOCK_SH`; no mutation. (c) **`registry.scan_for_scored_rows(session_id: str) -> list[CompletedRow]`** (resolves R49 W4 — single-model resume terminal-stage mismatch) — returns every `CompletedRow{stage="scored", session_id==target}` entry. Used exclusively by Phase 6's `_resume_scheduler_counters_from_registry` when `len(session_state.get_flag(session_id, "selected_models")) < 2` (single-model sessions), because in that mode `scored` is the session's terminal stage (no judging runs) and rebuilding the scheduler from `scan_for_judged_rows` would return an empty list and silently reset the `completed` counters to zero on resume — causing the scheduler to re-fire recognition probes for phases that already completed pre-kill. In two-model sessions this helper is NOT called (the judged helper is used instead) because cells reach both `stage="scored"` and `stage="judged"` and counting scored rows would double-count against the judged counter. Stateless single-pass JSONL read under `LOCK_SH`; no mutation. All three helpers are fully covered by `tests/benchmark/test_registry.py` (Phase 1's test file) — `test_scan_pending_probes_filters_fulfilled` seeds 3 `ProbePendingRow`s and 1 matching `RecognitionRow` and asserts only the 2 unfulfilled rows return; `test_scan_pending_probes_scopes_by_session_id` seeds rows from 2 sessions and asserts `session_id=S1` returns only S1 rows; `test_scan_for_judged_rows_filters_by_session_id_and_stage` seeds mixed-stage rows and asserts only `stage="judged"` rows for the target session return; `test_scan_for_scored_rows_filters_by_session_id_and_stage` seeds mixed-stage rows (some scored-only from a single-model session, some scored+judged from a two-model session) and asserts the helper returns only `stage="scored"` rows for the target session. **Phase 6's probe scheduler + resume path depend on this pre-declared surface** — Phase 6 adds no new registry methods, it only consumes `scan_pending_probes` / `scan_for_judged_rows` / `scan_for_scored_rows`. This closes the R44 B2 + R49 W4 ownership gap: all three helpers are declared in Phase 1 alongside `claim_judge`/`release_judge`/`is_pair_judged`.
- [ ] **Phase-drop tombstoning**: when paraphrase or equivalence fails for a phase, `registry.drop_phase(phase_id, reason)` appends a `DroppedRow` under the same lock. Any subsequent read of the registry for that phase's rows is filtered through `is_phase_dropped(phase_id)` which returns `True` if a `DroppedRow` exists for it. Aggregator (Phase 7) and reporter (Phase 8) both apply this filter; partially-written rows for a dropped phase are ignored in analysis but preserved on disk for post-hoc audit.
- [ ] **`core/benchmark/cli.py` module entrypoint (ensures `python -m core.benchmark.cli --help` exits 0)**: the file ends with the standard Typer entrypoint idiom — `if __name__ == "__main__": app()` — so `python -m core.benchmark.cli ...` resolves, imports the module as `__main__`, and dispatches into the Typer app. This is what makes the success-criterion invocation `python -m core.benchmark.cli --help` actually execute the CLI (not just instantiate the app object). A **`core/benchmark/__main__.py`** sibling is also created as a thin one-liner (`from .cli import app; app()`) so `python -m core.benchmark --help` works as a convenience alias. Both paths are exercised by a unit test in `tests/benchmark/test_cli_skeleton.py` asserting each returns exit 0 and produces the full subcommand list.
- [ ] Typer CLI skeleton registers all subcommands that will ship: `run`, `select`, `score`, `judge`, `paraphrase`, `probe`, `validate`, `report`, `resume`, `status`, `gc-anchors` (post-Phase-10 maintenance that lists / deletes `refs/heads/bench/<run_id>` anchors older than a `--keep-days` threshold — implementation lands in Phase 3's `runner.py` alongside `finalize_run()`), `record-contracts` (Phase 2-owned operator command that records Walter / Lomax / Below fixtures to `tests/benchmark/fixtures/*.yaml` via vcrpy against the live cluster; runs once during the Phase 2 discovery spike and again whenever a cluster node's API changes — implementation lands in Phase 2's `api_clients.py`). Each subcommand has a `--help` stub in Phase 1; only the stub is required to ship here.
- [ ] **Preflight is split into three tiers, each gated at the subcommand body, NOT at `cli.py` import time** (resolves R34 W1 — `br benchmark score --run-id <id>` is an offline re-score path that works from `refs/heads/bench/<run_id>` without OpenRouter or dispatch access, so gating it behind `execution_preflight` would incorrectly fail the exact scenario it is designed for). `core/benchmark/cli.py` only constructs the Typer `app` object and registers subcommand modules at import time — no network calls, no file-system assertions. (i) **`deps.execution_preflight()`** — the full hard check-set (OpenRouter verified POST-probes + model-ID verification, `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` presence, `dispatch-to-node.sh` path, `cluster-check.sh` path, dispatcher-internals grep, remote-node GPG probe). Called from the first line of subcommands that actually run contestants by dispatching them to the local cluster via `dispatch-to-node.sh`: `run`, `resume` — **NOT** `score` (offline re-score path), **NOT** `judge` / `probe` / `paraphrase` (pure-OpenRouter offline backfill paths — see `offline_preflight()` below; resolves R48 W8 — `br benchmark judge` and `br benchmark probe` are explicitly designed as offline backfill commands that operate on completed `benchmark_registry.jsonl` state via OpenRouter LLM calls and do not need the local dispatch infrastructure; routing them through `execution_preflight()` would hard-fail those commands in exactly the environments — e.g. a cluster-offline post-run judging pass or a stand-alone Below-offline probe backfill — where the plan mandates they still work). (ii) **`deps.scoring_preflight()`** — a local-and-optional-cluster check-set (asserts `.buildrunner/benchmarks/config.yaml` parses, asserts `.venv-benchmark/bin/python` exists, asserts the target clone exists under `refs/heads/bench/<run_id>`, soft-probes Walter + Lomax reachability for enrichment, **does NOT require OpenRouter or `dispatch-to-node.sh`**). Called from `score` — this is the tier that matches Phase 5's offline re-score contract: scoring executes pytest/vitest locally against a re-materialized clone and requires only venv + registry access, not remote dispatch or LLM calls. **`br benchmark score --run-id <id>` session_id resolution (resolves R49 B2 Codex offline-score session-state contract)**: the offline re-score path does NOT mint a new session and does NOT require an active session-state file at invocation time. `cli_score.py` resolves the target `session_id` by scanning `benchmark_registry.jsonl` under `LOCK_SH` for any row whose `run_id == <id>`; that row's `session_id` field is the authoritative session binding (every run-scoped registry row carries `session_id` per Phase 1's shared-field contract). The resolved `session_id` is used only for (a) loading the per-session file at `.buildrunner/benchmarks/sessions/<session_id>.json` **read-only** via `session_state.get_flag(session_id, ...)` to look up `preflight_walter_unreachable` / `preflight_lomax_unreachable` / `preflight_below_unreachable` so the offline rescore applies the same enrichment gates as the original session, (b) stamping the new `CompletedRow{stage="scored"}` with the correct `session_id` so the progressive-fill reducer joins it to the original session's cell history. `scoring_preflight()` therefore **does not write** any session-state flags — it only reads the existing per-session file if one exists and soft-degrades silently (logs a warning but does not fail) if the per-session file is missing (e.g. the session was gc'd after its per-session file hit the 30-day `--prune-sessions` threshold); in that missing-file case scoring proceeds with `walter_cluster_snapshot=None` / `lomax_cluster_snapshot=None` and the report's caveats section flags the re-scored runs as `rescored_without_session_state=True`. If the registry scan finds no row with matching `run_id`, `cli_score.py` hard-fails with a remediation message directing the operator to `br benchmark status` for the registry-visible run_id list. This preserves the Phase 1 per-session-file contract (no global-session read path) while making the offline re-score path work without requiring an active session at invocation time. Unit test `test_cli_score.py::test_score_resolves_session_id_from_registry` seeds a synthetic registry with one `CompletedRow{stage="run", run_id="R1", session_id="S1"}`, invokes `br benchmark score --run-id R1`, and asserts the new `stage="scored"` row carries `session_id="S1"` and that `session_state.get_flag("S1", "preflight_walter_unreachable")` was called read-only. Unit test `test_cli_score.py::test_score_soft_degrades_on_missing_session_file` deletes the per-session file before invoking score and asserts the command exits 0 with `walter_cluster_snapshot=None` and a stderr warning naming the missing session file. Walter/Lomax reachability is soft: unreachable writes the same session-state flags as `execution_preflight` so scoring can still proceed with `walter_cluster_snapshot = None` / `lomax_cluster_snapshot = None`. (iii) **`deps.analysis_preflight()`** — a file-system-only check-set (asserts `.buildrunner/benchmarks/config.yaml` exists and parses, asserts `benchmark_registry.jsonl` exists, asserts `hypotheses.md` and `decision-rule.md` exist). Called from `validate`, `report`, and `status` — offline analysis paths that must work when OpenRouter / the cluster are down because their input is disk-only. (iv) **`deps.offline_preflight()`** (resolves R48 W8) — a pure-OpenRouter check-set for commands that issue LLM calls against registry data without dispatching contestants or running local test suites. Asserts `.buildrunner/benchmarks/config.yaml` parses, asserts `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` is set AND verified via the same five role-specific 1-token `POST /api/v1/chat/completions` dry-probes as `execution_preflight()`, asserts `.buildrunner/benchmarks/benchmark_registry.jsonl` exists and is readable under `fcntl.flock(LOCK_SH)`. **Does NOT require `dispatch-to-node.sh`, `cluster-check.sh`, the dispatcher-internals grep, the remote-node GPG probe, Walter/Lomax reachability, or `.venv-benchmark/bin/python` existence** — pure-OpenRouter offline backfill has no local-dispatch, local-test-runner, or cluster-enrichment dependency. Soft-probes Below reachability (same contract as `execution_preflight`) because `paraphrase` and `probe` may consult Below for equivalence classification and layer heuristics respectively; a Below-unreachable state writes `preflight_below_unreachable=true` and degrades (DeepSeek fallback for equivalence, path-heuristic-only layer mapping in the probe path's contamination covariate). Called from `paraphrase`, `probe`, and `judge` — the three pure-OpenRouter subcommands that operate on registry state and do not dispatch contestants. This tier is deliberately narrower than `execution_preflight()` (no dispatch, no cluster-check, no venv) AND narrower than `scoring_preflight()` (no venv, no registered-clone check) — matching exactly the offline backfill design documented in Phase 4's recognition-probe retry path and Phase 6's `br benchmark judge` backfill contract. Unit test `test_deps.py::test_offline_preflight_requires_no_dispatch` constructs a test environment where `dispatch-to-node.sh` and `cluster-check.sh` are intentionally removed from `PATH`, monkeypatches `requests.post` to return the OpenRouter probe 200s and Below classify 200, invokes `offline_preflight()`, and asserts it returns without raising (whereas the same environment would hard-fail `execution_preflight()`). (v) **`deps.select_preflight()`** — a minimal check-set for `br benchmark select`. Asserts `.buildrunner/benchmarks/config.yaml` parses (needed for training-cutoff values loaded via `training_cutoffs.get_cutoffs()`) AND probes Below `/api/classify` reachability with a 2-second timeout. **`below_reachable` is returned as a boolean to the calling subcommand and passed directly into the selector constructor as a local parameter — it is NOT written to session-state (resolves R38 W2)**. `br benchmark select` is a standalone pre-run command that may execute before any `br benchmark run` has minted a `session_id`, so reading the per-session `preflight_below_unreachable` flag would consult undefined/stale state; instead the selector accepts an explicit `below_available: bool` constructor argument that `cli_select.py` populates from the fresh `select_preflight()` probe. The `run`/`resume` subcommands continue to populate `preflight_below_unreachable` on the per-session file via `execution_preflight()` for their own selector use, and Phase 2's selector routes the decision through a single helper `_is_below_available(session_state, constructor_override)` that prefers `constructor_override` when provided (the `select` path) and falls back to `session_state.preflight_below_unreachable` otherwise (the `run`/`resume` path). **If Below is reachable**, layer assignment uses the full path-heuristic + Below-classifier pipeline. **If Below is unreachable**, the selector runs in a **degraded mode** where ambiguous phases fall back to `fallback_fullstack` immediately (path-heuristic hits are unaffected) and a warning is printed to stderr naming the share of phases that would have been classified by Below. This matches the `layer_source` provenance pipeline already documented in Phase 2 — the degraded-mode fallback writes `layer_source="fallback_fullstack"` just as it would for any other Below-unreachable path, so the 20%-threshold guard in Phase 7 correctly drops the `layer` covariate when too many phases defaulted to `fullstack`. `br benchmark select` is **not** network-free in the general case (layer assignment can call Below for ambiguous phases), so a preflight tier is required; the tier is minimal because `select` still runs to completion against pure disk when Below is down (just with degraded provenance). Unit test `test_selector.py::test_select_uses_constructor_override_not_session_state` constructs a selector with `below_available=False` and **no** session-state file on disk (simulating pre-session `br benchmark select`) and asserts the selector routes ambiguous phases through the `fallback_fullstack` path without raising `FileNotFoundError` on the missing session file. **No preflight at all** for `--help` and for `gc-anchors` / `record-contracts` (operator maintenance; they do their own lightweight checks inline — `record-contracts` in particular probes each service's reachability before recording, which is its whole purpose). This guarantees `python -m core.benchmark.cli --help` and `br benchmark --help` succeed in any environment, including CI without OpenRouter credentials or cluster access, **and** guarantees the analysis/report steps run offline after the study completes.
- [ ] `deps.py` asserts (hard, fail-fast on missing, **called from work-subcommand bodies only per the gating rule above**): `dispatch-to-node.sh` exists and is executable; `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` is set **AND** OpenRouter reachability is verified via the **verified** endpoint `POST https://openrouter.ai/api/v1/chat/completions` (the only OpenRouter endpoint whose contract is documented in the BR3 dependency matrix — **resolves R32 B2**: prior drafts probed `GET /api/v1/models`, an endpoint the dependency matrix does not cover, so the preflight would rely on an unverified response shape; the verified `POST /chat/completions` endpoint is used exclusively now). `~/.buildrunner/scripts/cluster-check.sh` exists and is executable. **Model-ID preflight via verified endpoint (resolves R20 B13 / R16 C1's "unverified model identifiers" concern AND R32 B2)**: for each required model ID, `deps.py` issues a **1-token dry-probe** `POST /api/v1/chat/completions` with body `{"model": <id>, "messages": [{"role":"user","content":"ping"}], "max_tokens": 1}` and a 10 s timeout per probe. A 200 response (even with truncated output) confirms the model ID is live. A 400/404 with OpenRouter's structured error body containing `"error.code" == "model_not_found"` or `"error.message"` matching `/not a valid model/i` surfaces the **role-specific remediation message** below. Probes run sequentially (five at most: paraphraser_primary/secondary, judge_primary/secondary, equivalence_fallback — deduplicated — so ≤5 × 10 s = 50 s preflight budget worst-case). A 429 (rate limit) is retried once with 2 s backoff; persistent 429 is treated as "OpenRouter unreachable" (hard-fail). The total token cost across the five probes is ≤5 tokens — negligible and verified to not affect billing in meaningful ways. **The `/api/v1/models` endpoint is never called by the harness.** The required IDs are **computed at preflight time from the five role-specific fields** in `.buildrunner/benchmarks/config.yaml:openrouter.*` (the single canonical config file created in Phase 1's Files list above; `core/benchmark/config.py` exposes a `load_config()` helper that reads this file — there is no `core/benchmark/config.yaml`) via `required = dedup([c.openrouter.paraphraser_primary, c.openrouter.paraphraser_secondary, c.openrouter.judge_primary, c.openrouter.judge_secondary, c.openrouter.equivalence_fallback])` — **there is no `required_models` list in config.yaml; the role-specific fields are the single source of truth.** Frozen for the current study as **`paraphraser_primary = meta-llama/llama-3.1-405b-instruct`** (Phase 4), **`paraphraser_secondary = mistralai/mixtral-8x22b-instruct`** (Phase 4), **`judge_primary = openai/gpt-5`** (Phase 6), **`judge_secondary = google/gemini-2.5-pro`** (Phase 6), and **`equivalence_fallback = deepseek/deepseek-chat`** (Phase 4). These are the **canonical OpenRouter slugs** — any rename, deprecation, or typo surfaces at preflight with a **role-specific** remediation message: `"OpenRouter model <slug> not found for role <role_field_name> (probe returned <status> with error.code=<error.code>). Update .buildrunner/benchmarks/config.yaml:openrouter.<role_field_name> or request provisioning from OpenRouter support."` — the role name is named explicitly so the operator knows which role has the wrong id. Because the probe uses the verified `/chat/completions` endpoint rather than the unverified `/models` listing, fuzzy-match suggestions are **not** included in the remediation message (no authoritative local model list to match against); the operator instead consults OpenRouter's documentation page. **Every phase that references a specific model ID (Phase 4 for paraphraser + equivalence, Phase 6 for judges) reads that ID from its role-specific field** (`config.openrouter.paraphraser_primary`, `config.openrouter.judge_primary`, etc.) via `core/benchmark/config.py:load_config()` rather than hardcoding it in Python or iterating a flat list — so role-to-model mapping is typed and neither the preflight check nor the consumer code can drift. **Walter and Lomax reachability is NOT hard-fail** — they are consumed only as optional enrichment by Phase 5 (see Phase 5 deliverables: "does not enter the decision rule", `is_verified()` gates every read), so hard-failing on their reachability would contradict that contract and block benchmark runs that Phase 5 says are valid.
- [ ] `deps.py` asserts (soft, warn-and-degrade on failure) **using verified endpoints only** (resolves R32 W1 + R39 W1 — Walter/Lomax `/health` and `/api/health` ARE verified endpoints per the dependency matrix at lines 71-72 of this plan, while Below has no verified `/health` endpoint. Preflight reachability checks exercise the verified endpoints per-service): (a) **Walter reachability** — issue `GET http://10.0.1.102:8100/health` (verified) with a 5 s timeout; a 200 response confirms Walter is reachable. On non-200 / timeout, preflight writes `preflight_walter_unreachable = true` into session state and Phase 5 short-circuits Walter enrichment to `walter_cluster_snapshot = None`; (b) **Lomax reachability** — issue `GET http://10.0.1.104:8100/health` (verified per dep table) with a 5 s timeout; same degrade-on-failure contract writes `preflight_lomax_unreachable = true` and `lomax_cluster_snapshot = None`; (c) **Below reachability** — Below has no verified `/health` endpoint, so the preflight issues a minimal `POST http://10.0.1.105:8100/api/classify` dry-probe (the canonical verified Below endpoint per the BR3 dependency matrix — **resolves R36 B2**: prior drafts referenced the unverified `https://below.local:<port>` hostname + HTTPS/port combination that is nowhere established in the dependency matrix; the harness now exclusively uses the verified `http://10.0.1.105:8100/api/classify` URL that matches Below's actual service contract on the cluster IP `10.0.1.105` port `8100` over HTTP) with body `{"text": "ping", "categories": ["a","b"]}` and a 5 s timeout. A 200 response (even with arbitrary classification output) confirms Below is reachable and functioning; any non-200 / timeout / connection-refused result writes `preflight_below_unreachable = true`, the DeepSeek equivalence fallback is forced on, and startup continues. The classify-probe uses the **same endpoint production code uses** so "reachable" and "usable for classification" are the same check — no `/health` endpoint is assumed to exist or to reflect real service health. Because OpenRouter is hard-fail at preflight (see above), the DeepSeek path is always available when Below is down — there is no "both unreachable" case to handle here. **Phase 2's degraded selector logic also consults `preflight_below_unreachable`** and routes phase-layer classification through the path-heuristic + `fallback_fullstack` default when Below is unreachable — no secondary `/health` probe is issued from the selector; the single session-state flag is the source of truth.
- [ ] `deps.py` exposes a standalone `probe_node_pool()` function (distinct from `NodeAllocator`) that runs `~/.buildrunner/scripts/cluster-check.sh otis` and `...lomax` and returns the list of online nodes. Phase 3's `NodeAllocator` consumes this list — Phase 1 does not depend on any Phase 3 symbol. If only one node is online, the pool collapses to that node; `preflight_single_node = true` is recorded in session state, and Phase 7's mixed-effects regression drops the `node_name` covariate for that run (see Phase 7 deliverable).
- [ ] `cli/main.py` edit: `app.add_typer(benchmark_app, name="benchmark")` added alongside existing `add_typer` calls.
- [ ] No changes to the global `~/.buildrunner/scripts/dispatch-to-node.sh` — Phase 3's `dispatch_run` passes the prompt directly as the verified positional argv argument via `subprocess.Popen(..., shell=False)`, staying within the ~1 MiB argv limit on macOS (benchmark prompts are expected <50 KB; **hard-rejected at 100 KB — the single canonical threshold**, matching the remote-path size budget in Phase 3's `dispatch_run` argv contract). The harness is fully reproducible from the repo alone.
- [ ] Token-count capture schema: `TokenCounts { input: int, output: int, cached: int, source: Literal["stdout_json","stderr_usage_line","none"] }` — parsing rules documented for both Codex and Claude dispatches.
- [ ] `requirements-benchmark.txt` created in Phase 1 with the full pin list (see Phase 5 file list for the canonical contents) — this gives Phase 2 access to `pydantic`, `responses`, and `vcrpy` before any later phase consumes them. Phase 5's installer re-uses this same file plus adds the `npm` toolchain install.
- [ ] `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh` creates `.venv-benchmark/` and installs **all root-level `requirements*.txt` files** the project ships (verified as of 2026-04-16: `requirements-api.txt` is the sole root requirements file — `requirements.txt` does not exist at the repo root; the Phase 1 installer itself creates `requirements-benchmark.txt`, so immediately after Phase 1 lands the glob matches both files). **Pin-priority order is enforced via a two-pass install**, not a single glob loop — Pass 1 skips `requirements-benchmark.txt` and installs every other `requirements*.txt`; Pass 2 installs `requirements-benchmark.txt` last. The script starts with `#!/usr/bin/env bash` and `set -euo pipefail`. Pass 1 body: `shopt -s nullglob; for req in requirements*.txt; do [ "$req" = "requirements-benchmark.txt" ] && continue; .venv-benchmark/bin/pip install -r "$req"; done; shopt -u nullglob`. Pass 2 body: `if [ -f requirements-benchmark.txt ]; then .venv-benchmark/bin/pip install -r requirements-benchmark.txt; fi`. **Immediately after Pass 2 completes**, the script writes the canonical session baseline: `.venv-benchmark/bin/pip freeze > .venv-benchmark/.br3-baseline-freeze.txt` (atomic via `>` redirect into an unused file in an already-flocked path). This file is the deterministic pre-run reference point consumed by Phase 5's pre-run guard (`runner._detect_baseline_drift`) — it is never touched after Pass 2 until the next full re-install. This matches the stated auto-discovery intent — any future `requirements-<name>.txt` added at the repo root is picked up automatically on the next installer run — while guaranteeing the harness's pins win (pip's resolver favors the last-installed pin set on conflict). The two-pass order is also the canonical path for Phase 5's "reinstall after `editable_install_leaked=true`" recovery, so the recovery path never drifts from what a fresh install does. Idempotent: re-runs skip the venv-creation step if `.venv-benchmark/bin/python` already exists; both passes always re-run to pick up drift. Developers run this once after cloning; CI runs it in the benchmark workflow.
- [ ] `python -m core.benchmark.cli --help` returns exit 0 and lists every subcommand.
- [ ] Unit test: dataclasses serialize round-trip to JSON; registry write + read + skip works.

**Success Criteria:** `br benchmark --help` lists all 12 subcommands (`run`, `select`, `score`, `judge`, `paraphrase`, `probe`, `validate`, `report`, `resume`, `status`, `gc-anchors`, `record-contracts`) and exits 0 **without** invoking any preflight tier (the `--help` path imports `cli.py`, which only constructs the Typer app; all three preflight tiers are gated at subcommand-body entry, not at import). Additionally, `python -m core.benchmark.cli --help` and `python -m core.benchmark --help` both exit 0 with the same subcommand list (via the `__main__` entrypoints declared above). **Preflight-tier invocability check (Phase 1-appropriate scope — resolves R41 B1 — the prior "`br benchmark run --phases 0 --replications 0 --no-pilot` is the canonical smoke path" language depended on Phase 3's `cli_run.py` body AND a `test_phase1_smoke.py` file that was not listed in Phase 1's Files section, so it blocked Phase 1 acceptance on Phase 3 artifacts)**: the Phase 1-scoped verification is simply that each preflight-tier function is importable from `core.benchmark.deps` and is callable from a mocked subcommand stub. A unit test `tests/benchmark/test_deps.py::test_preflight_tiers_importable_and_callable` (file listed in Phase 1's Files section below — see `tests/benchmark/test_deps.py` entry) imports `execution_preflight`, `scoring_preflight`, `analysis_preflight`, `offline_preflight`, `select_preflight` from `core.benchmark.deps`; mocks out the underlying subprocess / HTTP calls (pytest `monkeypatch` on `subprocess.run`, `requests.get/post`); invokes each tier in turn; asserts each returns without raising and writes the expected session-state flags. The live-cluster full preflight against a real `br benchmark run --phases 0 ...` invocation is Phase 3's success criterion — not Phase 1's — because Phase 3 owns the `cli_run.py` body. The `--help` success criterion and the importable-preflight-tiers success criterion are the two Phase 1-scoped acceptance checks.

### Phase 2: Phase Selector + Contamination Stratification + API Contracts

**Goal:** `br benchmark select --count 30` returns a stratified candidate list. Walter + Lomax HTTP contracts documented and typed.

**Files:**

- `core/benchmark/selector.py` (NEW)
- `core/benchmark/training_cutoffs.py` (NEW)
- `core/benchmark/lockres.py` (NEW — shared lock-resolution helper, consumed by both selector and Phase 3's runner)
- `core/benchmark/api_clients.py` (NEW — typed Walter + Lomax + Below clients with pydantic response models. **Declared module-level functions (resolves R44 B3 — the `record_contracts` call site is backed by a real declaration)**: (a) `class WalterClient`, `class LomaxClient`, `class BelowClient` — per-service typed clients with pydantic request/response models for each endpoint documented in `api_contracts.md`. (b) **`record_contracts(config: BenchmarkConfig) -> ApiStatus`** — a module-level function that probes each client once against its live service, records the interaction as a vcrpy cassette at `tests/benchmark/fixtures/{walter,lomax,below}-contract.yaml`, computes the per-service `{verified: bool, reason: Optional[str], recorded_at_utc: str}` status by catching transport errors / non-2xx responses on each probe, assembles the three statuses into an `ApiStatus` pydantic model (declared alongside the clients in this file), and atomic-writes the model as JSON to `.buildrunner/benchmarks/api-status.json` via `tmp+fsync+rename`. `record_contracts` is the sole writer of both the three cassette files and `api-status.json`; it is called exclusively by `cli_record_contracts.py`'s command body. `ApiStatus.verified=False` on a service means that service's enrichment is disabled in Phase 5's scorer (per-client gate). Unit test `test_api_clients.py::test_record_contracts_writes_three_cassettes_and_status_json` monkeypatches the three `requests.*` calls, invokes `record_contracts(config)`, and asserts the three cassette files and the `api-status.json` artifact exist with the expected verified/reason fields.)
- `core/benchmark/api_contracts.md` (NEW — documents every endpoint consumed: URL, method, request schema, response schema, auth, retry policy)
- `core/benchmark/cli_select.py` (MODIFY — replace Phase 1 stub with the `select` command body that calls `selector.select(...)`. **Standalone session bootstrap (resolves R45 B2)**: `br benchmark select` is a standalone preview command — it does not run a benchmark session, it just prints candidate phases — but the selector/session-state contract is session-scoped (`selected_phase_ids`, `selector_cache`, `redraw_map`, exclusions filtering all key on `session_id`). To reconcile, the command body enforces this session-bootstrap rule: (1) `br benchmark select` mints a **fresh ephemeral `session_id = uuid4()`** at startup using the same `uuid4()` call as `br benchmark run` (not a shared session, not a reused session); (2) a new session-state row is written with `is_preview: bool = True` (pre-declared in Phase 1's frozen `SessionState` schema alongside `display_label` — **single-writer = this Phase 2 `cli_select.py` preview-bootstrap path ONLY, matching Phase 1's R47 W1 writer-attribution resolution** (resolves R48 W9 — earlier draft text here mistakenly attributed the writer to Phase 1's `deps.py`, contradicting the Phase 1 schema entry that names this cli*select.py path as the sole writer; the two attributions are now reconciled: Phase 1's `deps.py` owns only the `preflight*\*\_unreachable`fields, not`is_preview`/`preview_created_at_utc`); defaults `False`for`run`/`resume`-created sessions); (3) the selector runs against this ephemeral session, populating its `selector_cache`/`selected_phase_ids`under the ephemeral`session_id`; (4) **the command writes `session_state.preview_created_at_utc = now()`** and exits without running a benchmark. **Preview artifacts directory owner (resolves R53 W1)**: `cli_select.py`is the sole writer/owner of`.buildrunner/benchmarks/previews/<session_id>/` — a per-session directory that holds the preview's printable stratum-balance report (`.buildrunner/benchmarks/previews/<session_id>/stratum_balance.txt`) and a JSON dump of the selector's candidate phase list (`.buildrunner/benchmarks/previews/<session_id>/candidates.json`). The directory is created idempotently via `Path(".buildrunner/benchmarks/previews/<session_id>").mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)`at the top of the select command body, written to atomically via`tmp+fsync+rename`, and read by operators post-hoc for audit (the command's stdout is the primary user-facing surface; the on-disk artifacts are the durable copy). The `previews/`parent directory is created idempotently alongside`.buildrunner/benchmarks/sessions/`and`.buildrunner/benchmarks/prompts/`by Phase 1's`deps.py`startup (alongside the other`.buildrunner/benchmarks/`subdirectories). The per-session subdirectory is swept by Phase 3's`gc-anchors`class (f) (48-hour preview retention) alongside the session-state JSON file; teardown happens in the same sweep pass to avoid leaked subdirectories when the JSON is removed but the directory persists. Unit test`test_cli_select.py::test_select_writes_preview_artifacts`asserts that after invoking the command,`.buildrunner/benchmarks/previews/<session_id>/stratum_balance.txt`and`.buildrunner/benchmarks/previews/<session_id>/candidates.json`both exist and contain the expected payload shape.`br benchmark run`and`br benchmark resume`**never read preview sessions** (both scan only`is_preview=False`entries); the preview session never collides with a real run.`br benchmark gc-anchors`additionally sweeps`is_preview=True`session-state rows older than 48 hours (a new sweep class declared here, added to the four already documented). Unit test`test_cli_select.py::test_select_creates_ephemeral_preview_session`asserts that invoking the command body (a) writes a new session-state entry with`is_preview=True`and a fresh`uuid4()`session_id, (b) populates`selector_cache`under that session_id, (c) leaves no`selected_phase_ids`on any real (non-preview) session, and (d) the printed output matches the expected strata balance report. Unit test`test_cli_run.py::test_run_skips_preview_sessions`seeds a preview session and a real session and asserts`br benchmark resume`(the canonical resume subcommand owned by Phase 3's`cli_resume.py`; **resolves R54 Codex B3** — `br benchmark run --resume`is NOT a valid CLI flag surface in Phase 3's`cli_run.py`declaration,`resume` is a separate sibling subcommand per Phase 3's Files list) or the session-picker logic ignores the preview row.)
- `core/benchmark/cli_record_contracts.py` (MODIFY — replace Phase 1 stub with the `record-contracts` command body that calls `api_clients.record_contracts()` and writes the three vcrpy fixtures)
- `tests/benchmark/__init__.py` — **created in Phase 1**, not re-created here. Phase 2 only adds test modules into the existing directory.
- `tests/benchmark/test_selector.py` (NEW)
- `tests/benchmark/test_cli_select.py` (NEW — **resolves R51 W1**: pins the preview-session bootstrap contract declared in `cli_select.py`'s MODIFY entry above. Hosts `test_select_creates_ephemeral_preview_session` (asserts a fresh `uuid4()` session with `is_preview=True` + populated `selector_cache` is written, no real session's `selected_phase_ids` is touched, and the printed strata report matches) and `test_run_skips_preview_sessions` (asserts `br benchmark resume` (the canonical resume subcommand — **R54 Codex B3**) ignores `is_preview=True` rows). Referenced throughout Phase 2 acceptance text; without this explicit file declaration the preview-bootstrap contract would have no scheduled test.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_lockres.py` (NEW)
- `tests/benchmark/test_training_cutoffs.py` (NEW — **resolves R39 W2**; covers `get_cutoffs()` round-trip through `load_config()` and asserts no module-level date constants exist.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_api_clients.py` (NEW — uses responses/vcrpy against recorded fixtures)
- `tests/benchmark/fixtures/walter-contract.yaml` (NEW — vcrpy cassette recorded during the API-contract discovery spike; frozen request/response schema for Walter's endpoints)
- `tests/benchmark/fixtures/lomax-contract.yaml` (NEW — vcrpy cassette, same pattern as Walter)
- `tests/benchmark/fixtures/below-contract.yaml` (NEW — vcrpy cassette for Below `POST /api/classify`)
- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/layer-cache.json` (NEW — runtime artifact: keyed by `phase_id`, value = the layer string returned by Below `/api/classify` for phases whose declared-files list was ambiguous under the path-prefix mapping. Written by `selector.py` as a deterministic cache so subsequent selector invocations reuse the same classification rather than re-calling Below. **Concurrency protection via file lock (resolves R32 W2)**: every write wraps `tmp+fsync+rename` inside an `fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX)` acquired on a dedicated lock file `/tmp/br3-bench-layer-cache.lock` (not on the cache file itself, so reads do not need to acquire the lock). Every read acquires `fcntl.flock(LOCK_SH)` on the same lock file and then reads the cache file's current-on-disk contents. This protects against the concurrent-write race that would otherwise exist when `selector.redraw()` is called mid-run from Phase 3's scheduler (a cell failure path) while an unrelated `br benchmark select` or `br benchmark run` on Muddy is also writing the cache. The **single-writer invariant on the cache file's contents** still holds because the flock serializes writes; the only thing the lock adds over the earlier "serialized by CLI invocation" claim is safety against multiple concurrent orchestrator processes on Muddy — which is a documented supported state per the session-registry concurrent-orchestrator contract in Phase 1 (`SessionState.resume_session_id`). File is git-ignored by `.buildrunner/.gitignore`. Appears in this Files list so the owner phase is explicit.)
- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/layer_provenance.json` (NEW — runtime artifact: aggregate summary `{total_phases: int, by_source: dict[Literal["path_heuristic","below_classifier","fallback_fullstack"], int], fallback_share: float}`. Written by `selector.py` after every selection run and consumed by Phase 7's regression for the 20%-fallback-share layer-covariate-drop guard, and by Phase 8's report for the caveats section. **Same lock as `layer-cache.json`**: every `tmp+fsync+rename` write wraps `fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX)` on `/tmp/br3-bench-layer-cache.lock` (the **shared** lock for both layer artifacts — a single lock serializes all layer-classification state mutations). Reads take `LOCK_SH` on the same lock file. This resolves R32 W2 for the provenance artifact alongside the cache. The single-writer invariant holds even under concurrent `selector.redraw()` / selector `select()` / selector `select_with_buffer()` calls from two orchestrators, because every write path on the selector passes through the shared lock. Atomic write semantics are preserved by the existing `tmp+fsync+rename` pattern; the flock is added on top of it.)
- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/api-status.json` (NEW — runtime artifact: `{walter: {verified: bool, reason: Optional[str], recorded_at_utc: str}, lomax: {...}, below: {...}}`. Written by `api_clients.record_contracts()` after the Phase 2 API-contract discovery spike; read by Phase 5's scorer to gate Walter/Lomax enrichment per-client. Atomic write via `tmp+fsync+rename`.)

**Blocked by:** Phase 1 (needs `models.py`, `deps.py`)

**Deliverables:**

- [ ] BUILD-spec markdown parser. Input corpus: `.buildrunner/builds/BUILD_*.md` in this repository (the benchmark runs on this repo's own past phases). From each markdown file the parser extracts **phase number, declared files, checklist items** — these are the fields that live in the markdown. The **`lock:` commit SHA is NOT parsed from markdown** (BUILD files do not record the SHA inline); instead the parser passes `(build_file, phase_number)` to `lockres.resolve_lock()` (the shared helper defined in this phase) which resolves the SHA by walking git history for commits whose subject matches `^lock: claim Phase <N>` and whose diff touched `<build_file>`. The markdown parser and `lockres` are the two input sources for `PhaseSpec`; they are orthogonal and produce non-overlapping fields — no contradiction.
- [ ] **Layer assignment (populates `PhaseSpec.layer`, consumed by Phase 7/8 stratification and Phase 2 `redraw` stratum)**: layer is derived deterministically from the phase's declared-files list via the path-prefix mapping documented in `selector.py`: `ui/**` or `src/components/**` → `frontend`; `api/**`, `core/**`, `supabase/functions/**` → `backend`; both prefixes present → `fullstack`; `.buildrunner/**` or `*.md`-only changes → `docs`; `scripts/**`, `*.yaml`, `*.toml`, dotfiles → `infra`; `tests/**`-only → `testing`; `migrations/**` → `data-migration`. If the declared-files list is empty or the mapping is ambiguous, a Below `POST /api/classify` call over the phase's goal + first-3 deliverables + declared-files classifies among the seven canonical categories; the classification is cached to `.buildrunner/benchmarks/layer-cache.json` keyed by `phase_id` so subsequent runs are deterministic. Below-unreachable fallback: default to `fullstack` and log a `layer_fallback` entry in the selector's output — a conservative label that keeps the phase in the pool without biasing stratification. **Provenance tracking (resolves R24 W16 / codex layer-fallback-distortion)**: `PhaseSpec` carries a companion `layer_source: Literal["path_heuristic","below_classifier","fallback_fullstack"]` field (declared in Phase 1's `PhaseSpec` schema alongside `layer`) recording which branch assigned the label. The selector writes this field for every phase; the aggregator (Phase 7) groups by `layer_source` and reports the share-by-source in `.buildrunner/benchmarks/layer_provenance.json`. **Guard rule**: if `fallback_fullstack` share exceeds **20%** of the achieved phase pool, Phase 7's regression **drops the `layer` covariate** (same auto-drop path as Walter/Lomax) because the factor is dominated by a conservative label rather than a measured one, and the report's caveats section flags "layer stratification degraded: N/M phases defaulted to fullstack due to Below unreachability". Phase 2's selector also re-weights the stratified draw to compensate — `fallback_fullstack`-sourced phases **still carry `PhaseSpec.layer="fullstack"` and still count toward the `fullstack` stratum's quota** (resolves R48 W10 — `PhaseSpec.layer` remains the single stratification key; there is NO implicit extra stratum and `Literal["backend","frontend","fullstack","docs","infra","testing","data-migration"]` stays 7-valued), but are drawn **uniformly within the `layer_source`-partitioned subset of the `fullstack` stratum** so the draw does not silently over-select Below-inferred fullstacks relative to path-heuristic-confirmed fullstacks. Concretely: within the `fullstack` stratum, the selector partitions candidates into two buckets by `layer_source` (`path_heuristic`/`below_classifier` vs `fallback_fullstack`); the target count for the stratum is allocated proportionally to the bucket sizes (not uniformly across buckets — that would under-weight path-heuristic fullstacks when few fallbacks exist, and over-weight them when many do). If the `fullstack` stratum's target count exceeds the path-heuristic/below-classifier bucket size, the selector draws the remainder from the fallback bucket and emits a `stratum_warning: fallback_drawn=<n>` entry in the selector's output so the report caveat is exact. The `PhaseSpec.layer="fullstack"` invariant is preserved end-to-end: Phase 7's regression stratification, Phase 8's report stratification, and Phase 2's `redraw` stratum all consume `PhaseSpec.layer` alone and observe no extra stratum value. Unit test `test_selector.py::test_fallback_fullstack_preserves_layer_stratum` seeds a candidate pool with 3 `path_heuristic fullstack` + 5 `fallback_fullstack` phases and a stratum quota of 4, asserts that (a) every drawn phase has `PhaseSpec.layer="fullstack"` (no drawn phase has a non-fullstack layer because of fallback), (b) the within-stratum draw respects the proportional split, and (c) no `layer` stratum value appears in the selector's output other than the seven canonical ones. Unit test `test_selector.py::test_layer_provenance` covers all three source values including the 20%-threshold guard. Selector unit test covers each of the seven mapping cases plus the Below-classify fallback path with a stubbed client.
- [ ] **Shared lock-resolution helper**: `core/benchmark/lockres.py` (NEW, created in this phase) exposes `resolve_lock(build_file, phase_number) -> LockResolution`. **LockResolution has exactly three variants**: `ok(sha: str, warnings: list[str])`, `no_lock`, `merge_commit_lock`. There is **no separate `ambiguous_lock` variant**: when multiple commits match the phase number, the helper resolves the ambiguity in-helper by preferring the most recent non-merge commit and returns `ok(sha, warnings=["ambiguous_lock: <n> candidates matched"])`. Callers (selector + runner) therefore pattern-match on exactly three cases, and warnings flow through `ok.warnings` to the session log without changing the call-site's control flow. **Evidence check (2026-04-16 against actual BR3 git history)**: `git log --all --grep='^lock: claim Phase' --format='%H %s'` returns many matches, and **not all of them touch a BUILD file** — e.g. `560b2465 lock: claim Phase 5 - Codex Power Features` has no BUILD file in its diff, while `ab6bc1b3 lock: claim Phase 4 - /commit Hard Walter Gate + Direct Push` touches `.buildrunner/builds/BUILD_walter-auto-provision.md`. So a pathspec filter on `-- <build_file>` would reject valid phases whose lock commit only bumped the lockfile or other non-BUILD paths. The helper therefore uses a **three-stage resolver**:
  - **Stage 1 (scope, no pathspec)**: `subprocess.run(["git", "log", "--all", "--extended-regexp", "--grep=^lock: claim Phase " + str(phase_number) + "($|[^0-9])", "--format=%H %P %s"], ...)`. Using `--extended-regexp` (ERE) is mandatory because the alternation `($|[^0-9])` is not valid in git's default basic-regex mode (`--grep` is BRE-by-default, where `$|` is a literal `$|` two-character sequence, not an alternation). ERE lets the word-boundary disambiguation (`Phase 10` must not match `Phase 1`) work as intended. `%P` is printed so the helper can detect merge commits (more than one parent SHA).
  - **Stage 1b (reachability filter — resolves R30 W4)**: `--all` intentionally casts wide so we can find lock commits that live on merged feature branches, but it also sweeps up commits on **remote-tracking branches that were never merged into the working branch** (abandoned work) and on tags. After Stage 1, the helper filters each candidate SHA through `git merge-base --is-ancestor <sha> <anchor_ref>` where `anchor_ref` is resolved as the first of: (a) `HEAD`'s upstream if configured (`git rev-parse --abbrev-ref --symbolic-full-name @{u}`), (b) `refs/heads/main`, (c) `HEAD` — whichever first resolves to a valid ref in the repo. Exit 0 means reachable and the candidate survives; exit 1 means the commit is not an ancestor of the working line of history (abandoned branch / stale remote-only ref) and the candidate is dropped with a `unreachable_from_anchor` note in the internal trace. The anchor ref is chosen once per `resolve_lock` call and logged via `warnings=["anchor_ref=<name>"]` when any candidate was filtered, so the report can attribute drops. Unit test `test_lockres.py::test_reachability_filter` seeds a synthetic repo with (i) a lock commit on `main`, (ii) a lock commit on a remote-only `origin/abandoned-feature` branch never merged, and (iii) a lock commit on a merged feature branch — asserts the abandoned-branch candidate is dropped while the merged-branch candidate survives.
  - **Stage 2 (prefer BUILD-file-touching commits)**: for each candidate, `git show --stat --format= <sha>` is scanned for the target `<build_file>` path. Candidates whose diff touched `<build_file>` form the **preferred set**. If the preferred set is non-empty, the resolver returns `ok(most_recent_non_merge_in_preferred_set, warnings=[])` or — if more than one preferred candidate exists — `ok(most_recent, warnings=["ambiguous_lock: <n> build-file-touching candidates"])`.
  - **No Stage 3 fallback (safer-drop policy)**: if the Stage-2 preferred set is empty (no candidate touched `<build_file>`), `resolve_lock` returns **`no_lock`** rather than guessing. Phase numbers repeat across BUILD files (`Phase 1` exists in every BUILD spec), so a bare `lock: claim Phase N` commit that touched no BUILD file cannot be proven to belong to `<build_file>` vs any other BUILD file's `Phase N`. Selecting the wrong pre-phase commit would corrupt both the clone checkout (wrong code state for the contestant) and the cutoff stratification (wrong commit date → wrong pre/post-cutoff stratum). Returning `no_lock` drops the phase via `selector.redraw(phase_id)` and enqueues a replacement — the safer failure mode. **Operational note**: in this repository, lock commits are conventionally created by the `/begin` command which amends the BUILD spec with a phase-in-progress note, so real lock commits nearly always touch `<build_file>`. Phases whose lock commits touched no BUILD file (observed in early BR3 development before the `/begin` convention was enforced) are intentionally excluded from the benchmark pool. **Zero BUILD-file-touching non-merge candidates → `no_lock`**; **only merge commits match `<build_file>` → `merge_commit_lock`** (Phase 3's `setup_clone` treats both as terminal-drop outcomes, per the deliverable below). Unit test `test_lockres.py::test_stage2_only_no_fallback` seeds a synthetic repo with (a) `BUILD_A.md` claiming Phase 3 via commit touching only `BUILD_A.md`, (b) `BUILD_B.md` claiming Phase 3 via commit touching only `BUILD_B.md`, (c) a bare `lock: claim Phase 3 ...` commit touching neither BUILD file; asserts `resolve_lock(BUILD_A.md, 3)` returns the BUILD_A-touching commit (not the bare or BUILD_B commit), and `resolve_lock(BUILD_C.md, 3)` (a BUILD file with no touching commit) returns `no_lock` regardless of whether bare candidates exist.
  - The `--all` flag is included because some lock claims live on merged feature branches rather than on `main`'s linear history; the scan remains fast (git stores commit subjects in the commit graph). The unit test in `test_lockres.py` seeds a synthetic repo with (a) two BUILD files each claiming "Phase 1" where only one's lock commit touches the BUILD file, (b) a phase whose lock commit touches no BUILD file at all, and (c) a `Phase 10` commit present in the same repo as a `Phase 1` commit — and asserts (1) the ERE word-boundary rejects the `Phase 10` match from the `Phase 1` result set, (2) the BUILD-file-touching preferred set wins when non-empty and ties within the preferred set resolve to `ok(most_recent, warnings=["ambiguous_lock: <n> build-file-touching candidates"])`, (3) when the preferred set is empty the helper returns exactly `no_lock` — **not** a bare-candidate fall-through (resolves R29 B2 contract contradiction: the earlier draft's "fall-back returns most-recent match" language was stale from a pre-R28 three-stage design and has been removed; the current contract is Stage 1 scope → Stage 2 BUILD-file-preferred → `no_lock`, with no Stage 3), and (4) a candidate commit with multiple parents (merge) that does touch `<build_file>` returns `merge_commit_lock`. Both the selector (Phase 2) and the runner (Phase 3) call this helper — there is no second lock-resolution path.
- [ ] Candidate scoring formula (checklist count + files touched + verify steps + layer diversity).
- [ ] Self-containment filter (excludes phases referencing deliverables from later phases).
- [ ] External-only-files filter (excludes phases with zero in-repo file changes).
- [ ] Training-cutoff stratification: `core/benchmark/training_cutoffs.py` exposes a single function `get_cutoffs() -> dict[Literal["claude","codex"], datetime]` that calls `core.benchmark.config.load_config()` and reads the **`contestants.*_training_cutoff_utc`** fields from `.buildrunner/benchmarks/config.yaml` (resolves R38 W1 + R39 B1 — the single source of truth is Phase 1's `BenchmarkConfig.contestants` block declared in the preconditions table at line 81, NOT a parallel `training_cutoffs:` key; earlier drafts referenced a non-existent `training_cutoffs: {claude, codex}` subobject which would have produced a KeyError at config load). The canonical fields are `contestants.claude_training_cutoff_utc: str` (ISO-8601) and `contestants.codex_training_cutoff_utc: str` (ISO-8601), values frozen in Phase 1's config template as `claude_training_cutoff_utc: "2026-01-31T00:00:00Z"` and `codex_training_cutoff_utc: "2025-11-01T00:00:00Z"`. `get_cutoffs()` parses each value via `datetime.fromisoformat(value.replace("Z","+00:00"))` and returns `{"claude": <datetime>, "codex": <datetime>}`. The selector imports `get_cutoffs` (not module-level constants) and tags each phase `pre`/`post` per model based on the `lock:` commit date from `resolve_lock` — same-day-or-earlier = `pre`, later = `post`. Unit test `tests/benchmark/test_training_cutoffs.py::test_cutoffs_loaded_from_config` (**resolves R39 W2** — explicitly declared in Phase 2's Files list alongside the module it tests) writes a synthetic config.yaml with known `contestants.{claude,codex}_training_cutoff_utc` fields, imports `get_cutoffs()`, and asserts the returned dict matches the file verbatim (round-trip through `load_config`). A second test asserts the module defines **no** top-level date constants — it introspects `training_cutoffs` for any `datetime` or `date`-typed attributes and fails if any exist, cementing the "config-only" contract.
- [ ] Exclusion of phases already present in `benchmark_registry.jsonl`.
- [ ] **`.buildrunner/benchmarks/exclusions.jsonl` — single-source-of-truth contract (resolves R26 W5 double-ownership)**: the pydantic model `ExclusionRow` is **declared exclusively in Phase 1's `core/benchmark/models.py`** (single schema owner, listed in Phase 1's declarative-up-front model list alongside `RegistryRow`). **Phase 2 is the first _writer_, not a schema owner** — Phase 2's selector imports `ExclusionRow` from `models.py` and calls the shared append-writer. The file path `.buildrunner/benchmarks/exclusions.jsonl` is top-level single file (no per-run-id subdir). Each line is one JSON object matching the Phase 1 schema: `{phase_id: str, reason: Literal["paraphrase_failed","equivalence_failed","stratum_violation","pool_exhausted"], attempt_count: int, failed_at_utc: str, session_id: str, extra: dict}`. `extra` is reason-specific: for `stratum_violation` it carries `{"original_stratum": str, "substituted_stratum": str}`; for `pool_exhausted` it carries `{"achieved_n": int, "stratum_distribution": dict[str,int]}`; for `paraphrase_failed` / `equivalence_failed` it is `{}` (empty). Appended under `fcntl.flock` exactly like the registry. All three writers — Phase 2's `redraw`, Phase 4's paraphrase/equivalence failure path, and Phase 2's `pool_exhausted` final write — use the same pydantic writer imported from `models.py`; the reader is a stateless line-by-line JSONL scan in Phase 7/8. **No schema is (re)declared in Phase 2 — only the writer call-site and the file-path invariant are documented here.**
- [ ] **Stratified redraw rule on phase drop (preserves stratification invariant)**: the selector exposes `redraw(dropped_phase_id) -> Optional[PhaseSpec]`. Strata are the cartesian product `{layer} × {cutoff_stratum_codex, cutoff_stratum_claude}` (since cutoffs are per-model, the paired cell is what must stay balanced). Rule: (1) attempt to draw a replacement from the **same stratum** as the dropped phase, using the selector's deterministic ranking; (2) if that stratum is exhausted, draw from the nearest adjacent stratum under a fixed distance metric (same layer, other cutoff pair; then adjacent layer, same cutoff pair) and append a `stratum_violation` entry (schema above) naming the original and substituted strata; (3) if fewer than two strata have any survivors left (i.e. the pool can no longer support even a minimal balance), abort selection, record the achieved N and stratum distribution (as a `pool_exhausted` entry), and hand off to the Phase 7 degraded-N decision rule. The selector unit test exercises all three paths with a synthetic pool and asserts the log file path is exactly `.buildrunner/benchmarks/exclusions.jsonl`.
- [ ] **API contract discovery spike (Phase 2 deliverable, runs once before Phase 5)**: endpoint _paths_ are verified (see dependency table) but request/response _body shapes_ are not. Phase 2 exercises each endpoint once with a real request, records the full request/response via `vcrpy` to `tests/benchmark/fixtures/{walter,lomax,below}-contract.yaml`, and pydantic-generates typed models from the recordings. The recorded fixtures become the frozen contract the rest of the harness codes against. If a fixture recording fails (e.g. Walter refuses the request shape we try, or the status payload does not contain a parseable verdict field), the affected client is marked `unverified` in `.buildrunner/benchmarks/api-status.json` and Phase 5 scoring falls back to its local-only path for that client (see Phase 5 deliverables). No fabricated body fields enter scoring logic: a field is only consumed after it has been observed in a live fixture.
- [ ] `WalterClient` surface: `trigger_run(project, payload: dict) -> TriggerResponse`, `get_run_status(run_id) -> RunStatus`, `get_latest_results(project?) -> ResultsPage`. `payload` and response models are whatever `vcrpy` records during the spike; if the spike can't produce a response with a parseable verdict, the client is marked `unverified` and `WalterClient.is_verified() -> False`. All scoring code gates on `is_verified()` — Walter is treated as **optional enrichment**, not a primary scoring path. Primary test-pass is computed locally by Phase 5 (see below).
- [ ] `LomaxClient` surface: `trigger_build(project) -> TriggerResponse`, `get_build_status(project) -> BuildStatus`, `list_projects() -> [Project]`. Same discovery-spike rule: request/response shapes come from the recorded fixture. **No per-run slug creation is attempted** (no verified API exists for it). If the spike can produce a status payload with a parseable build verdict against the _existing_ `br3-benchmark` project slug (which an operator pre-registers on Lomax once before Phase 9 — see ops step in Phase 5), Lomax is used as optional enrichment serialized through that single slug via `/tmp/br3-bench-lomax.lock`. If the slug does not exist or the spike fails, `LomaxClient.is_verified() -> False` and Phase 5 skips Lomax entirely.
- [ ] `BelowClient.classify(text, categories) -> {category, confidence}` — matches the verified `POST /api/classify` single-text multi-category contract (already confirmed during preflight). The equivalence-check wrapper in Phase 4 composes the A/B prompt.
- [ ] All three clients return typed pydantic models generated from the recorded fixtures; retries on 5xx with jittered backoff, fail-fast on 4xx.
- [ ] `api_contracts.md` lists each endpoint consumed, the fixture file that defines its shape, auth header form, and what the harness does on schema drift (hard fail with fixture-mismatch error; re-record required before re-run).
- [ ] **Selector API surface (three explicit call sites)**:
  - `select(count: int) -> list[PhaseSpec]` — picks `count` stratified candidates, used by Phase 10 for the N=30 full-run draw.
  - `select_with_buffer(target: int, buffer: int) -> list[PhaseSpec]` — picks `target + buffer` stratified candidates and returns them in deterministic rank order; the caller (Phase 9 pilot) consumes the first `target` survivors after paraphrase+equivalence filtering. This is the over-draw mode Phase 9 needs; it is a separate method (not a flag) so its semantics are explicit in the type signature.
  - `pool_survivors_after_paraphrase_equivalence` — **read-only property on the selector instance**. Returns `int` equal to `len(selected_phase_ids) - exclusions_scanned`, where `exclusions_scanned` is the count of distinct `phase_id`s in `.buildrunner/benchmarks/exclusions.jsonl` with `reason in {"paraphrase_failed","equivalence_failed"}` AND `session_id == self.session_id` (selector is session-scoped per Phase 1's `SessionState`). Computed on read via a stateless JSONL scan that opens its own file descriptor on `.buildrunner/benchmarks/exclusions.jsonl` and takes `fcntl.flock(LOCK_SH)` **on that descriptor** (resolves R30 W3 — the lock is scoped to `exclusions.jsonl`, not to `benchmark_registry.jsonl`; the registry reducer's `LOCK_EX` on the registry file is unrelated). The `LOCK_SH` here is compatible with the `exclusions.jsonl` writer's `LOCK_EX` on the same file (shared readers block exclusive writers and vice versa), so the count is always consistent with in-flight appends. Unit test `test_selector.py::test_pool_survivors_after_paraphrase_equivalence` seeds a synthetic exclusions.jsonl with 4 paraphrase_failed + 2 equivalence_failed + 1 stratum_violation entries and asserts the property returns `len(selected) - 6` (stratum_violation is not a paraphrase/equivalence drop and is excluded).
  - `replacement_phases_enqueued_by_redraw` — **read-only property on the selector instance**. Returns `int` equal to `len(session_state.redraw_map)` where `redraw_map: dict[str, str]` is the per-session dropped→replacement mapping written by `redraw()` (Phase 1 schema). Computed on read by reading the per-session file `.buildrunner/benchmarks/sessions/<session_id>.json` under the existing `SessionState` read path (no separate lock needed because `SessionState` reads are atomic-file reads via `tmp+fsync+rename` writes). This counts exactly the phases that were drawn from the candidate buffer to replace paraphrase/equivalence-dropped phases. Phase 10's achieved-runs formula `achieved_phases = min(30, selector.pool_survivors_after_paraphrase_equivalence + selector.replacement_phases_enqueued_by_redraw)` is now composed of two explicitly-typed properties on the same selector instance — no undefined symbol. Unit test `test_selector.py::test_replacement_phases_enqueued_by_redraw` seeds a session-state file with `redraw_map={"phase_a":"phase_x", "phase_b":"phase_y"}` and asserts the property returns 2.
  - `get_phase(phase_id: str) -> Optional[PhaseSpec]` — **read-only helper (resolves R29 B4 consumer-side)** that looks up a previously-drawn phase in the selector's session-state candidate cache by `phase_id`. Returns the cached `PhaseSpec` if the phase was drawn into the buffer (by `select()`, `select_with_buffer()`, or a prior `redraw()`), else `None`. Used by Phase 3's `runner.py` replacement-phase scheduler to materialize replacement `PhaseSpec` objects from `session_state.redraw_map` values without re-running the stratified draw (the stratified draw already happened inside `redraw()`; the scheduler just needs the object). The cache is populated at draw time by every path that mints a new `PhaseSpec`; `get_phase` never performs a fresh draw. Unit test `test_selector.py::test_get_phase_lookup` asserts cache hits for drawn phases and `None` for undrawn phase IDs.
  - `selected_phase_ids: list[str]` — **read-only property (resolves R32 B4)** returning the ordered list of `phase_id`s the selector has drawn into this session's buffer. Computed on read by returning a copy of `session_state.selected_phase_ids` (Phase 1 SessionState field; single-writer = Phase 2's selector). Phase 3's `runner.resume(session_id)` consumes this property to reconstruct `pending_queue` after a kill/restart (`pending = [selector.get_phase(pid) for pid in selector.selected_phase_ids if pid not in terminal_phase_set]` — see Phase 3's replacement-phase scheduler resume logic). This is the **only** symbol the resume path uses to enumerate drawn phases; no earlier draft's undefined `selector.selected_phases` attribute exists. Unit test `test_selector.py::test_selected_phase_ids_after_draws` asserts the property reflects `select()` / `select_with_buffer()` / `redraw()` appends in order.
  - `surviving_phase_count: int` — **read-only property (resolves R33 W1)** returning the count of distinct `phase_id` values in the selector's session whose paraphrase AND equivalence filters passed — equivalently, the number of phases for which at least one `CompletedRow` with `stage in {"scored","judged"}` exists in the registry for `session_id == self.session_id`. Computed on read by (a) opening `.buildrunner/benchmarks/benchmark_registry.jsonl` with `fcntl.flock(LOCK_SH)`, (b) scanning for `CompletedRow` rows with `row_type=="completed"` AND `stage in {"scored","judged"}` AND `session_id == self.session_id`, (c) projecting to `phase_id` and deduplicating, (d) excluding phases that appear in `.buildrunner/benchmarks/exclusions.jsonl` with `reason in {"paraphrase_failed","equivalence_failed"}` AND `session_id == self.session_id`. Returns `int`. This is the canonical input to Phase 10's `achieved_phases` formula and replaces the earlier additive formula that over-counted redraw reservations. Unit test `test_selector.py::test_surviving_phase_count` seeds a synthetic registry with 5 scored phases + 2 exclusions + 3 dropped phases and asserts `surviving_phase_count == 5`.
  - `redraw(dropped_phase_id: str, reason: str) -> Optional[PhaseSpec]` — stratified replacement (same stratum, then nearest adjacent, then abort) used mid-run when a phase drops per Invariant 16. **`redraw` is the SOLE writer of `DroppedRow`** (resolves R36 W1). **Idempotent on `dropped_phase_id`**: the first call for a given `dropped_phase_id` — under a **strict two-lock acquisition order: session-state flock FIRST (`/tmp/br3-bench-session-<session_id>.lock`), then registry flock SECOND (`/tmp/br3-bench-registry.lock`), never the reverse** (**resolves R54 Claude B2** — two code paths, `selector.redraw()` and any runner path that writes a registry row while also writing session-state, could each hold one of the two flocks and block on the other, deadlocking the orchestrator. The canonical lock order is session-state FIRST, registry SECOND; every code path in the harness that needs both flocks acquires them in this order and releases them in reverse (registry release first, session-state release second). `selector.redraw()`, `runner.run_cell()`'s three-row judge commit, `runner.finalize_run()`'s two-stage CompletedRow write, `cli_judge.py`'s backfill commit, and every other two-lock call site enforces this order. Unit test `test_selector.py::test_redraw_lock_order_is_session_first_registry_second` monkeypatches `fcntl.flock` to record acquisition order and asserts the session-state lock is acquired strictly before the registry lock in `selector.redraw()`) — `fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX)` acquisition — (a) appends a `DroppedRow{row_type="dropped", phase_id, reason, dropped_at_utc}` to `benchmark_registry.jsonl` via `registry.drop_phase(phase_id, reason)` (which `redraw` calls internally; no other code path in the harness calls `registry.drop_phase` directly — Phase 3's `setup_clone` and Phase 4's paraphrase/equivalence failure paths pass their reason string into `redraw` and `redraw` forwards it to `registry.drop_phase`), (b) atomically reserves a replacement slot by recording the replacement `phase_id` in the session-state file's `redraw_map: dict[str, str]` field (added to Phase 1's `SessionState` schema; single-writer = Phase 2's selector), (c) appends a sibling `ExclusionRow` to `.buildrunner/benchmarks/exclusions.jsonl` with the same reason (for Phase 2's `paraphrase_failed`/`equivalence_failed` reasons the `ExclusionRow` matches the reason; for Phase 3's `lock_unresolvable:<outcome>` reason the `ExclusionRow` reason is the Literal `pool_exhausted`-adjacent case — when lock resolution fails during selection, `redraw` writes `ExclusionRow.reason="stratum_violation"` only if the stratum runs out, else no `ExclusionRow` is written for lock-unresolvable drops since those are individual-phase-drop events not pool-level exclusions), and (d) returns the replacement `PhaseSpec`. **Subsequent calls for the same `dropped_phase_id` are no-ops** — `redraw` reads `redraw_map`, sees the existing mapping, and returns the already-reserved `PhaseSpec` (or `None` if the prior call exhausted the pool) without re-appending any row to either log. This guarantees that even if multiple per-cell failure paths (e.g. Phase 3's `setup_clone` lock-unresolvable, Phase 4's paraphrase failure) fire for the same `phase_id` across different `(model, sub_study, replication)` cells, **exactly one `DroppedRow` is appended AND exactly one replacement phase is enqueued into the full cell matrix**. The replacement phase's cells (all models × sub_studies × replications) are then dispatched as a cohort by the runner's top-level scheduler (not by the failing cell's code path), which keeps phase-balance intact. The per-cell failure paths in Phase 3 (`setup_clone` lock failure) and Phase 4 (paraphrase/equivalence failure) call `selector.redraw(phase_id, reason)` purely to trigger / idempotently confirm the replacement — they never try to dispatch the replacement's cells themselves. Unit test `test_selector.py::test_redraw_is_sole_dropped_row_writer` seeds a synthetic registry, calls `selector.redraw("phase-7", "paraphrase_failed")` twice, and asserts exactly ONE `DroppedRow` is present for `phase-7` after both calls (idempotence + sole-writer invariant combined).
  - `set_paraphrase(phase_id: str, sub_study: Literal["native","neutral"], prompt: str) -> None` — **writer method (resolves R38 B1)** that persists a paraphrased prompt for `(phase_id, sub_study)` onto the selector's session-state `selector_cache[phase_id]` entry. Single-writer = this selector instance; called exclusively from Phase 3's `runner.run_cell` inside the phase-scoped `/tmp/br3-bench-paraphrase-<phase_id>.lock` after the paraphraser + equivalence checks both pass. Implementation (**resolves R39 B2** — session-scoped helpers take `session_id` as their first argument per the Phase 1 declaration): reads the current selector_cache map via `SessionState.get_flag(self.session_id, "selector_cache")` which returns a `dict[str, dict]` (the full cache; Phase 1's `get_flag` does not accept sub-keys), looks up `cache[phase_id]` in memory, validates it back into a `PhaseSpec` pydantic instance, sets `spec.paraphrased_prompt_native = prompt` or `spec.paraphrased_prompt_neutral = prompt` based on `sub_study`, re-serializes via `spec.model_dump()`, and writes back through `SessionState.set_map_entry(self.session_id, "selector_cache", phase_id, updated_dict)` (the 4-arg `set_map_entry` helper declared in Phase 1: `(session_id, key, sub_key, sub_value)`; atomic `tmp+fsync+rename` under the same session-state write path). Rejects unknown `phase_id` values (raises `KeyError`) because `set_paraphrase` is only legal after `select`/`redraw` minted the phase into the cache. Unit test `test_selector.py::test_set_paraphrase_persists_into_cache` calls `set_paraphrase("phase-7", "native", "...prompt...")` and asserts both (a) the in-memory selector's `get_phase("phase-7").paraphrased_prompt_native` reflects the new value AND (b) a fresh selector instance reading the same session-state file sees the persisted value (round-trip through disk).
  - All three share the same underlying ranking + filter pipeline; only the draw policy differs. Unit tests cover each path.
- [ ] `br benchmark select` outputs ranked candidates with strata balance report.

**Success Criteria:** Returns 30 candidates balanced across layers and cutoff strata. API-client contract tests round-trip **against the recorded vcrpy fixtures** (`tests/benchmark/fixtures/{walter,lomax,below}-contract.yaml`) under pytest — no live cluster call is made during the contract-test suite, so Walter/Lomax/Below being offline never breaks Phase 2's test gate. The fixtures are recorded **once** during the discovery spike (deliverable above) against the live cluster when it is green; re-recording requires an explicit operator run of `br benchmark record-contracts`, not a normal test invocation.
