This preserves the soft-fail posture (Phase 1 / Phase 5 say Walter + Lomax are optional enrichment) without forfeiting contract verification: schema drift versus the recorded fixture fails the test with a "fixture mismatch, re-record required" error.

---

### Phase 3: Execution Engine — Worktree + Dispatch + Replication Loop

**Goal:** Runner sets up an isolated worktree at the pre-phase commit, dispatches to a given (model, node) pair via cluster, captures all outputs, and executes `replications` independent attempts per (phase, model, sub-study) cell.

**Files:**

- `core/benchmark/runner.py` (NEW — exposes `class Runner` (**`__init__` signature resolves R43 B3 — `config: BenchmarkConfig` is a required constructor argument**; full signature: `Runner(config: BenchmarkConfig, scorer: Optional[ScorerProtocol] = None, judge: Optional["BenchmarkJudge"] = None, probe_scheduler: Optional["ProbeScheduler"] = None)`. `config` is the `BenchmarkConfig` instance returned from `load_config()` (Phase 1 `config.py`) and is stored as `self.config` on the Runner; every internal method that needs config values reads from `self.config` (e.g. `run_session`'s `expected_cell_count = len(self.config.selector.sub_studies) * self.config.selector.replications` for `probe_scheduler.schedule(...)`, the replacement-phase scheduler's identical `expected_cell_count` computation, `runner.dispatch_run`'s `lease_seconds = self.config.registry.lease_seconds`, and `runner._claim_judge_lease_seconds = self.config.registry.judge_lease_seconds`). The `config`-first constructor ordering keeps dependency injection uniform: all downstream optional dependencies are `None`-defaulted so unit tests can construct a Runner with `Runner(config=load_config())` and no live scorer/judge/scheduler. Phase 5's wire-in updates the CLI entry points to pass `Runner(config=config, scorer=BenchmarkScorer(config))`; Phase 6 extends that to `Runner(config=config, scorer=BenchmarkScorer(config), judge=BenchmarkJudge(config), probe_scheduler=ProbeScheduler(config))`. The module-level shim `run_cell(...)` is updated to read `config = load_config()` internally before instantiating `Runner(config=config)` so simple CLI call sites still work without threading config through every call site. Both surfaces are documented and both wrap the same `setup_clone → dispatch_run → finalize_run → [scorer.score_run?] → teardown_clone` call order. `BenchmarkScorer` is the class exported from Phase 5's `core/benchmark/scorer.py`.)
- `core/benchmark/node_allocator.py` (NEW — randomized + balanced node assignment, consumes `deps.probe_node_pool()`)
- `core/benchmark/prompts.py` (MODIFY — add `build_native_prompt` + `build_neutral_prompt`)
- `core/benchmark/cli_run.py`, `cli_resume.py`, `cli_status.py`, `cli_gc_anchors.py` (MODIFY — replace Phase 1 stubs with command bodies that call into `runner.py` / `registry.py`. **`cli_run.py` flag surface (resolves R30 B3)**: the `run` subcommand exposes these Typer options, fully declared in Phase 3: `--phases <int>` (count of phases to draw, default from `config.selector.target_phases`), `--replications <int>` (default from `config.selector.replications`), `--sub-studies <str>` (comma-separated, accepts `native`, `neutral`, or `native,neutral`; default `native,neutral`), `--models <str>` (**resolves R42 B1 — cross-phase model-identifier consistency**: comma-separated **short model keys** drawn from `config.contestants.*_runtime_flag` (canonical values `"claude"` and `"codex"` — see Phase 1's `ContestantsConfig` schema declaration above), NOT the longer `*_model_version` strings (`"claude-opus-4-7"`, `"codex-5-4"`). The short key is the canonical `model` field value flowing through every phase downstream: Phase 2's `training_cutoffs.get_cutoffs()[model]` (dict-indexing against the no-arg signature declared in Phase 2 — `get_cutoffs() -> dict[Literal["claude","codex"], datetime]`; resolves R52 B2 — the caller indexes the returned dict by the short model key rather than passing the key as an argument, preserving Phase 2's no-arg signature authoritative), Phase 4's `RecognitionRow.model` field, Phase 6's `probe_scheduler.schedule(phase_id, model, ...)` / `notify_cell_judged(phase_id, model)` calls, Phase 7's aggregator `groupby(cell_key.model)`, and every `CompletedRow.model` / `JudgeClaimRow.worker_id`-free field all use `{"claude","codex"}` exclusively. The `*_model_version` values (`"claude-opus-4-7"`, `"codex-5-4"`) are display-and-audit-only: Phase 3's `run_meta.json` records the model version string (so the audit trail pins the exact version benchmarked), and Phase 8's report methods section prints both the `_runtime_flag` (the `model` key used in analysis) and the `_model_version` (the exact contestant version) so readers can map the short key back to the pinned version. `cli_run.py` rejects any `--models` value not in `{config.contestants.claude_runtime_flag, config.contestants.codex_runtime_flag}` with remediation message `"--models accepts only short runtime-flag keys from config.contestants.*_runtime_flag (claude|codex); got '<value>'"`. Unit test `test_cli_run.py::test_models_flag_rejects_long_version_strings` asserts that `--models claude-opus-4-7` exits non-zero with the remediation message and that `--models claude` succeeds. Default `--models claude,codex` (both contestants), `--pilot / --no-pilot` (boolean flag, default `--no-pilot`; when set the scheduler writes results under `.buildrunner/benchmarks/results/pilot/<session_id>/` and enables the pilot-specific completion gates described in Phase 9 — reduced-N acceptance, pilot-deblind assertion, contention-ratio check; when unset results go under `.buildrunner/benchmarks/results/full-n30/<session_id>/`), `--session-id <str>` (**display-only, resolves R31 W1 + W5**: accepted on the `run` subcommand solely for operator convenience when scripting pre-computed run labels; the flag's value is **not** used as the session id. `br benchmark run` always mints a fresh `session_id = uuid4()` internally (matches Phase 1's `SessionState` contract byte-for-byte — `uuid4`, NOT `uuid7`; all earlier UUIDv7 references are superseded by this single-UUID-scheme policy). If `--session-id` is passed AND the supplied value differs from the minted `uuid4`, the operator-supplied value is echoed in the startup banner as the "display label" and recorded in `SessionState.display_label: Optional[str]` (a new optional field added to Phase 1's `SessionState` schema as part of this resolution; single-writer = Phase 1 `deps.py`), but the authoritative `session_id` is always the minted uuid4. **`br benchmark resume --session-id <id>` is unchanged** — resume requires a real minted session id, not a display label. This removes the ambiguity that R31 W1 flagged: `run` never accepts an externally-supplied session id for resume semantics; only the display-label path exists.) The `--pilot` flag is declared here in Phase 3's `cli_run.py` so Phase 9's `br benchmark run --pilot ...` invocation is backed by a real flag; Phase 9 does not MODIFY `cli_run.py`, it only consumes the flag.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_runner.py` (NEW)
- `tests/benchmark/test_cli_run.py` (NEW — **resolves R43 B1 (Codex)**: CLI-level unit tests for the `br benchmark run` Typer command body added in `cli_run.py`. Covers: `test_models_flag_rejects_long_version_strings` (asserts `--models claude-opus-4-7` exits non-zero with the remediation message and that `--models claude` succeeds — pins the R42 B1 short-key enforcement contract); `test_models_flag_rejects_unknown_key` (asserts `--models foo` exits non-zero); `test_session_id_flag_is_display_only` (asserts the minted `session_id` in `SessionState` is a fresh uuid4 even when `--session-id display-label-123` is passed, and that `display_label` is recorded); `test_pilot_flag_selects_pilot_results_dir` (asserts `--pilot` writes results under `.buildrunner/benchmarks/results/pilot/<session_id>/` and `--no-pilot` writes under `full-n30/<session_id>/`). Listed here in Phase 3's Files list because Phase 3 is the sole owner of `cli_run.py`; R42 B1's test name reference here would otherwise be a dangling file reference.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_node_allocator.py` (NEW)
- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/results/<run_id>/run_meta.json` (NEW — per-run metadata artifact written by `runner.finalize_run()` for every cell. Schema: `{run_id: str, phase_id: str, model: str, sub_study: str, replication_index: int, node_name: str, pre_run_commit_sha: str, post_run_commit_sha: str, no_changes: bool, wall_clock_ms: int, exit_code: int, token_counts: TokenCounts, token_source: Literal["stdout_json","stderr_usage","none"], prompt_audit_path: str, dispatch_exit_code: int, anchor_ref: str, created_at_utc: str}`. This artifact is the durable per-run audit trail that complements the registry's progressive-fill rows — `CompletedRow` carries the same `RunResult`/`ObjectiveMetrics`/`AdherenceMetrics` fields for analysis, while `run_meta.json` carries the invocation-level metadata (dispatch exit code sub-class, token parse source, prompt audit path) the scorer and the aggregator do not need to index. Written via `tmp+fsync+rename`. Read by the report (Phase 8) and `br benchmark score --run-id <id>` (Phase 5 re-score path). Listed here so the owning phase is explicit.)

**Blocked by:** Phase 1, Phase 2 (imports `core/benchmark/lockres.py` and `api_clients.py`), Phase 4 (imports `paraphraser.paraphrase_spec()` and `equivalence.check_equivalence()` — the runner calls both before dispatching the contestant, so paraphrase+equivalence must land **before** the runner is integrated)

**Deliverables:**

- [ ] **Architecture note — why a FRESH LOCAL CLONE, not a worktree, is the isolation primitive (verified 2026-04-16 against `~/.buildrunner/scripts/dispatch-to-node.sh`).** The dispatcher has **two** behaviors incompatible with `git worktree`-based isolation and we cannot modify the global script:
      (1) **Line 48** rejects any path whose `.git` is not a directory: `if [ ! -d "$PROJECT_PATH/.git" ]; then ... exit 2`. A `git worktree` places a `.git` **file** (containing `gitdir: <parent>/.git/worktrees/<name>`), not a directory. Verified: `git worktree add --detach /tmp/probe HEAD` produces `[ -f .git ] && ! [ -d .git ]`. So passing any worktree path as `$PROJECT_PATH` makes the dispatcher exit 2 before it does any work.
      (2) **Lines 617–641** run `git merge --ff-only "$SESSION_NAME"` against `ORIGINAL_BRANCH` (fast-forward always succeeds on a branch that started at HEAD), then `git branch -d "$SESSION_NAME"` — the SESSION_NAME branch is deleted on success. Relying on that branch surviving to read `refs/heads/bench-<run_id>` afterward would fail with "unknown revision".
      The clean fix avoiding any global-script patch: **run each benchmark run in a fresh local clone**, not a worktree. `git clone --local --shared` creates a full standalone `.git` directory (passing the line-48 check) while sharing object storage with the parent repo via `objects/info/alternates` (so clone creation is ≤2 seconds for this repo even at 35k files). The contestant's post-run commit ends up on `ORIGINAL_BRANCH` inside the clone via the dispatcher's ff-merge; we then `git fetch` that branch from the clone into the parent repo under `refs/heads/bench/{run_id}` to give it a durable anchor, after which the clone is disposable.
- [ ] `setup_clone(phase, run_id) -> CloneHandle`: calls `lockres.resolve_lock(phase.build_file, phase.phase_number)` (attribute names match the Phase 1 `PhaseSpec` dataclass exactly — `build_file: str` and `phase_number: int`). **Non-SHA outcome handling**: `resolve_lock` returns exactly one of three `LockResolution` variants: `ok(sha, warnings)`, `no_lock`, `merge_commit_lock` (Phase 2 deliverable). `setup_clone` pattern-matches on three cases — there is no fourth `ambiguous_lock` variant because Phase 2's resolver collapses ambiguity into `ok(sha, warnings=["ambiguous_lock: ..."])` internally. If the result is `no_lock` or `merge_commit_lock`, `setup_clone` does **not** clone — it calls `selector.redraw(phase_id, reason=f"lock_unresolvable:{outcome}")` to request a stratified replacement (same redraw path used by Invariant 16). **`selector.redraw()` is the SOLE writer of `DroppedRow`** (resolves R36 W1 — prior drafts had `setup_clone` appending a `DroppedRow` directly AND calling redraw, which double-wrote the same drop event; the corrected contract is that callers never call `registry.drop_phase` directly; redraw owns both the drop-log append and the replacement-slot reservation under a single lock acquisition). `setup_clone` receives the replacement `PhaseSpec` (or `None` on pool-exhausted) and returns `None` for the originating cell (callers treat `None` as "cell short-circuited, no RunResult to emit"; the replacement's cells are dispatched as a cohort by the top-level scheduler per Phase 2's redraw contract). For `ok(sha, warnings)`, `warnings` are appended to the session log (so ambiguity is audit-visible) and the clone proceeds: `git clone --local --shared --no-hardlinks --quiet <PARENT_REPO> /tmp/br3-bench-<run_id>/ && git -C /tmp/br3-bench-<run_id>/ checkout -q -b bench-src-<run_id> <pre_run_commit_sha>`. This invariant (only `ok(sha, ...)` survives past `resolve_lock`; the two non-`ok` variants are drops) is the single contract between Phase 2's `lockres` and Phase 3's `setup_clone`; it is enforced by `resolve_lock` being typed `-> LockResolution` with exactly the three variants and `setup_clone` pattern-matching on all three. `--local --shared` shares the parent's object store via alternates (fast, low-disk), `--no-hardlinks` keeps the clone fully mutable without affecting the parent. **Parent-repo GC protection (resolves R48 W4 — shared-alternates vs git gc race)**: because the clone's `.git/objects/info/alternates` points at the parent repo's object store, any `git gc` / `git prune` / `git repack -a -d` invocation against the parent repo during an in-flight benchmark run could reap objects still referenced only from the clone, causing "missing object" errors on `git diff` / `git rev-parse` in `finalize_run`. Two defensive layers guard against this: **(1)** `setup_clone` writes a **keepalive ref** into the parent repo at `refs/keep/bench-<run_id>` pointing at `pre_run_commit_sha` immediately after the clone is created (single `git -C <PARENT_REPO> update-ref refs/keep/bench-<run_id> <pre_run_commit_sha>` call, wrapped in the same clone-setup transaction). This keepalive ref is visible to the parent's gc as a live ref, so the entire commit graph reachable from `pre_run_commit_sha` — which includes every object the clone might reference — is pinned against reaping for the duration of the run. The ref is removed by `teardown_clone` via `git -C <PARENT_REPO> update-ref -d refs/keep/bench-<run_id>` AFTER the `refs/heads/bench/<run_id>` anchor ref is written (so the authoritative anchor takes over the pin before the keepalive goes away — the two refs' lifetimes overlap by design). **(2)** `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh` additionally sets `git -C <PARENT_REPO> config gc.auto 0` and `git -C <PARENT_REPO> config gc.autoPackLimit 0` at benchmark-session start, and restores the prior values at session end via a session-scoped config backup file `.buildrunner/benchmarks/.git-gc-config-backup.json` (written at session-start with the pre-session values, read at session-end; if the backup is missing — e.g. the harness was killed before session-start completed — the restore path re-reads the current config as a best-effort reset). **Orphan-gc.auto recovery (resolves R50 W2)**: because a kill between the session-start config write and the session-end restore would leave the parent repo with `gc.auto=0` permanently (silently disabling automatic git garbage collection for BuildRunner3 until manually restored), **every `br benchmark` CLI entry point runs an orphan-recovery check at startup**: `deps.execution_preflight()` / `deps.offline_preflight()` / `deps.scoring_preflight()` / `deps.analysis_preflight()` / `deps.select_preflight()` each call a shared `deps._recover_orphaned_gc_config()` helper that (i) checks whether `.buildrunner/benchmarks/.git-gc-config-backup.json` exists AND the current session's session*id does NOT match the backup's `owning_session_id` field (stored alongside the pre-session values at backup time) — a mismatch means the backup belongs to a prior killed session, not the running one; (ii) checks whether `git -C <PARENT_REPO> config gc.auto` currently returns `0` (matching the disabled state the killed session set); (iii) if BOTH conditions hold, restores the backup's pre-session values via `git -C <PARENT_REPO> config gc.auto <prior>` + `git -C <PARENT_REPO> config gc.autoPackLimit <prior>`, deletes the stale backup file, and logs a warning `"recovered orphaned gc.auto config from killed session <owning_session_id>"` to stderr. If `(i)` fails (no backup file, OR backup's session matches the current session which means this is a legitimate in-progress session continuing across a resume), the helper is a no-op. **The preflight also handles the symmetric case where a restore succeeded but a later kill still left `gc.auto=0`**: the helper additionally checks `git -C <PARENT_REPO> config gc.auto` against a hardcoded-default expectation — if the value is exactly `0` AND no backup file exists AND no live session lock file (`/tmp/br3-bench-session-<session_id>.lock`) is held by a running pid, the helper unsets `gc.auto` entirely (`git -C <PARENT_REPO> config --unset gc.auto`) which reverts to git's own default behavior (typically re-enabled). This second path is gated behind an explicit `BR3_BENCH_FORCE_RESTORE_GC_AUTO=1` env var so a legitimate operator who intentionally set `gc.auto=0` on their BuildRunner3 checkout is not silently overridden. Unit test `test_deps.py::test_recover_orphaned_gc_config_restores_from_backup` seeds a stale backup file with a different session*id + `gc.auto=0` in the current config, runs the recovery helper, and asserts `gc.auto` is restored to the backup's prior value and the backup file is deleted. Unit test `test_deps.py::test_recover_orphaned_gc_config_noop_during_live_session` seeds a backup whose owning*session_id matches the running session_id and asserts the helper does not touch the config. Unit test `test_deps.py::test_recover_orphaned_gc_config_skips_without_env_flag_for_bare_zero` seeds `gc.auto=0` with no backup and asserts the helper does not unset it unless `BR3_BENCH_FORCE_RESTORE_GC_AUTO=1` is set. This prevents both automatic background gc and auto-pack from firing against the parent repo during the benchmark window, independently of how many clone-derived keepalive refs exist. **(3)** `setup_clone` also disables gc on the clone itself (`git -C /tmp/br3-bench-<run_id>/ config gc.auto 0`) so the clone's own 6-hour-plus lifetime never triggers its own gc that could race with a still-in-flight dispatcher subprocess. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_setup_clone_writes_keepalive_ref` asserts `refs/keep/bench-<run_id>` exists in the parent repo after `setup_clone` returns, pointing at `pre_run_commit_sha`; `test_teardown_clone_removes_keepalive_ref` asserts the ref is removed only AFTER the anchor ref `refs/heads/bench/<run_id>` is written (anchor-before-keepalive-delete ordering); `test_install_benchmark_deps_disables_parent_gc` asserts `gc.auto == "0"` after session start and restores the prior value after session end. The clone has a real `.git` **directory** (line-48 compliant). `bench-src-<run_id>` is the clone's `ORIGINAL_BRANCH` — the name the dispatcher's `git branch --show-current` will report when invoked with `PROJECT_PATH=/tmp/br3-bench-<run_id>/`. The handle records: `{clone_path: "/tmp/br3-bench-<run_id>/", src_branch: "bench-src-<run_id>", pre_run_commit_sha: str, pre_run_test_surfaces: {python: bool, ui: bool}}`. `pre_run_test_surfaces` is computed immediately after checkout: `python = (<clone_path>/tests/).exists() and any((<clone_path>/tests/).rglob("test**.py"))`(resolves R51 B2 — pytest's default discovery pattern is`test**.py`with the underscore AFTER`test`; the earlier `test**.py`glob matched only files ending in`*.py`like`testfoo\_.py`and missed normal pytest filenames like`test*models.py`, silently misclassifying every existing Python test surface as absent and opening the test-surface-deletion guard to a free-pass bypass); `ui = (<clone_path>/ui/package.json).exists() and \_safe_parse_package_json(<clone_path>/ui/package.json).get("scripts",{}).get("test") is not None`(resolves R51 B3 —`json.loads`on a contestant-produced malformed`package.json`would raise`json.JSONDecodeError`and crash the scorer before a verdict could be recorded;`\_safe_parse_package_json(path: Path) -> dict`is a shared helper exported from Phase 1's `core/benchmark/deps.py`(resolves R52 B3 — helper relocated from Phase 5's`toolchain.py`to Phase 1's`deps.py`so Phase 3's`setup_clone`has a legitimate import target under the declared build order`1 → 2 → 4 → 3 → 5` — Phase 3 previously depended on a file Phase 5 had not yet created) that wraps`json.loads(path.read_text())`in a`try/except json.JSONDecodeError`and returns`{"**malformed**": True, "**error**": str(e), "**path**": str(path)}`on any decode failure.`pre_run_test_surfaces[ui]`evaluates to`False`when the sentinel is present, and the scorer treats a post-run malformed`package.json`as a scored`install_failed`outcome per the Phase 5 malformed-JSON handler — never an uncaught exception). This is the reference state the scorer compares against at run-complete time to detect surface deletion (Phase 5's test-surface deletion guard). **Owner file for gc-anchors detection (resolves R47 B1 — contestant diff contamination)**: immediately after the clone + checkout,`setup_clone`writes the owner file to a **sibling path OUTSIDE the clone** —`/tmp/br3-bench-<run_id>.owner`(note the lack of trailing`/` — the file sits next to the clone directory, not inside it). The file contains the orchestrator's current pid (`str(os.getpid())`) and `created_at_utc`. Writing OUTSIDE the clone is mandatory because the verified dispatcher flow runs `git add -A`inside the clone to capture the contestant's changes; an owner file inside the clone would be staged and contaminate the scored diff (Phase 5's adherence metrics and Phase 7's regression would silently include the`.buildrunner-owner`delta as if it were contestant work).`br benchmark gc-anchors`reads`/tmp/br3-bench-*.owner`(glob-matches the sibling path) to decide whether the clone dir is orphaned — if the pid is no longer running AND the clone dir is >6 hours old, both the clone dir and its sibling owner file are swept.`teardown_clone`explicitly removes`/tmp/br3-bench-<run_id>.owner`via`os.unlink(..., missing_ok=True)`alongside the`rm -rf`of the clone directory (the owner file is no longer inside the clone so`rm -rf`on the clone dir does not remove it — teardown must take the explicit second step). Unit test`test_runner.py::test_setup_clone_writes_owner_outside_clone`asserts`.buildrunner-owner`does NOT exist inside`/tmp/br3-bench-<run_id>/`after`setup_clone`returns, AND that`/tmp/br3-bench-<run_id>.owner`(sibling path) DOES exist. Unit test`test_runner.py::test_dispatch_commit_does_not_contain_owner_file`runs a synthetic contestant dispatch, invokes the dispatcher's`git add -A + commit`path against the clone, and asserts the resulting commit's file list does not contain`.buildrunner-owner`.
- [ ] `dispatch_run(runtime, node, prompt_text, handle)` invokes `dispatch-to-node.sh` with `PROJECT_PATH=handle.clone_path`, `SESSION_NAME=bench-dispatch-<run_id>` (unique, won't collide with `bench-src-<run_id>`). The dispatcher creates its internal `.dispatch-worktrees/bench-dispatch-<run_id>/` _inside the clone_ (which is fine — the clone's `.git` is a directory, and the internal worktree's inner `.git` file lives one level deeper and never gets passed back into the dispatcher itself). The dispatcher then: branches from the clone's HEAD (== pre*run_commit_sha via the prior checkout), rsyncs to remote, runs contestant, rsyncs back, commits on `bench-dispatch-<run_id>`, **ff-merges `bench-dispatch-<run_id>` into the clone's current branch `bench-src-<run_id>`**, and deletes `bench-dispatch-<run_id>`. Net effect: the contestant's commit lands on `bench-src-<run_id>` inside the clone. Exit codes (**verified empirically against `~/.buildrunner/scripts/dispatch-to-node.sh` on 2026-04-16** — exact locations annotated so the mapping is auditable): `1`=node-offline (line 96: `check_node_health` failure), `2`=usage/validation/dispatch-lock/runtime-nonzero (lines 45/50/66/72/82/462: missing args, non-git path, unsupported runtime, concurrent dispatch lock held, or runtime subprocess exit ≠ 0), `3`=build-spec-sync-failed (lines 290/336: rsync or BUILD spec missing after sync), `4`=rate-limited (line 456: regex match on rate-limit pattern in remote stderr), `5`=retry-also-failed-or-no-changes-after-retry (lines 520/533: the dispatcher's one-shot retry path gave up), `6`=runtime-preflight-failed (line 140: codex preflight failed on remote node). All six are classified as `dispatch_failed` by `runner.dispatch_run`, **but remediation IS discriminated by sub-code AND, for exit 2, by a secondary signal (resolves R30 W7 + R31 B7 — exit 2 is overloaded inside `dispatch-to-node.sh`: lines 45/50/66/72/82 are pre-SSH local-validation failures, while line 462 is contestant-runtime-nonzero after rsync-back; these two sub-cases require opposite handling)**: exit codes `{1, 3, 4, 5, 6}` are **retryable** (transient: node offline, rsync failed, rate-limited, retry-also-failed, runtime preflight failed — all legitimately fixable by trying a different node or after a backoff). Exit code `{2}` is **sub-classified by the runner via a `_classify_exit2(handle, stderr) -> Literal["validation_terminal","runtime_nonzero_scored"]` helper** that applies two signals in order: (a) **git-state signal (primary)** — immediately after dispatch, the runner reads `post_run_commit_sha = git -C <clone_path> rev-parse refs/heads/bench-src-<run_id>` (or the dispatcher's internal worktree HEAD); if `post_run_commit_sha != pre_run_commit_sha` OR the dispatcher's internal `.dispatch-worktrees/bench-dispatch-<run_id>/` directory exists and contains any commit newer than the pre-run SHA, the runtime actually ran on the remote node (even though it errored at the end) and the outcome is `runtime_nonzero_scored`; (b) **stderr-pattern signal (fallback when no commit landed)** — `_classify_exit2` matches the dispatcher's stderr against the union regex `(Usage: dispatch-to-node\.sh|PROJECT_PATH must be a git repo|Unsupported runtime|dispatch lock held|missing required argument)` which covers the five local-validation exit paths on lines 45/50/66/72/82; a match returns `validation_terminal`, a non-match (stderr has runtime output but no validation marker) defaults conservatively to `runtime_nonzero_scored` since the dispatcher got far enough to run remote code. **`validation_terminal`** → `SkippedRow{reason="dispatch_terminal_exit2_validation"}`, no retry, phase continues with other cells (same as before). **`runtime_nonzero_scored`** → treated as a legitimate failed scored run: `finalize_run` still executes, `post_run_commit_sha` is captured (even if it equals pre-run SHA when the contestant errored before committing), and the scorer emits an `ObjectiveMetrics` with `local_test_result.combined_status="fail"` and `run_result.exit_code=2`; the cell's `CompletedRow{stage="run"}` is appended and scoring proceeds. **No-op vs runtime-failure discriminator (resolves R49 W6 — exit-2 runtime failure with no commit must be distinguishable from a legitimate `no_changes=True` zero-adherence no-op, which is structurally identical in `post_run_commit_sha == pre_run_commit_sha` + empty-diff terms)**: `RunResult` carries two mutually-exclusive discriminator fields pre-declared in Phase 1's `models.py`: (i) **`no_changes: bool`** — set to `True` **only** when `run_result.exit_code == 0 AND post_run_commit_sha == pre_run_commit_sha` (the contestant's process exited cleanly without committing anything, which is the legitimate zero-adherence choice the benchmark measures); in all other combinations `no_changes` is `False`. (ii) **`runtime_failure_no_commit: bool`** — set to `True` **only** when `run_result.exit_code != 0 AND post_run_commit_sha == pre_run_commit_sha` (the contestant's process errored before committing, which is a hard runtime failure NOT a legitimate no-op); in all other combinations this field is `False`. The two fields are mutually exclusive by construction — no `RunResult` ever carries both `True`, and `finalize_run` asserts this invariant before appending the `CompletedRow{stage="run"}`. **Phase 7 aggregator treatment**: `no_changes=True` rows enter the primary adherence analysis as zero-adherence observations (the contestant chose to not act; this is a valid and measurable choice). `runtime_failure_no_commit=True` rows are **excluded from the adherence point estimate** and enter a separate failure-rate covariate that Phase 7's regression models explicitly — they count toward the per-model failure rate but do not pull the adherence mean down to zero (which would conflate "chose not to act" with "could not finish"). Phase 8's report surfaces the failure rate alongside the adherence rate in separate panels, and the caveats section explicitly calls out the count of `runtime_failure_no_commit` rows per model per phase. **Conservative-default auditability**: when `_classify_exit2` falls through to the conservative `runtime_nonzero_scored` default (exit 2, no commit, stderr does NOT match any validation regex), the `CompletedRow{stage="run"}` additionally carries `exit2_classification_reason: Literal["post_run_commit_present","stderr_validation_marker_matched","conservative_default_no_commit_no_marker"]` — set to `"conservative_default_no_commit_no_marker"` for the ambiguous path. This makes the fallback traceable in the registry so an operator can post-hoc audit which runs hit the conservative default vs which had explicit evidence; Phase 7's regression can model this field as a covariate to test whether the conservative-default runs behave differently from explicitly-evidenced runtime-failure runs. **The combination of `runtime_failure_no_commit=True` + `exit2_classification_reason="conservative_default_no_commit_no_marker"` on the same row is the canonical "ambiguous exit-2" case**: it is scored as a runtime failure (not a no-op), its empty diff is expected and correct (no contestant work landed), and it enters Phase 7 as a failure-rate observation with an explicit audit flag. This closes the R31 B7 hole where contestants whose own code errored out at the runtime level would otherwise be silently dropped via a skipped row instead of recorded as a failed outcome AND closes the R49 W6 hole where such rows would be conflated with legitimate zero-adherence no-ops in the adherence point estimate. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_dispatch_exit_code_classification` seeds the four scenarios: exit 2 + no post-run commit + stderr matches validation regex → `validation_terminal`; exit 2 + post-run commit present → `runtime_nonzero_scored` with `runtime_failure_no_commit=False` (commit exists); exit 2 + no commit + stderr lacks validation marker → `runtime_nonzero_scored` with `runtime_failure_no_commit=True` AND `exit2_classification_reason="conservative_default_no_commit_no_marker"` (conservative default); exits 1/3/4/5/6 → one retry-on-different-node before abandoning. Companion unit test `test_runner.py::test_no_changes_vs_runtime_failure_mutual_exclusion` asserts that across a synthetic battery of (exit_code, commit_present) combinations, `no_changes` and `runtime_failure_no_commit` are never both `True` on the same `RunResult`. Companion unit test `test_aggregator.py::test_runtime_failure_no_commit_excluded_from_adherence_mean` seeds a registry with one legitimate `no_changes=True` row (exit_code=0, adherence=0) and one `runtime_failure_no_commit=True` row (exit_code=2, adherence undefined/excluded), and asserts the aggregator's adherence mean is 0.0 (one zero-adherence observation, the runtime-failure row excluded) and the aggregator's failure-rate count is 1. **Preflight pin (see next deliverable)**: `deps.py` also greps the dispatcher for the line-48 `.git`-directory check and the ff-merge-then-delete flow, so any future dispatcher rewrite that changes this exit-code mapping or those flows fails preflight before the benchmark runs. **Recovery policy** (distinct from Invariant 16, which governs paraphrase/equivalence failures only): for the **retryable** exit codes `{1, 3, 4, 5, 6}` only (exit 2 short-circuits per above and never enters this path), the cell retries once with a new `run_id` on a **different node when one exists**; when `preflight_single_node=true` (the pool has collapsed to one node), the retry runs on the **same node** after a 60-second jittered backoff rather than aborting — single-node retries are legitimate because most retryable failure classes (exit 1=offline, 3=sync-failed, 4=rate-limited) are transient on the node itself. On a second consecutive dispatch failure for the same `(phase_id, model, sub_study, replication_index)` cell (regardless of whether the retry was same-node or other-node), the run is marked `dispatch_abandoned` via a `SkippedRow` with `reason="dispatch_abandoned"` but the **phase is not dropped** — the phase continues with any other cells that succeed, and the Phase 7 aggregator's "partial-completion exclusion rule" (Phase 7 deliverable) then decides whether the phase's partially-complete cells enter primary analysis (they do not — partial phases are moved to the sensitivity branch). Dispatch failure is therefore an orthogonal recovery path from Invariant 16's whole-phase drop; both are documented in `runner.py` module docstring. **Temporal precedence (resolves R24 W0 + R37 B2 — paraphrase is a PHASE-LEVEL step, NOT a per-cell step)**: Invariant 16 fires **before** `dispatch_run` can run for a given phase. **Paraphrase + equivalence check runs exactly once per phase across the entire 2-models × N-sub-studies × R-replications cell matrix (2×2×3 = 12 cells per phase with canonical defaults)**, not once per cell. The single paraphrased prompt produced by that first invocation is **cached on `session_state.selector_cache[phase_id].paraphrased_prompt_native`** and **`session_state.selector_cache[phase_id].paraphrased_prompt_neutral`** (two sub-study-specific prompts per phase; fields pre-declared on the `PhaseSpec` pydantic model in Phase 1's `models.py` alongside the existing `checklist_items`/`layer`/`declared_files` fields so no later phase adds schema fields — declared as `paraphrased_prompt_native: Optional[str] = None` and `paraphrased_prompt_neutral: Optional[str] = None`, populated by the first `run_cell` for a phase to attempt paraphrase, read by every subsequent `run_cell` for the same phase). The flow at the top of `runner.run_cell(phase, model, sub_study, replication_index)`: `(1) registry.is_phase_dropped(phase.phase_id) → early-skip via SkippedRow; (2) if phase.paraphrased_prompt*<sub*study> is None: → acquire the phase-scoped paraphrase lock /tmp/br3-bench-paraphrase-<phase_id>.lock (fcntl.flock LOCK_EX) → RE-READ phase from selector_cache to pick up any concurrent writer's result → if still None: paraphraser.paraphrase_spec(phase, sub_study) → may call selector.redraw(phase_id, reason="paraphrase_failed") + return None → equivalence.check_equivalence(original_spec, paraphrased_prompt) → may call selector.redraw(phase_id, reason="equivalence_failed") + return False → on success, write paraphrased_prompt*<sub*study> onto the cached PhaseSpec in selector_cache via selector.set_paraphrase(phase_id, sub_study, prompt) → release lock; (3) proceed with the cached paraphrased_prompt*<sub_study>; (4) setup_clone → dispatch_run → [retry-once on other/same node] → finalize_run → scorer → teardown_clone`. **Concurrency contract**: the phase-scoped flock guarantees that even when multiple `run_cell`invocations for different`(model, sub_study, replication)`cells of the same phase fire concurrently (up to 12 parallel cells per phase), exactly ONE paraphrase call hits the paraphraser API per`(phase_id, sub_study)`pair (2 API calls total per phase). The double-check-after-lock pattern prevents the classic races where thread A checks None, thread B also checks None before A takes the lock, A takes the lock and computes, releases, and B then re-computes — the re-read inside the lock catches A's result. **Crash resilience**:`selector.set_paraphrase`writes to`session_state.selector_cache`atomically via`tmp+fsync+rename` on every call, so a kill mid-paraphrase resumes from the cached value (if present) or re-runs paraphrase (if not). **`selector.set_paraphrase(phase_id: str, sub_study: Literal["native","neutral"], prompt: str) -> None`** is a new Phase 2 selector method (single-writer = Phase 2's selector, added to Phase 2's file list's selector API surface declared alongside `redraw`/`selected_phase_ids`/`get_phase`). On paraphrase failure, `selector.redraw(phase_id, reason)`drops the phase per Invariant 16 — the drop is still at phase granularity (both models × both sub-studies × all replications abandoned together), matching Invariant 16's cell-balance preservation. The`dispatch_run`retry policy therefore only applies to cells whose phase **survived** the paraphrase/equivalence gate; there is no scenario where both policies fire on the same cell. Unit test`test_runner.py::test_paraphrase_runs_once_per_phase_sub_study`seeds two concurrent`run_cell`invocations against the same`(phase_id, sub_study)`(different models/replications), mocks the paraphraser, and asserts`paraphraser.paraphrase_spec`is called exactly ONCE;`test_paraphrase_cached_across_cells`asserts the second and later`run_cell`s for the same `(phase_id, sub_study)`read from`selector_cache` without calling the paraphraser.
- [ ] **`dispatch-to-node.sh` preflight for the benchmark entry point**: before `br benchmark run` starts dispatching, `deps.py` asserts the two behaviors the harness depends on by reading the live script from `~/.buildrunner/scripts/dispatch-to-node.sh`. **Regex tolerance (resolves R31 W3 — literal grep patterns are fragile to quoting/whitespace edits that preserve behavior)**: each check uses an **extended-regex match** with explicit whitespace tolerance and quote-style alternation rather than a literal string: (a) check the `.git`-directory guard via `grep -Eq '^[[:space:]]*if[[:space:]]+\[[[:space:]]+!([[:space:]]+-d)[[:space:]]+"?\$\{?PROJECT_PATH\}?/.git"?[[:space:]]+\][[:space:]]+;?[[:space:]]*then' ~/.buildrunner/scripts/dispatch-to-node.sh` — matches the guard regardless of `"$PROJECT_PATH"`-vs-`"${PROJECT_PATH}"` quoting, extra whitespace, trailing semicolons, or a `then` on the same line vs next line; (b) check the ff-merge-then-delete flow via two regexes — `grep -Eq 'git[[:space:]]+merge[[:space:]]+--ff-only[[:space:]]+"?\$\{?SESSION_NAME\}?"?' ~/.buildrunner/scripts/dispatch-to-node.sh` AND `grep -Eq 'git[[:space:]]+branch[[:space:]]+-d[[:space:]]+"?\$\{?SESSION_NAME\}?"?' ~/.buildrunner/scripts/dispatch-to-node.sh` — same whitespace + brace-quoting tolerance. If the regex library or the shell's `grep -E` is unavailable, `deps.py` falls back to a Python `re.search()` with the same patterns (bypassing grep entirely). The preflight prints the matched line for each check so an operator can inspect which exact line the assertion latched onto, and if a future dispatcher rewrite changes the variable name (e.g. `PROJECT_PATH` → `PROJ_PATH`) the check fails with a remediation message that names both the expected regex and the actual file lines around the failed match, so the fix is obvious. If either check fails, preflight exits with a remediation message naming the missing line pattern; the benchmark refuses to run against an unexpected dispatcher contract.
- [ ] `finalize_run(handle) -> FinalizedRun`: reads `post_run_commit_sha = git -C <clone_path> rev-parse refs/heads/bench-src-<run_id>`. If `post_run_commit_sha == pre_run_commit_sha`, the contestant produced no commit; the `RunResult` is flagged using the **two mutually-exclusive discriminator fields** declared above (resolves R49 W6): `no_changes=True` **iff** `run_result.exit_code == 0` (legitimate zero-adherence no-op — the contestant's process exited cleanly without committing anything); `runtime_failure_no_commit=True` **iff** `run_result.exit_code != 0` (runtime failure — the contestant's process errored before committing). `finalize_run` asserts the mutual-exclusion invariant (`not (no_changes and runtime_failure_no_commit)`) before returning the `FinalizedRun`. The two states are scored differently in Phase 7 per the aggregator treatment above: `no_changes=True` enters the primary adherence analysis as a zero-adherence observation; `runtime_failure_no_commit=True` is excluded from the adherence point estimate and enters the per-model failure-rate covariate instead. Then **transfer the commit and its objects into the parent repo as a durable anchor**: `git -C <parent_repo> fetch --quiet "/tmp/br3-bench-<run_id>/" "refs/heads/bench-src-<run_id>:refs/heads/bench/<run_id>"`. The `git fetch` from a local path copies required objects (the parent's alternates-shared objects are already present; only the contestant's new commit + tree + blobs cross over). After the fetch, the parent has an independent `refs/heads/bench/<run_id>` ref pointing at the contestant's post-run SHA; the clone can be deleted without losing anything. Captures the diff via `git -C <parent_repo> diff <pre_run_commit_sha>..refs/heads/bench/<run_id>` and the per-file list via `--name-status` for the scorer. **No separate finalize-commit step is performed** — the dispatcher already committed.
- [ ] **GPG-signing risk on dispatch-to-node.sh's remote commit (resolves R35 W2 — preflight must verify a _usable key_ exists, not just that the config flag is set)**: the runtime on the remote node executes `git add -A && git commit -m 'feat: dispatched phase work'`, which will fail if the remote node has `commit.gpgsign=true` and no usable key for the signing identity. The dispatcher also runs a local-side commit at line ~598 with the same default git config. `deps.probe_node_pool()` augments its node readiness check with a **two-step SSH probe per candidate node**: (i) `ssh <node> 'git config --global --get commit.gpgsign || echo false'` — reads the signing flag; (ii) **only if step (i) returns `true`**, `ssh <node> 'git config --global --get user.signingkey || echo none; gpg --list-secret-keys --with-colons 2>/dev/null'` — reads the configured signing key id AND lists the remote node's available secret keys. The Python-side check parses the `gpg --list-secret-keys --with-colons` output for lines starting with `sec:` (a usable secret key record) and, **if a `user.signingkey` fingerprint is explicitly configured**, additionally asserts that fingerprint appears in the `fpr:` sub-records of the returned block (so a configured-but-missing key is caught). The node passes the preflight only when `commit.gpgsign=false` OR (`commit.gpgsign=true` AND at least one `sec:` line exists AND, if `user.signingkey` is set, its fingerprint is present in `fpr:`). On failure the node is rejected from the pool with a remediation message naming the three possible fixes: (a) `git config --global commit.gpgsign false` on the node for the benchmark account, (b) install a signing key via `gpg --gen-key` + `git config --global user.signingkey <fpr>`, or (c) unset the stale `user.signingkey` that points to a deleted key. **Local (Muddy) check mirrors the remote logic exactly**: `deps.py` runs the same three commands locally (`git config --get commit.gpgsign`, `git config --get user.signingkey`, `gpg --list-secret-keys --with-colons`) and applies the same pass/fail rule; the harness refuses to start if Muddy itself has `commit.gpgsign=true` without a usable key. One-time ops fix, documented in `api_contracts.md`. Unit test `test_deps.py::test_gpg_preflight_requires_usable_key` mocks the three subprocess calls across the scenarios (gpgsign-false → pass, gpgsign-true+sec-present → pass, gpgsign-true+no-sec → fail, gpgsign-true+signingkey-missing-from-fpr → fail) and asserts the correct pass/fail verdict.
- [ ] `teardown_clone(handle)`: `rm -rf /tmp/br3-bench-<run_id>/`. **Call-order invariant and Phase 5 dependency-injection contract (resolves the "Phase 3 calls Phase 5 symbol" ordering concern)**: Phase 3 defines a `ScorerProtocol` (typing.Protocol with a single method `score_run(handle: CloneHandle, phase: PhaseSpec, run_result: RunResult, runner: "Runner") -> tuple[ObjectiveMetrics, AdherenceMetrics]` — **resolves R40 B2** — the fourth positional `runner` argument is the Runner instance that invoked the scorer, passed as `self` from `Runner.run_cell`; Phase 5's `BenchmarkScorer.score_run` consumes the runner reference when forwarding into `toolchain.run_local_tests(handle, runner)` so the toolchain module's declared helper dispatches (`runner._detect_baseline_drift`, `runner._acquire_venv_lock`, etc.) are satisfied without any module-level lookup. The protocol signature is byte-for-byte identical to the Phase 5 `BenchmarkScorer` class method so Phase 5's wire-in is pure duck-typed subclassing) and `runner.run_cell(...)` accepts `scorer: Optional[ScorerProtocol] = None` as a constructor-injected dependency. When `scorer is None` (Phase 3 landed alone, Phase 5 not yet implemented), the clone is torn down immediately after `finalize_run`; scoring is deferred to the offline `br benchmark score --run-id <id>` command, which re-materializes the tree from `refs/heads/bench/<run_id>` via `git worktree add /tmp/br3-bench-rescore-<run_id>`. When `scorer is not None` (Phase 5 has landed and wired in — see Phase 5 deliverable "wire scorer into runner.run_cell"), `run_cell` orders per-run operations as `setup_clone → dispatch_run → finalize_run → scorer.score_run(handle, phase, run_result, self) → teardown_clone` (the `self` argument is the Runner instance, supplying the helper dispatches `BenchmarkScorer` forwards into `toolchain.run_local_tests(handle, runner)` — **resolves R40 B2**). The scorer call is inside a `try` block; `teardown_clone` is called in `finally`. This means Phase 3's tests pass **without** Phase 5 existing (the `scorer=None` path is the default tested in `test_runner.py`), and Phase 5's integration is a pure-additive wiring step — no Phase 3 symbol depends on a Phase 5 symbol at import time or at test time. The contestant's commit survives in the parent via the `refs/heads/bench/<run_id>` anchor fetched in `finalize_run`, so any later re-scoring (Phase 5's `score --run-id <id>` re-materialization path) can reconstitute a scratch tree without the clone. `dispatch-to-node.sh`'s internal cleanup (auto-merge + `git branch -d bench-dispatch-<run_id>` + internal worktree remove) already ran before we got here and affected only the clone's state — those ops are immaterial once the clone is deleted. Anchor branches in the parent are cleaned up by the `br benchmark gc-anchors` subcommand (registered in Phase 1's CLI skeleton, implementation in Phase 3's `runner.py`). **`gc-anchors` scope (explicit list, so post-run disk accumulation never silently grows)**: the subcommand sweeps five classes of filesystem state created by the harness — (a) `refs/heads/bench/<run_id>` refs older than `--keep-days` (default 30); (b) **orphaned clones** at `/tmp/br3-bench-*/` not referenced by any live orchestrator (detected by listing `/tmp/br3-bench-*.owner` sibling files — the owner files live **outside** the clone per the R47 B1 fix — and filtering against the pid recorded in each `.owner` file that `setup_clone` writes at creation; stale owners whose pid is no longer running are swept, and the corresponding clone directory AND its sibling `.owner` file are both removed; a 6-hour minimum age prevents races with in-flight runs); (c) **orphaned rescore worktrees** at `/tmp/br3-bench-rescore-*/` over 6 hours old; (d) **audit prompt files** at `.buildrunner/benchmarks/prompts/*.txt` older than `--keep-days` — an operator-tunable retention because the corpus reaches ~18 MB at 360 runs × 50 KB (acceptable but unbounded without a sweep); (e) **orphaned keepalive refs** at `refs/keep/bench-*` in the parent repo older than `--keep-days` (**resolves R50 W1** — `setup_clone` writes `refs/keep/bench-<run_id>` to pin the parent's object store against gc during an in-flight run, and `teardown_clone` removes it after the anchor ref lands. If the process is killed between `setup_clone` and `teardown_clone`, the keepalive ref persists indefinitely and silently prevents parent-repo gc from running on the entire reachable graph — which over many killed-session cycles can retain multi-GB of contestant churn. `gc-anchors` sweeps every `refs/keep/bench-<run_id>` whose commit-time is older than `--keep-days` using `git -C <PARENT_REPO> for-each-ref --format='%(refname) %(committerdate:unix)' refs/keep/bench-` + age comparison + `git -C <PARENT_REPO> update-ref -d <refname>`. The sweep logs the count of reaped refs and the total object-reachability freed (estimated via `git count-objects -v` before/after) so operators can verify disk was returned. The anchor ref `refs/heads/bench/<run_id>` covers the same object-reachability pin for completed runs, so sweeping the orphaned keepalive refs is safe: any run that reached `finalize_run` already has its anchor, and any run that did not reach `finalize_run` has no useful scoring data to preserve anyway); **(f) preview session-state rows (resolves R52 W2 — Phase 2 declares that `br benchmark select` writes `SessionState{is_preview: True, ...}` rows that are swept after 48 hours of inactivity, and the `--prune-sessions` flag on `gc-anchors` additionally prunes ALL session-state files (preview and non-preview) older than 30 days. Earlier drafts did not enumerate the 48-hour preview sweep as a scheduled class under `gc-anchors`, leaving Phase 2's retention contract without an owner in Phase 3's cleanup surface. The corrected scope is two distinct sweeps: a SHORT-retention sweep for preview sessions (48 hours) and a LONG-retention sweep for all sessions via `--prune-sessions` (30 days). Both sweeps live under `gc-anchors`)**: the subcommand reads every `.buildrunner/benchmarks/sessions/<session_id>.json` file, parses the JSON, and for each row where `is_preview == True`, compares `max(session_state.created_at_utc, session_state.last_updated_utc)` against `now() - timedelta(hours=48)`. Every preview row older than 48 hours is deleted (the file removed and any sibling transient artifacts at `.buildrunner/benchmarks/previews/<session_id>/` recursively removed). The `--prune-sessions` flag (default `False`) additionally sweeps ALL session-state rows (both `is_preview=True` and `is_preview=False`) whose age exceeds 30 days, using the same mtime comparison path. The two sweeps are ordered: (f) fires first against preview rows, then `--prune-sessions` (if set) against the full set. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_gc_anchors_sweeps_48h_preview_sessions` seeds two preview session files — one 49 hours old, one 1 hour old — and a 45-day-old non-preview session file, then runs `gc-anchors` WITHOUT `--prune-sessions` and asserts (a) the 49-hour-old preview is removed, (b) the 1-hour-old preview is preserved, (c) the 45-day-old non-preview session is preserved (since `--prune-sessions` was not set). Companion test `test_gc_anchors_prune_sessions_sweeps_all_over_30_days` runs the same seed with `--prune-sessions` and asserts the 45-day-old non-preview session IS removed. `--reset-venv` (Phase 5 extension) is orthogonal; it operates on `.venv-benchmark/` regardless of the other classes. All five classes are swept under `fcntl.flock("/tmp/br3-bench-gc.lock")` to prevent two concurrent gc invocations from racing on the same refs/dirs. Unit test in `test_runner.py::test_gc_anchors` seeds one of each class (with synthetic owner pid / mtime / ref committerdate) and asserts the sweep removes exactly the expected set.
- [ ] `NodeAllocator.assign(phase, model, replication, sub_study)` returns a node such that, within each phase, Codex and Claude each run on Otis and Lomax the same number of times. Seed is deterministic per-phase for reproducibility.
- [ ] `dispatch_run` argv contract — **verified invocation that matches the global `dispatch-to-node.sh` CLI exactly**: `argv = ["/Users/byronhudson/.buildrunner/scripts/dispatch-to-node.sh", "--runtime", runtime, node, handle.clone_path, prompt_text, "bench-dispatch-<run_id>"]`, invoked via `subprocess.Popen(argv, shell=False, cwd=handle.clone_path, ...)`. The prompt is passed as the positional `<prompt>` argument (argv[5]); the explicit SESSION_NAME at argv[6] pins the dispatcher's session branch to `bench-dispatch-<run_id>` so we never collide with `bench-src-<run_id>`. Because `shell=False`, no local shell parsing or substitution occurs. **Remote-path size budget (SSH command-line)**: `dispatch-to-node.sh` embeds `$PROMPT` into a remote SSH command that runs a quoted heredoc on the target node. SSH's practical command-line ceiling is ~128 KiB before hitting OpenSSH `ARG_MAX` on the remote side; benchmark prompts are expected ≤50 KB and are rejected with `prompt_too_large` if they exceed **100 KB** (a conservative ceiling well below the verified SSH limit). The local argv limit (~1 MiB on macOS) is therefore never the binding constraint. **Heredoc-delimiter safety**: the global script embeds `$PROMPT` inside a quoted heredoc `<<'PROMPT_EOF'` on the remote node, so the only possible breakage would be a prompt line whose content is exactly `PROMPT_EOF`. `dispatch_run` pre-scans the prompt and rejects it with `prompt_heredoc_conflict` if any line equals `PROMPT_EOF`; it also rejects null bytes. These cases are vanishingly unlikely in practice but are caught and logged. The prompt is **also** written to `.buildrunner/benchmarks/prompts/{run_id}.txt` in the **parent repo**, explicitly **outside** the clone, as an audit trail (path recorded on the `RunResult` as `prompt_audit_path`). This placement is deliberate: the dispatcher's remote runtime runs `git add -A` in the rsynced tree, which would otherwise stage and commit the prompt file into the contestant's diff, contaminating the scored artifact with harness-generated content and revealing the paraphrased spec verbatim to the judge. Writing the prompt to the parent repo's `.buildrunner/benchmarks/prompts/` directory keeps it out of the clone's tree entirely. The `prompts/` directory is created idempotently in Phase 1's `deps.py` startup (alongside the other `.buildrunner/benchmarks/` subdirectories). The file is not consumed by the dispatcher; it exists purely for reproducibility and post-hoc inspection. No wrapper script is needed; no changes to the global dispatcher are needed.
- [ ] Environment allowlist: `PATH`, `HOME`, `USER`, `LOGNAME`, `SHELL`, `LANG`, `LC_ALL`, `TERM`, `SSH_AUTH_SOCK`, `SSH_KNOWN_HOSTS`. **Stripped (identity-revealing):** `BR3_RUNTIME`, `BR3_SHADOW_RUNTIME`, `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, `ANTHROPIC_*`, `OPENAI_API_KEY`, `OPENAI_*`, `CLAUDE_*`, `CODEX_*` — any env var whose presence would tell a contestant which model it is. The headless CLIs (`claude` / `codex`) read credentials from their **installed config files on the dispatch node** (e.g. `~/.anthropic/config.json` on the node) rather than from env, so no API key needs to reach the contestant's process environment. **Residual-inference caveat (W7, methods note)**: a sufficiently adversarial contestant could still infer which runtime it is by reading its own config files or binary paths (e.g. `$HOME/.anthropic` existing but `$HOME/.codex` empty); the harness does not — and cannot in the dispatch model — mask the node's own installed-runtime layout from a process that has read access to `$HOME`. This is a disclosed limitation (the recognition probe in Phase 4 measures it post-hoc and enters the score as a covariate, not a filter). No practical evidence suggests either contestant currently performs that inference; the harness assumes cooperative behavior on the contestant side and audits with the recognition-probe signal. `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` is only needed by the harness (paraphraser, judge, equivalence) and is stripped from the contestant env. The allowlist is documented at the top of `runner.py` and enforced by a unit test that asserts `ANTHROPIC_*` and `OPENAI_*` are absent from the Popen env.
- [ ] Token counts parsed per `TokenCounts.source` rules from Phase 1; if neither stdout JSON nor stderr usage line is present, `source="none"` and the run is flagged in `run_meta.json` but not excluded.
- [ ] Wall-clock, exit code, stdout, stderr, and resulting diff captured for every run.
- [ ] `replications: int` is a **config-loaded constant** read from `config.selector.replications` (Phase 1 `SelectorConfig`) by `runner.run_session(...)`; `run_session` iterates `replication_index ∈ range(replications)` and invokes the per-cell entry point **`runner.run_cell(phase, model, sub_study, replication_index: int)`** once per attempt (**resolves R53 W2 — the canonical `run_cell` signature takes a single `replication_index: int`, matching the `cell_key = (phase_id, model, sub_study, replication_index)` registry key and all downstream scheduler/aggregator references; an earlier draft mistakenly documented `run_cell(..., replications)` as if the per-cell entry point took the replication count rather than a single index, which would have broken the `cell_key` registry filter, the claim-lock dedup, and Phase 7's per-replication aggregation**). Each replication emits its own `RunResult` with `replication_index`, and each `CompletedRow` / `ClaimRow` / `HeartbeatRow` / `SupersededRow` / `SkippedRow` carries that same `replication_index` as a top-level column.
- [ ] Native sub-study loads the model's own skill preamble (`/codex` or `/opus`) symmetrically; neutral sub-study uses the shared minimal prompt.
- [ ] **Atomic write + resume (keyed on `cell_key`, not `run_id`, using a Phase-3-local reducer)**: each `CompletedRow` (progressive-fill; see Phase 1) is appended to `benchmark_registry.jsonl` via the `O_APPEND + fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX)` append-writer. `runner.resume()` **does not depend on Phase 7's aggregator** (Phase 7 lands after Phase 3 in the build order `1 → 2 → 4 → 3 → 5 → 6 → 7 → ...`). Instead Phase 3 defines a **lightweight inline cell_key dedup scan** in `runner.py` — `_reduce_registry_by_cell_key(registry_path) -> dict[cell_key, CellStatus]` where `CellStatus = Literal["terminal","in_flight","eligible"]`. The scan is a single-pass JSONL read under `fcntl.flock(LOCK_SH)` that groups rows by `cell_key = (phase_id, model, sub_study, replication_index)` and applies three rules in order: (1) if ANY `CompletedRow` for the cell has `stage in {"scored","judged"}` and no later `SupersededRow` references its `run_id`, the cell is `terminal` and is skipped on resume; (2) else if ANY live `ClaimRow`/`HeartbeatRow` with non-expired lease exists for the cell AND no terminal `CompletedRow` exists, the cell is `in_flight` and is skipped to avoid double-dispatch; (3) else (all rows `SupersededRow`-flagged or only `stage="run"` rows without live leases or no rows at all), the cell is `eligible` and the resumed orchestrator mints a **new `run_id`** for its attempt (retries never reuse a prior `run_id`, per the claim-dedup contract). This inline reducer is **independent of** and **simpler than** Phase 7's aggregator reducer — Phase 7's reducer additionally joins scoring/judgment payloads for analysis, which `runner.resume()` does not need. Phase 7's aggregator MAY internally re-use `_reduce_registry_by_cell_key` (imported from `runner.py`) for its first pass, but the dependency direction is one-way: Phase 3 → Phase 7, never the reverse. **Skipping by `run_id` would be wrong** — retries mint new `run_id`s, so two attempts for the same logical cell have different `run_id`s and a `run_id`-keyed skip would re-run the cell. This deliverable keeps resume semantics and claim-dedup semantics on the same key (`cell_key`) for consistency. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_resume_cell_key_reducer` seeds a synthetic registry with all three cell states (terminal, in_flight with live lease, eligible) and asserts `runner.resume()` dispatches only the eligible cells.
- [ ] **Phase-drop early-exit in the runner**: before dispatching each cell, `runner.run_cell(...)` calls `registry.is_phase_dropped(phase_id)`. If true, the cell is skipped (no dispatch, no `RunResult` emitted) and a `SkippedRow` with `reason="phase_dropped"` is appended for audit. This means when paraphrase/equivalence fails for a phase, any already-scheduled cells for that phase that haven't dispatched yet are short-circuited; in-flight cells (already dispatched) are allowed to finish and their `CompletedRow`s are filtered out by the aggregator's `is_phase_dropped` filter. This prevents dropped phases from consuming additional runs and keeps node-assignment balance intact.
- [ ] **Replacement-phase scheduler (resolves R29 B4 — owns enqueue of replacement cell matrices)**: `runner.py` owns the single top-level scheduler `run_session(selector, replications, models, sub_studies)` that orchestrates the full benchmark session and is the **sole caller** of `run_cell()`. The scheduler maintains an explicit in-memory `pending_queue: list[PhaseSpec]` seeded from `selector.select(...)`'s initial draw. On every iteration the scheduler (1) pops the next `PhaseSpec`, (2) expands it into its full `len(models) × len(sub_studies) × replications` cell matrix, (3) dispatches each cell via `run_cell()` (which internally runs paraphrase/equivalence → setup_clone → dispatch_run → scorer → teardown), and (4) **after the cell matrix for that phase completes, diffs the live session-state `redraw_map: dict[str, str]` against a local `seen_redraws: set[str]` snapshot taken at the start of the iteration**. Any newly-added `dropped_phase_id → replacement_phase_id` entry triggers the scheduler to: (a) resolve the replacement `PhaseSpec` via `selector.get_phase(replacement_phase_id)` (a new read-only helper that fetches a previously-drawn candidate from the selector's session-state cache — not a fresh stratified draw; the `redraw()` call already made the stratified selection, the scheduler just needs the `PhaseSpec` object), (b) append it to `pending_queue`, (c) **register the replacement phase with the probe scheduler** (resolves R41 B1 — the initial-draw loop in `run_session` calls `probe_scheduler.schedule(phase_id, model, expected_cell_count)` once per `(phase_id, model)` at session startup for every phase in the initial stratified draw; without this step, replacement phases enqueued mid-run via `selector.redraw()` would never be registered with the scheduler, so the probe watermark for each replacement phase would be zero instead of `len(sub_studies) × replications`, and `_maybe_fire(replacement_phase_id)` would fire immediately on the FIRST `notify_cell_judged` call instead of waiting for the full cell matrix to complete — violating the Phase 4 "never primes" trigger contract and firing a recognition probe while scored+judged runs are still outstanding). The scheduler executes, immediately after appending to `pending_queue`: `if self.probe_scheduler is not None: for model in models: self.probe_scheduler.schedule(replacement_phase_id, model, expected_cell_count=len(sub_studies) * replications)` — where `models`, `sub_studies`, and `replications` are the parameters already passed to the enclosing `run_session(selector, replications, models, sub_studies)` call (the `--models` subset, the sub-study list, and the replication count). **Resolves R46 B2**: iterating the CLI-scoped `models` list instead of the previously-hardcoded `("claude", "codex")` tuple means a single-model run like `--models claude` registers only the `claude` `(phase, model)` pair with the probe scheduler, so `_maybe_fire` (which iterates only the registered pairs — see Phase 4's subset-aware `_maybe_fire` contract) waits for exactly the cells that will actually be dispatched instead of indefinitely waiting for codex completions that never happen. The call is idempotent: `ProbeScheduler.schedule` overwrites the `(phase_id, model)` entry with the same `{expected: N, completed: 0, fired: False}` record on each invocation, so a resumed session that re-processes an already-enqueued replacement phase does not corrupt counters (the `completed` counter is rebuilt separately by `_resume_scheduler_counters_from_registry`). If `probe_scheduler is None` (Phase 4/6 not yet wired in during bottom-up test paths), the line is a no-op. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_replacement_phase_gets_scheduled_into_probe_scheduler` seeds a synthetic selector that fails paraphrase on phase A, invokes `run_session(models=["claude", "codex"])` with a mock `probe_scheduler`, and asserts `probe_scheduler.schedule` is called with `(replacement_phase_id, "claude", expected_cell_count)` AND `(replacement_phase_id, "codex", expected_cell_count)`. Companion unit test `test_runner.py::test_replacement_phase_respects_models_subset` invokes `run_session(models=["claude"])` and asserts `probe_scheduler.schedule` is called only with `(replacement_phase_id, "claude", ...)` and NEVER with `"codex"` — pinning the subset-aware iteration contract for replacement phases. (d) update `seen_redraws` to include the new `dropped_phase_id`. The scheduler loop continues until `pending_queue` is empty AND `redraw_map` has stabilized (two consecutive iterations observe no new entries). This guarantees that a paraphrase/equivalence failure in run_cell step (2) or a lock-unresolvable failure in setup_clone — both of which call `selector.redraw(phase_id)` to record the replacement — actually results in the replacement phase's full cell matrix being dispatched, satisfying Invariant 16's "phase is re-drawn" contract. The scheduler is **idempotent on resume**: `runner.resume()` reconstructs `pending_queue` from `selector.selected_phase_ids` (the Phase 2 read-only property; see Phase 2 Selector API Surface) minus `{phase_id for phase_id, cell_status in _reduce_registry_by_cell_key(registry).items() if all cells for that phase are terminal}` plus `[p for p in redraw_map.values() if p not in that terminal set]`, each materialized into a `PhaseSpec` via `selector.get_phase(phase_id)` (also a Phase 2 helper — both symbols are defined members of the selector's API surface, resolving R32 B4). Replacement phases enqueued by a prior session survive a kill/resume cycle. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_replacement_phase_scheduling` seeds a synthetic selector that fails paraphrase on phase A, asserts that phase A's replacement X appears in `redraw_map` after the failed cell, and asserts the scheduler dispatches all `(X, model, sub_study, replication)` cells — not just X's first cell — within the same session.
- [ ] **`selector.get_phase` consumer note (resolves R30 W2 dual-ownership — the helper is owned, implemented, and unit-tested in Phase 2; Phase 3 only consumes it).** Phase 2's `core/benchmark/selector.py` owns the implementation of `get_phase(phase_id: str) -> Optional[PhaseSpec]` (see Phase 2's Selector API Surface deliverable for the full signature + semantics). Phase 2's `tests/benchmark/test_selector.py` owns the unit test `test_get_phase_lookup`. Phase 3's `runner.py` imports and calls `get_phase` from the scheduler's replacement-phase expansion path. Phase 3 does **not** re-test the helper's own contract — `test_runner.py::test_replacement_phase_scheduling` (see above) asserts the scheduler's end-to-end behavior with `get_phase` as an assumed-working dependency; the helper's correctness is Phase 2's unit-test responsibility. No dual ownership: schema + impl + helper-unit-test are all Phase 2; Phase 3 owns only the scheduler-level integration test.

**Success Criteria:** Single `runner.run_cell(...)` executes end-to-end on a real past phase and produces N `RunResult` rows, N = replications, with balanced node assignment and recoverable after kill.

---

### Phase 4: Contamination Defenses — Paraphrasing + Equivalence Check + Post-Scoring Recognition Probe

**Goal:** Each phase's spec is paraphrased by a non-contestant, non-judge model and validated as semantically equivalent before the run. A separate, non-priming recognition probe runs _after_ scoring to log a per-(phase, model) contamination covariate.

**Files:**

- `core/benchmark/paraphraser.py` (NEW)
- `core/benchmark/equivalence.py` (NEW — Below `/api/classify` NLI wrapper)
- `core/benchmark/recognition_probe.py` (NEW)
- `core/benchmark/cli_paraphrase.py`, `cli_probe.py` (MODIFY — replace Phase 1 stubs with command bodies)
- `tests/benchmark/test_paraphraser.py` (NEW)
- `tests/benchmark/test_equivalence.py` (NEW)
- `tests/benchmark/test_recognition_probe.py` (NEW)
- (The `test_openrouter_min_contract.py` contract test is owned by **Phase 6** — see Phase 6's Files list. It cannot live in Phase 4 because the build order is `1 → 2 → 4 → 3 → 5 → 6 → ...` and `core/benchmark/openrouter.py` does not exist until Phase 6. Phase 4 owns the **invariant** — "`openrouter.py` must additively re-export everything in `openrouter_min.__all__`" — but the test that enforces it is a Phase 6 deliverable because Phase 6 is when both files exist and the invariant becomes testable.)
- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/equivalence-calibration.json` (NEW — persisted calibration artifact written by Phase 4's `equivalence.py` during the equivalence-validator calibration pass. Schema: `{primary: Literal["below","deepseek"], below_reachable: bool, below_agreement_rate: Optional[float], deepseek_agreement_rate: Optional[float], human_agreement_pairs: int, calibrated_at_utc: str, calibration_prompt_version: str, pairs: list[CalibrationPair]}` where `CalibrationPair` is imported from Phase 1's `models.py` (same pydantic model — see Phase 1 for the full field set and Literal values; no schema duplication) — the 20 hand-reviewed pairs (10 true-equivalent + 10 true-divergent) are stored in the `pairs` array so the calibration decision is auditable and re-runnable. Phase 4's `check_equivalence()` reads the aggregate fields on startup to decide which validator to treat as primary (`"below"` when reachable and `below_agreement_rate ≥ 0.8`, else `"deepseek"`). The per-pair predictions are preserved so that if Below or DeepSeek's API contract changes (model deprecation, endpoint rename), the harness can re-score the calibration pairs against the new client and re-derive the agreement rate without Byron re-labeling. Atomic write via `tmp+fsync+rename`. Read-only for Phase 7's aggregator (enters as an `equivalence_validator` covariate in the regression). `CalibrationPair` is declared as a pydantic model in Phase 1's `models.py` alongside the other benchmark row types so every reader imports the same shape.)
- `core/benchmark/openrouter_min.py` (NEW — **minimal** OpenRouter auth + chat-completion helper used by Phase 4's paraphraser, equivalence-fallback DeepSeek call, and the recognition probe. Phase 6's `core/benchmark/openrouter.py` extends this by re-exporting the same API and adding judge-specific retry/structured-error handling; Phase 6 imports `openrouter_min` and does not duplicate its logic. **Additive-only re-export contract (resolves R24 N11)**: Phase 6's `openrouter.py` is pinned to an **additive-only** relationship — it MAY add new symbols (new retry classes, new error types, new judge-specific helpers) and MAY re-export every symbol in `openrouter_min.__all__` unchanged, but MUST NOT rename, remove, or change the signature of any symbol Phase 4 imports. The test suite pins this contract: `test_openrouter_min_contract.py` (**owned and created in Phase 6's Files list** — see Phase 6; Phase 4 owns the invariant but cannot own the test because `openrouter.py` does not exist until Phase 6 in the build order `1 → 2 → 4 → 3 → 5 → 6 → ...`) asserts `set(openrouter_min.__all__) ⊆ set(dir(openrouter))` AND that every attribute in `openrouter_min.__all__` is callable with the same signature in `openrouter` (introspected via `inspect.signature` comparison). Any Phase 6 change that breaks this contract fails the test suite at Phase 6 integration time, not silently at Phase 10 run time.)

**Blocked by:** Phase 2 (uses `api_clients.BelowClient`; introduces `openrouter_min.py` used downstream by Phase 6)

**Deliverables:**

- [ ] Paraphraser uses OpenRouter `meta-llama/llama-3.1-405b-instruct` (primary) with a retry-once-with-different-seed on transient failure. **Secondary paraphraser (also via OpenRouter):** `mistralai/mixtral-8x22b-instruct` — used only if the primary errors twice in a row or returns a clearly-malformed paraphrase (pre-check on preserved identifiers). Never Claude/Codex/GPT-5/Gemini. Model id logged per paraphrase. **If both OpenRouter paraphrasers fail for the same phase after 3 total attempts**, paraphrase-failure is declared and the entire phase is dropped per Invariant 16 — there is no local-generation fallback (Below's verified contract is classification-only; no text-generation endpoint has been confirmed).
- [ ] Paraphrase preserves file paths and identifier names verbatim (regex-enforced post-check); only prose is rewritten.
- [ ] Original spec retained for scorer ground truth and never shown to the contestant.
- [ ] Equivalence validator contract: Below `POST /api/classify` expects `{text: str, categories: [str]}` (verified shape — single text, multi-category). The validator sends `{text: "A:\n<original>\n\n---\n\nB:\n<paraphrase>\n\nAre A and B semantically equivalent?", categories: ["equivalent","partial","diverged"]}` and a symmetric cross-check with A/B swapped. Both passes must return `category="equivalent"` with `confidence ≥ 0.6`.
- [ ] **Below calibration (pre-pilot) — generation + labeling is a Phase 4 deliverable**: produce an offline calibration set of 20 `(original, paraphrase)` pairs by (a) drawing 20 BUILD-spec phases **not in the benchmark candidate pool** (e.g. from the PROJECT_SPEC features or archived non-selected phases), (b) paraphrasing each via the OpenRouter paraphraser to produce 10 "true-equivalent" pairs, and (c) producing 10 "true-divergent" pairs by intentionally paraphrasing a different phase's spec as the "paraphrase" of the target (i.e. deliberately mismatched). Byron hand-reviews the 20 pairs once and writes the binary label (`equivalent` / `divergent`) to `.buildrunner/benchmarks/equivalence-calibration.json`. Running the calibration pairs through Below's classifier happens automatically at Phase 4 setup time. If Below agrees on ≥16/20 (80%) it is accepted as the primary validator; otherwise Below is dropped and DeepSeek becomes the primary validator. Calibration labels, Below outputs, and decision are all committed to the same JSON file for reproducibility.
- [ ] **Equivalence logic (precise):**
  - `primary = "below"` (or `"deepseek"` if Below failed calibration). Primary must return `equivalent` on both A/B directions with `confidence ≥ 0.6`.
  - If Below is **reachable** but returns `partial`/`diverged` or low confidence → call DeepSeek as a confirming second validator; accept only if DeepSeek also returns `equivalent`; otherwise treat as a paraphrase failure.
  - If Below is **unreachable** (transport error, Ollama down, timeout) → promote DeepSeek to sole validator for this call; `equivalence_validator` field records `"deepseek"`; DeepSeek alone must return `equivalent`.
  - Result of "both agreed" is recorded as `"both"`; "below-only" as `"below"`; "deepseek-only" as `"deepseek"`; paraphrase-failure as `"na"`. This field enters the Phase 7 regression as a covariate so heterogeneous validation does not become a hidden source of variance.
- [ ] **No fallback to the original spec**: if paraphrasing or equivalence checking fails after 3 retries with different seeds, the **entire phase** is dropped from both models and both sub-studies (Invariant 16) via a single call `selector.redraw(phase_id, reason)` (Phase 2 deliverable — where `reason` is `"paraphrase_failed"` or `"equivalence_failed"`). **`selector.redraw()` is the SOLE writer of `DroppedRow`** (resolves R36 W1 — prior drafts had Phase 4 call `registry.drop_phase(phase_id, reason)` AND `selector.redraw(phase_id)`, double-writing the same drop event; the corrected contract is that Phase 4's failure path never calls `registry.drop_phase` directly; `selector.redraw` is the single entry point that atomically appends the `DroppedRow`, reserves the replacement slot in `session_state.redraw_map`, and returns the replacement `PhaseSpec` under one lock acquisition — enforcing the stratified replacement rule: same stratum first, nearest adjacent with `stratum_violation` log on exhaustion, abort when <2 strata survive). Exclusions are logged via the shared `ExclusionRow` pydantic writer to `.buildrunner/benchmarks/exclusions.jsonl` using the schema declared up-front in Phase 1 / Phase 2 (reasons: `paraphrase_failed`, `equivalence_failed`) — this is a separate sibling log to `DroppedRow`, written inside `selector.redraw()` alongside the `DroppedRow` append (both under the same lock). Appended under `fcntl.flock` like the registry.
- [ ] Recognition probe dispatches a one-shot prompt asking "Have you seen a project called X with the following checklist?" in a **fresh OS process**. Output is written as a single `RecognitionRow` (declared in Phase 1's row-type union) with fields `{row_type: "recognition", session_id, phase_id, model, recognition_score: float ∈ [0, 1], probed_at_utc}` — **`session_id` is required** (resolves R40 B1) per Phase 1's session-scoped invariant; the probe scheduler reads the current `session_id` from the running orchestrator's `SessionState` and passes it to the writer. Never fed back to the contestant. **Trigger condition (single precise rule, post-terminal-stage gate — resolves R25 recognition-probe contradiction AND R50 W3 single-model-mode trigger divergence)**: the probe fires for a `(phase_id, model)` pair when, checked under the registry lock, **every `(phase_id, any_registered_model, sub_study, replication)` cell for this phase has a `CompletedRow` at its session's terminal stage** — where the session's terminal stage is determined by `len(session_state.get_flag(session_id, "selected_models"))`: `stage="judged"` when the session is two-model (`len == 2`) or `stage="scored"` when the session is single-model (`len < 2`, no judging ever runs so `scored` is the final stage). `any_registered_model` means the models actually registered with the scheduler via `schedule()` — i.e. the subset passed to `--models` — NOT a hardcoded `{claude, codex}` pair. Once that condition is met, probes are scheduled for each registered `(phase_id, model)` pair (one per registered model: two probes per phase in two-model sessions, one probe per phase in single-model sessions). **The "never primes" invariant is preserved identically in both modes**: the recognition probe fires strictly AFTER the phase's runs reach their session's terminal stage, so the probe's output cannot prime any run that is still producing analyzable data. In two-model mode, terminal is `judged` because the run's scored metrics would still be fed through pairwise judgment; firing the probe before `judged` would leak a post-hoc recognition signal into judge prompts assembled from scored-stage data.
