In single-model mode, terminal is `scored` because no judging runs — the scored row IS the run's final analyzable output, so the probe fires strictly after that output is sealed and cannot prime it. The earlier wording that hardcoded `stage="judged"` is REMOVED; it was correct for two-model sessions but impossible to satisfy in single-model sessions (no judged row ever exists), which would have indefinitely delayed probe firing in single-model mode. The mode-aware gate on "all cells for the phase are at the session's terminal stage" is the correct invariant: it guarantees zero future terminal-stage writes remain outstanding for either model's runs on this phase, eliminating the residual taint window in both modes. The scheduler polls the registry after each `stage="judged"` row is appended and dispatches the probe when both conditions become true for a given `(phase_id, model)` pair. Only one probe ever fires per pair (deduplicated via a `RecognitionRow` existence check under the same lock). The "fresh OS process" constraint still applies: the probe runs in a subprocess with a clean env (same allowlist as the main runner) so no in-memory state from prior runs can bias the response.
- [ ] Recognition score used only as a regression covariate in Phase 7 analysis — not a filter.
- [ ] **Probe aggregation + append-only compatibility**: the probe runs **once per `(phase, model)` pair** — deterministically when the two-condition trigger above fires — producing a single scalar written as one `RecognitionRow`. The aggregator (Phase 7) joins this scalar onto each reduced-run record for the matching `(phase_id, model)` at analysis time via a left-join in `aggregator.load_runs()`; `CompletedRow`s never carry a `recognition_score` field (it's populated only in the in-memory analysis dataframe). There is **no in-place update of earlier rows** — the JSONL log stays strictly append-only. The join rule is documented in both `recognition_probe.py` and `aggregator.py`. If a pair never gets a `RecognitionRow` (e.g. run aborted before judgment completed for the opposing model), its joined `recognition_score` is `NaN` and the Phase 7 regression uses pairwise-complete data (documented in the methods section). **Probe-failure retry + backfill path (resolves R30 W6)**: a single probe dispatch can fail on transient OpenRouter 5xx, rate-limit 429, or subprocess timeout. The scheduler's post-judgment trigger **attempts the probe up to 3 times with jittered backoff** (2 s, 8 s, 32 s) in-process before giving up. If all three attempts fail, the scheduler appends a `ProbePendingRow` (declared in Phase 1's union: `{row_type: "probe_pending", session_id, phase_id, model, attempt_count: int, last_error: str, last_attempted_at_utc: str}` — **`session_id` is required** per Phase 1's schema; R40 B1) to the registry — still append-only, under the same `LOCK_EX`. The `br benchmark probe` subcommand (already declared in Phase 1's command list) is then a **backfill pass**: it scans the registry for `ProbePendingRow` entries that do NOT yet have a matching `RecognitionRow` — the dedup key is **`(session_id, phase_id, model)`** (resolves R42 B2 — Phase 1's `RecognitionRow` and `ProbePendingRow` schemas both carry `session_id` as the primary-session discriminator; any dedup that drops `session_id` would let a later session's completed `RecognitionRow` suppress an earlier session's pending probe, or let two concurrent sessions' probes collide on a shared `(phase_id, model)` bucket. The full 3-tuple match matches Phase 1's schema exactly: a `ProbePendingRow{session_id=S1, phase_id=P, model=M}` is only considered "already fulfilled" when a `RecognitionRow{session_id=S1, phase_id=P, model=M}` exists — a `RecognitionRow{session_id=S2, ...}` from a different session does NOT satisfy it). `br benchmark probe` defaults to scoping its scan to the current `SessionState.session_id` (so an operator-invoked backfill only touches its own session's pending rows); `br benchmark probe --session-id <id>` re-runs backfill for a past session; `br benchmark probe --all-sessions` backfills across every session present in the registry (surfaced as a separate flag because cross-session backfill is a rare operator action and opt-in). For each un-fulfilled `ProbePendingRow`, the backfill re-attempts with the same 3-retry policy. A successful backfill appends the `RecognitionRow` as normal; continued failure appends a new `ProbePendingRow` with incremented `attempt_count`. The aggregator's left-join in Phase 7 prefers `RecognitionRow` if present; if only `ProbePendingRow` exists for a pair, the covariate is `NaN` and the methods-section caveat names the affected pairs and attempt counts. Phase 9's pilot-gate deliverables and Phase 10's full-study completion gate call `br benchmark probe` once as a backfill pass after all runs + judgments are complete, so otherwise-complete phases do not silently lose the recognition covariate on transient probe failure. Unit test `test_recognition_probe.py::test_retry_then_pending_then_backfill` covers: 3x failure → `ProbePendingRow` appended, backfill invocation → `RecognitionRow` appended, final join → covariate present.

**Success Criteria:** Paraphrased specs pass symmetric equivalence check. Probe runs fully post-scoring and does not appear in any scored-run context. Probe returns a scalar score per (phase, model).

---

### Phase 5: Objective Scoring + Plan Adherence + Toolchain Installation

**Goal:** Scorer produces `ObjectiveMetrics` and `AdherenceMetrics` for any completed run, with explicitly defined partial-credit rules.

**Files:**

- `core/benchmark/scorer.py` (NEW — implements Phase 3's `ScorerProtocol`)
- `core/benchmark/cli_score.py` (MODIFY — replaces Phase 1's stub body with the real `br benchmark score` command that re-scores a completed run from registry by invoking `BenchmarkScorer.score_run()` against a re-materialized clone per the execution-target contract in this phase. The command body imports from `core/benchmark/scorer.py`; `core/benchmark/cli.py` is not touched — it already imports `cli_score` and calls its `register(app)` hook from Phase 1.)
- `core/benchmark/cli_gc_anchors.py` (MODIFY — adds the `--reset-venv` flag to the `br benchmark gc-anchors` command. The flag removes `.venv-benchmark/` and re-runs Phase 1's `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh` so the next benchmark session starts from the deterministic parent-repo requirements set per Phase 5's end-of-session rollback contract. **Venv flock acquisition is mandatory before `rm -rf .venv-benchmark/` (resolves R52 W1 — an operator-invoked `br benchmark gc-anchors --reset-venv` fired while a concurrent orchestrator's `run_local_tests` holds `/tmp/br3-bench-venv.lock` mid-pytest would, without this guard, remove `.venv-benchmark/` out from under the in-flight pytest's Python interpreter, crashing the scorer with `FileNotFoundError` on `.venv-benchmark/bin/python` or a mid-process SIGBUS on an mmap'd `.so` file; the in-flight contestant's run would be lost AND the flock would be released onto a non-existent venv for the next waiter. The fix serializes venv destruction behind the same `/tmp/br3-bench-venv.lock` that scorer runs hold)**: the `--reset-venv` code path calls `runner._acquire_venv_lock()` (the same helper Phase 5 declares on `Runner` for scorer paths — wraps `fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX)` on `/tmp/br3-bench-venv.lock` with a **30-minute ceiling for the operator path** (longer than scorer-path's 10-min ceiling because operator-invoked resets are infrequent and the operator explicitly accepts a longer wait when an in-flight run is holding the lock) before `rm -rf .venv-benchmark/`, then re-runs `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh` under the same held lock, then releases. If the 30-min ceiling is hit, the command exits with a remediation message naming the holding pid (read from `flock -x --verbose` or `fuser /tmp/br3-bench-venv.lock`) and the age of the lock, so the operator can decide to wait or to SIGKILL the stuck scorer. Unit test `tests/benchmark/test_cli_gc_anchors.py::test_reset_venv_acquires_venv_flock_before_rm` mocks `subprocess.run` and `fcntl.flock`, seeds a held lock, invokes `--reset-venv` with a 1-second ceiling, and asserts (a) `fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX)` is called BEFORE `shutil.rmtree(.venv-benchmark/)`, (b) on ceiling hit the command exits with the remediation message and never removes the venv. Companion test `test_reset_venv_releases_lock_after_reinstall` asserts the lock is released AFTER `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh` completes, so the next waiter sees a freshly-installed venv. The command body extension imports `_acquire_venv_lock` from `core/benchmark/runner.py` (which also owns the venv path constants); `core/benchmark/cli.py` is not touched — Phase 1's register hook is unchanged.)
- `core/benchmark/cli_run.py` (MODIFY — **this is the actual scorer wiring site (resolves R29 B3 AND R44 B1)**. Phase 3 left `cli_run.py` constructing `Runner(config=config)` with `scorer=None` defaulted because `BenchmarkScorer` did not yet exist. In Phase 5, `cli_run.py`'s `register(app)` hook is updated to `from core.benchmark.scorer import BenchmarkScorer` at module scope and to construct `Runner(config=config, scorer=BenchmarkScorer(config))` inside the command body — **both arguments use the canonical config-first signature declared in Phase 3's `Runner.__init__`** (R43 B3) and Phase 5's `BenchmarkScorer(config)` constructor (see `scorer.py` declaration below). `config = load_config()` is already constructed at the top of `cli_run.py`'s command body from Phase 1's wiring. Phase 6 then extends this same call site again to pass `judge` and `probe_scheduler`. The same edit applies to `cli_resume.py` — see the additional MODIFY entry below. This MODIFY is what guarantees the full `br benchmark run` and `br benchmark resume` paths actually exercise the scorer instead of silently staying on Phase 3's `scorer=None` path.)
- `core/benchmark/cli_resume.py` (MODIFY — same config-first wiring as `cli_run.py`: import `BenchmarkScorer` and construct `Runner(config=config, scorer=BenchmarkScorer(config))` in the resume command body using the canonical config-first signature (R43 B3 / R44 B1). Phase 3 owned the initial stub; Phase 5's scorer-integration edit lands here too so resumed sessions score their runs.)
- `core/benchmark/runner.py` (MODIFY — **Phase 5 owns these new methods on `Runner`** (resolves R32 B3 ownership gap): `_detect_baseline_drift(baseline_freeze: str, current_freeze: str) -> VenvDriftReport`, `_detect_venv_drift(pre_freeze: str, post_freeze: str) -> VenvDriftReport`, `_acquire_venv_lock() -> fcntl.flock handle` (wraps `/tmp/br3-bench-venv.lock` with `LOCK_EX` + 10-min ceiling), `_reset_baseline_before_run(clone_path: Path)` (executes the pre-run guard's `current_freeze = pip freeze` comparison against `baseline_freeze` and forcibly recreates `.venv-benchmark/` via `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh` if drift), `_cleanup_editable_install(editable_package_name: Optional[str])` (runs `pip uninstall -y <editable_package_name>` under the venv flock), `_recreate_venv_at_session_end()` (invoked by `cli_run.py` finally-block and by `br benchmark gc-anchors --reset-venv`), **`_reinstall_contestant_requirements(clone_path: Path) -> None`** (**resolves R44 B4 — explicit declaration in Phase 5's Runner method ownership list**; the two-pass reinstall helper that matches Phase 1's install-benchmark-deps.sh ordering contract: Pass 1 iterates `sorted((clone_path).glob("requirements*.txt"))` and pip-installs every file EXCEPT `requirements-benchmark.txt` into `.venv-benchmark/`; Pass 2 installs `requirements-benchmark.txt` LAST so the harness's narrower pins win on overlap with any contestant requirements; both passes execute under `self._acquire_venv_lock()` with `pip install --python .venv-benchmark/bin/python -r <file>`; any non-zero pip exit propagates as `VenvReinstallFailed` with the failing file name; a final `VenvDriftReport` from `_detect_venv_drift` is returned to the caller. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_reinstall_preserves_two_pass_order` (already referenced in Phase 5's toolchain deliverable) seeds a synthetic clone with `requirements.txt`, `requirements-benchmark.txt`, and `requirements-dev.txt`, monkeypatches `subprocess.run`, and asserts the three `pip install` calls fire in the order `[requirements.txt, requirements-dev.txt, requirements-benchmark.txt]` with `requirements-benchmark.txt` last. The helper is called by `toolchain.run_local_tests(handle, runner)` via the injected Runner reference per the R40 B2 dispatch contract.). Phase 3 already defined `run_cell()` to call `self.scorer.score_run(...)` when `self.scorer is not None` — that wiring is unchanged. Phase 5's additions live as new `_private` helpers on `Runner` (the class-owner); the `BenchmarkScorer` calls these helpers by reference on the injected `Runner` (`self.runner._detect_baseline_drift(...)`), keeping the drift-detection code where the venv is managed. Phase 5's `test_runner.py::test_detect_baseline_drift_classifies_four_cases` + `test_runner.py::test_pre_run_guard_rejects_baseline_pure_addition` + `test_runner.py::test_editable_install_cleanup` unit-test these helpers directly. If `self.scorer is None` at runtime, `run_cell()` skips scoring silently — that branch is preserved exclusively for the unit-test constructor path. The actual `BenchmarkScorer` instantiation happens in `cli_run.py` / `cli_resume.py`. **Every method listed above is net-new in Phase 5 and owned by Phase 5**; no Phase-3 method is modified. Phase 3's existing `Runner` API surface (`run_cell`, `run_session`, `resume`, `dispatch_run`, `setup_clone`, `teardown_clone`) is unchanged.)
- `core/benchmark/pass_at_k.py` (NEW)

Referenced throughout Phase 1/5 acceptance; without this explicit file declaration the re-scoring contract would have no scheduled test.)

**Blocked by:** Phase 2, Phase 3 (uses `api_clients.py` for optional Walter/Lomax enrichment; uses the `CloneHandle` yielded by `setup_clone()` and enriched with `post_run_commit_sha` by `finalize_run()`; the scorer runs **inside the clone, before `teardown_clone()`**, per the execution-target contract in the deliverables below)

**Deliverables:**

- [ ] `.buildrunner/benchmarks/tools/package.json` is created with the pinned Node tools. During Phase 5 setup, `npm install` is run once in that directory to generate `package-lock.json`, which is committed to the repo for reproducibility.
- [ ] `scripts/install-benchmark-tools.sh` is idempotent and composes two installs: (a) **delegates to Phase 1's `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh`** for the Python venv + `requirements-benchmark.txt` (no duplication); (b) runs `(cd .buildrunner/benchmarks/tools && if [ -f package-lock.json ]; then npm ci; else npm install && echo "WARN: generated lockfile; commit it"; fi)` for Prettier, ESLint, tsc, jscpd. The `npm ci` path is the reproducible path used by CI; the `npm install` fallback only fires in first-run / lockfile-missing situations.
- [ ] `toolchain.py` exposes three public symbols (**resolves R36 B3** — earlier drafts only listed `PROJECT_TOOLS` and `ensure_installed()`, but the scorer path already invokes `toolchain.run_local_tests(handle, runner)`; the function is now a first-class part of the module's declared surface): (a) `PROJECT_TOOLS = { 'prettier': '.buildrunner/benchmarks/tools/node_modules/.bin/prettier', 'eslint': '...eslint', 'tsc': '...tsc', 'jscpd': '...jscpd', 'black': '.venv-benchmark/bin/black', 'ruff': '...ruff', 'lizard': '...lizard' }` resolved relative to the repo root; (b) `ensure_installed()` — `os.access(X_OK)` each path and fail fast with the install command if missing (**never relies on `PATH`** — no global binary can shadow a project-local one); (c) **`run_local_tests(handle: CloneHandle, runner: "Runner") -> LocalTestResult`** (**resolves R40 B2** — the signature now takes an explicit `runner: "Runner"` reference as the second positional argument so the function has a declared dependency on the six helper methods Phase 5 owns on `Runner` per the `core/benchmark/runner.py` MODIFY entry above. Earlier drafts declared `run_local_tests(handle)` with an implicit `self.runner.*` assumption on the caller's side, leaving the scoring path underspecified and un-wireable without a Runner reference. With the explicit parameter, the scorer protocol in Phase 3 is updated to `score_run(handle: CloneHandle, phase: PhaseSpec, run_result: RunResult, runner: "Runner") -> tuple[ObjectiveMetrics, AdherenceMetrics]` and `Runner.run_cell()` calls `self.scorer.score_run(handle, phase, run_result, self)` — passing `self` through so `BenchmarkScorer.score_run` can forward it into `toolchain.run_local_tests(handle, runner)`. The Runner-helpers (`_detect_baseline_drift`, `_detect_venv_drift`, `_acquire_venv_lock`, `_reset_baseline_before_run`, `_cleanup_editable_install`, `_recreate_venv_at_session_end`) remain owned by Phase 5's `runner.py` MODIFY entry; ownership does not split between `toolchain.py` and `runner.py` — `toolchain.py` calls them via the injected `runner` reference, preserving single-owner semantics) — the scorer-facing entry point that performs the full install → pytest → vitest → teardown sequence documented in the next deliverable. Internally it calls into the four-class drift detector (`runner._detect_baseline_drift` / `runner._detect_venv_drift`), the venv-flock acquirer (`runner._acquire_venv_lock`), the editable-install leak guard (`runner._cleanup_editable_install`), and the per-surface pytest/vitest invocations. The function is declared here in `toolchain.py` (not `scorer.py`) because it owns the shared-venv resource and the node/python tool paths, and because the scorer protocol (`score_run(handle, phase, run_result, runner) -> (ObjectiveMetrics, AdherenceMetrics)`) calls `toolchain.run_local_tests(handle, runner)` to produce `ObjectiveMetrics.local_test_result`. Unit test `test_toolchain.py::test_run_local_tests_surface` asserts the three symbols are importable from `core.benchmark.toolchain` and that `run_local_tests` accepts the two-arg `(handle, runner)` signature (mocks Runner and verifies the helpers are dispatched on the injected reference, not looked up in a module-level registry).
- [ ] Chen 2021 pass@k unbiased estimator: `1 − C(n−c, k) / C(n, k)`; unit-tested against the Codex paper's worked examples.
- [ ] **Primary test-pass verdict is LOCAL** (this is the source of truth for `ObjectiveMetrics.test_pass`). **Execution-target contract** (resolves the "no checked-out tree after teardown" risk): the scorer runs **inside the Phase 3 clone at `handle.clone_path`** while `bench-src-<run_id>` is still checked out, **before** `teardown_clone(handle)` is invoked. Phase 3's `runner.run_cell()` orders the calls as `setup_clone → dispatch_run → finalize_run → scorer.score_run(handle, ...) → teardown_clone`; `teardown_clone` never runs until the scorer has returned. The scorer signature is therefore `run_local_tests(handle: CloneHandle, runner: "Runner") -> LocalTestResult` (**resolves R41 B2** — single canonical signature across the entire Phase 5 section; earlier drafts kept a stale single-arg `(handle)` form here that diverged from the toolchain.py API-surface declaration. Both occurrences in Phase 5 now use the 2-arg form byte-for-byte) and it receives the full handle plus the Runner reference so it can resolve `handle.clone_path` (the filesystem tree with the contestant's post-run files materialized on `bench-src-<run_id>`), `handle.pre_run_commit_sha` (to re-derive the diff if needed), AND the six Runner-owned drift/flock/cleanup helpers dispatched as `runner._detect_baseline_drift`, `runner._acquire_venv_lock`, etc. If for any reason the scorer is re-invoked after teardown (e.g. from `br benchmark score --run-id <id>` as a re-scoring pass from registry data), it **re-materializes** the clone by checking out `refs/heads/bench/<run_id>` (the anchor ref Phase 3 fetched into the parent repo) into a fresh scratch dir via `git worktree add /tmp/br3-bench-rescore-<run_id> refs/heads/bench/<run_id>` — acceptable here because the scorer never shells out to `dispatch-to-node.sh` from this scratch tree (the line-48 `.git`-is-directory check does not apply to the scorer's own subprocess calls). Re-materialized scratch trees are removed on scorer exit via a `finally` block. After Phase 3's `finalize_run()` yields the handle, the scorer runs the repo's own test commands inside the clone via `toolchain.run_local_tests(handle, runner)` (Runner reference forwarded from `BenchmarkScorer.score_run(handle, phase, run_result, runner)` per the Phase 3 ScorerProtocol signature). The UI test path is gated on directory + package.json existence: **verified present as of 2026-04-16** — `ui/` contains `package.json` whose `scripts.test` equals `"vitest"`. **Dependency-install step (precedes every test invocation; without it `pytest` and `vitest` fail in a fresh clone because the clone does not copy `node_modules/` or the Python venv — they are untracked):**
  - **Python**: `run_local_tests` does **not** create a new venv per run (a per-run venv costs ~30 s — ~3 hrs over the 360-run full study, which would break the schedule). It reuses the repo's shared `.venv-benchmark/` which Phase 1 provisions with **all root `requirements*.txt` files** the project ships — as of 2026-04-16 that is `requirements-benchmark.txt` (harness deps: pytest, pytest-timeout, scikit-learn, scipy, statsmodels, pydantic, responses, vcrpy, typer) plus `requirements-api.txt` (BR3 API runtime deps). The Phase 1 installer iterates over every matching root file, so any future root-level `requirements*.txt` is picked up automatically. This ensures the contestant's imports of existing BR3 modules do not fail on missing third-party packages unrelated to their changes. **Contestant-introduced new deps (W3 handling)**: if the contestant's diff modifies any root-level `requirements*.txt` inside the clone, the runner detects the change via a `git diff --name-only <pre_run_commit_sha>..HEAD` scan at scorer entry and, under the same `/tmp/br3-bench-venv.lock`, re-runs the **two-pass install in Phase 1's canonical order** (**resolves R40 W1** — a naive single-loop `for req in <clone_path>/requirements*.txt; do pip install -r "$req"; done` in lexicographic order would install `requirements-api.txt` AFTER `requirements-benchmark.txt`, silently reversing the harness-pin-priority contract Phase 1's `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh` enforces via its explicit two-pass structure. The per-run reinstall must match the installer's pass order exactly so the scorer's invariant `pytest<9.0`-class pins always win on the resolver's last-write): **Pass 1** — `shopt -s nullglob; for req in <clone_path>/requirements*.txt; do [ "$(basename "$req")" = "requirements-benchmark.txt" ] && continue; .venv-benchmark/bin/pip install -r "$req"; done; shopt -u nullglob` (skips the harness's own file). **Pass 2** — `if [ -f <clone_path>/requirements-benchmark.txt ]; then .venv-benchmark/bin/pip install -r <clone_path>/requirements-benchmark.txt; else .venv-benchmark/bin/pip install -r <PARENT_REPO>/requirements-benchmark.txt; fi` (installs the harness's own file LAST so its pins cap any overlapping pins from Pass 1). **Parent-repo fallback (resolves R51 B1 — historical pre-phase commits that Phase 3's `setup_clone` checks out via `checkout -b bench-src-<run_id> <pre_run_commit_sha>` predate Phase 1 and therefore do NOT contain `<clone_path>/requirements-benchmark.txt`; a plain `if [ -f ... ]; then ...; fi` guard would silently skip Pass 2 and let any contestant-pinned version in Pass 1's `requirements-api.txt` win the resolver's last-write, defeating the harness-pin-priority contract on every benchmark run against the real corpus)**: when the clone's historical commit lacks the harness file, Pass 2 falls back to the **current parent repo's** `requirements-benchmark.txt` (read at benchmark-session start, before any checkouts happen, so the fallback path is pinned to the version of the harness file that was present when the session started — not whatever the parent might be on at teardown). The fallback path is always safe because the harness file is **defined** to live in the parent repo (Phase 1 owns it), and the scorer's pin-priority contract is "harness pins win, contestant pins fill", which requires the harness file regardless of what the contestant's checkout contains. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_pass2_falls_back_to_parent_when_clone_missing_harness_file` seeds a clone whose checkout predates Phase 1 (no `requirements-benchmark.txt` in the tree), runs the two-pass reinstall, and asserts the harness's `pytest<9.0` pin is applied (via `pip show pytest`) against the parent repo's copy. Companion unit test `test_pass2_uses_clone_when_present` seeds a clone with its own copy of `requirements-benchmark.txt` and asserts the clone's copy is used (not the parent's), so a contestant legitimately updating the harness file during a Phase-1-or-later run is still reflected in the installed pins. The two-pass invocation is wrapped in a Python helper `runner._reinstall_contestant_requirements(clone_path: Path)` that shells out to `bash -c` with the two pass bodies concatenated so the single subprocess gets the same ordering guarantee as Phase 1's installer. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_reinstall_preserves_two_pass_order` seeds a clone with both `requirements-api.txt` pinning `pytest==8.1.0` and `requirements-benchmark.txt` pinning `pytest<9.0`, runs the reinstall path, and asserts `.venv-benchmark/bin/pip show pytest` reports a version satisfying `<9.0` (the harness pin wins, not the contestant's Pass-1 pin). This picks up newly-pinned deps so a contestant's `import httpx`-plus-`echo "httpx" >> requirements-api.txt` edit is scored as a working change rather than an `install_failed`. A contestant that imports a new third-party package **without** pinning it in any `requirements*.txt` file still surfaces as `status="fail"` from pytest with the expected `ModuleNotFoundError` — that is scored as a model failure (incomplete work), which is the correct outcome. After the pytest run, the transient reinstall is **not rolled back mid-session** (rolling back adds ~30 s to every run and would race on the flock), so the venv accumulates the union of all contestants' pinned deps across the full study. **Version-change isolation (resolves the shared-venv leakage concern + R25 W3 dependency-removal/same-major-replacement)**: to prevent a contestant's edit of an already-present dep's **version** (e.g. `pydantic==2.5.0` → `pydantic==2.6.0`), a contestant's **removal** of a pinned dep (e.g. deleting a line from `requirements-api.txt`), or a contestant's **same-major replacement** (e.g. `pydantic==2.5.0` → `pydantic==2.5.3` where the first two version components match) from silently changing later runs' test outcomes, the runner maintains a **session baseline** `baseline_freeze` written once to `.venv-benchmark/.br3-baseline-freeze.txt` by `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh` immediately after the Pass-2 install completes, then never touched for the rest of the session. **Pre-run guard (resolves R28 W3 in-run isolation — the current run's pytest/vitest must execute against a venv equal to `baseline_freeze + only this run's additions`, not against whatever cumulative state prior contestants left behind)**: at the start of every scorer invocation, **before** the contestant's `pip install -r requirements*.txt` + `pip install -e .` steps run, the runner computes `current_freeze = pip freeze` and compares it against `baseline_freeze` using the same four-class drift detector defined below. If `_detect_baseline_drift(baseline_freeze, current_freeze)` returns any drift class, the runner forcibly recreates `.venv-benchmark/` via `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh` under `/tmp/br3-bench-venv.lock` and re-samples `current_freeze` (which by construction now equals `baseline_freeze`). Only after this guard passes does the runner then (a) snapshot `pre_freeze = current_freeze`, (b) run the contestant's dep install + editable install, (c) snapshot `post_freeze = pip freeze`, and (d) execute pytest/vitest. This two-step comparison — `baseline_freeze → current_freeze` as a pre-run guard, then `pre_freeze → post_freeze` as the this-run-only contribution check — guarantees in-run isolation even when a prior run's drift slipped past its own post-install check (e.g. drift introduced during `pip install -e` resolving transitive deps that were not caught as dep-edits in the prior run's `git diff`). The post-install comparison against `pre_freeze`: **Four drift classes trigger `venv_version_drift=true`** (any one is sufficient): (a) **downgrade** — `package` present in both, `post.version < pre.version` per PEP 440 `packaging.version.Version` comparison; (b) **cross-major-version change** — `package` present in both, `post.version.major != pre.version.major`; (c) **same-major replacement** — `package` present in both, `post.version != pre.version` and `post.version.major == pre.version.major` (this subsumes minor and patch bumps within a major line, e.g. `2.5.0 → 2.5.3` or `2.5.0 → 2.6.0`, which can change library behavior even without the major bump); (d) **dependency removal** — `package in pre_freeze and package not in post_freeze` (the contestant's diff implicitly uninstalled a pinned dep, which means a subsequent run's import of that package would fall through to whatever transitive install the next contestant's `pip install -e` resolves, turning a missing-dep failure into a false pass). Clean upward version bumps against a net-new package (the package is in `post_freeze` but not in `pre_freeze`) are **not** drift — they are pure additions, the expected contestant pattern. **Undeclared-import cross-contamination guard (resolves R29 W2 — pure additions from prior runs would otherwise silently satisfy a later run's undeclared `import foo`)**: the pre-run guard above already recreates `.venv-benchmark/` whenever `_detect_baseline_drift(baseline_freeze, current_freeze)` returns ANY class of drift. Crucially, this guard's drift-class set is **extended to include pure additions against the baseline** (not just downgrade/cross-major/same-major-replacement/removal) — formally: `_detect_baseline_drift` returns drift when `current_freeze != baseline_freeze` on any dimension, including `package in current_freeze and package not in baseline_freeze` (a pure addition relative to baseline). This is stricter than the post-install `_detect_venv_drift(pre_freeze, post_freeze)` check, which still treats pure additions as non-drift for its this-run-only isolation purpose (because a contestant is allowed to add deps in its OWN run). The two checks intentionally differ: post-install allows additions as legitimate contestant work; pre-run rejects them because they indicate a prior contestant's additions have leaked into this run's starting environment. The net effect is that every run's pytest/vitest executes against exactly `baseline_freeze + only this run's additions` — no prior contestant's add can ever be visible to a later contestant's imports. The fast path (no recreation) still fires when baseline is intact, which is the expected case because the post-install drift check catches this-run drift and recreates the venv at the NEXT run's pre-run guard. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_pre_run_guard_rejects_baseline_pure_addition` seeds a venv with baseline + a synthetic `import-free-rider` package (simulating a prior run's addition), runs the pre-run guard, and asserts the venv is recreated before the current run's contestant install fires. Implementation: the drift check in `runner._detect_venv_drift(pre_freeze, post_freeze)` returns a `VenvDriftReport` pydantic model `{drift: bool, classes: list[Literal["downgrade","cross_major","same_major_replacement","dependency_removal"]], affected_packages: dict[str, {pre: Optional[str], post: Optional[str], class_: str}]}` which is attached to `LocalTestResult.venv_drift_report`. **Order of operations (resolves R47 B4 — previously pytest/vitest executed BEFORE venv recreation so the current run was scored against the drifted env; fixed order ensures the current run's tests run against a pristine-baseline + only-this-run's-contestant-install state)**: (1) snapshot `pre_freeze`; (2) run contestant's `pip install -r requirements*.txt` + `pip install -e .`; (3) snapshot `post_freeze`; (4) compute `_detect_venv_drift(pre_freeze, post_freeze)`; (5) **if drift detected, BEFORE running any pytest/vitest**, the runner forcibly recreates `.venv-benchmark/` via `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh` under the same flock, then re-runs `_reinstall_contestant_requirements(clone_path)` (the two-pass install + editable install) against the fresh venv, then re-snapshots `post_freeze_v2` for audit. This second install starts from the pristine baseline rather than from an accumulated multi-run state, so any transitive drift introduced by a prior contestant's cumulative deps is washed out. (6) **Only after the recreate-then-reinstall path** (or directly after step 4 if no drift was detected) does the runner execute pytest/vitest. (7) The test verdict is computed against the final state of `.venv-benchmark/` and is the authoritative scored outcome. The `venv_version_drift=true` flag is still attached to `LocalTestResult` as a provenance marker so Phase 7's regression can include it as a covariate (answering "did runs that triggered a mid-run recreate score differently from runs that did not?"), but the score itself reflects a clean environment. **End-of-session recreation remains** as a defensive reset for any state the mid-run recreate path might have missed. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_drift_triggers_recreate_before_pytest` seeds a clone whose `requirements*.txt` downgrades a baseline-pinned package, runs the scorer path, and asserts (a) `.venv-benchmark/` is recreated, (b) contestant reinstall is invoked a second time against the fresh venv, (c) pytest runs exactly once AFTER the recreate completes (not before), (d) `LocalTestResult.venv_drift_report.drift==True`, (e) the `pytest` subprocess started-at timestamp is strictly later than the venv recreation's finish timestamp. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_no_drift_skips_recreate` asserts the fast path (no drift → no recreate → single install → pytest). The ~30 s recreation cost is paid only when drift is detected (expected to be <5–10% of runs — most contestant `requirements*.txt` edits are **additions**, with occasional version bumps and rare removals). For pure additions (new packages with no pre-existing version), the fast path holds and no recreation fires; the next run still sees its own `PYTHONPATH`-resolved imports first, so extra packages in the venv widen the import surface but cannot change which version a pre-existing dep imports. This bounds cross-run version leakage to a single run's scoring output — the flagged run is tagged in the registry as `venv_drift_recovery` (enters Phase 7 as a regression covariate) and subsequent runs execute against a freshly-installed venv. This is acceptable because: (a) `PYTHONPATH` is set to the clone, so the next run's imports still resolve against the clone's tree first; (b) extra packages already in the venv cannot cause a `ModuleNotFoundError` — they only widen what's importable, which is indistinguishable from the Phase 1 installer picking them up; (c) version drift is actively detected and recovered via the pip-freeze diff. **End-of-session rollback**: when `br benchmark run` completes (or on operator invocation of `br benchmark gc-anchors --reset-venv`), the harness removes `.venv-benchmark/` and re-runs `scripts/install-benchmark-deps.sh` so the next benchmark session starts from the deterministic parent-repo requirements set. The venv recreation path on `editable_install_leaked=true` remains the defensive mid-session reset. The runner sets `PYTHONPATH=<clone_path>:<clone_path>/core` so pytest imports the contestant's code from the clone rather than from the outer repo. **Concurrency-serialization**: the shared venv is a single-writer resource when editable installs are in play; concurrent `run_local_tests` invocations (from multiple orchestrators on Muddy, or from parallel pytest processes if `-n` ever gets added) would race on `pip install -e` / `pip uninstall`. The runner holds `/tmp/br3-bench-venv.lock` via `fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX)` around the full `install → pytest → uninstall` sequence. Per-run wall-clock for pytest is bounded by the 5-minute timeout, so worst-case contention is one pending orchestrator waiting ≤5 min to score — acceptable given the orchestrator cadence of ~7 min/run. The lock is also grabbed in `.venv-benchmark/`'s setup/teardown path so concurrent CLI invocations of `br benchmark score --run-id <id>` do not trample each other. If the lock cannot be acquired within a 10-minute ceiling, the scorer surfaces `status="install_failed"` with `reason="venv_lock_timeout"` (scored outcome). **Venv-recreation flock interaction (resolves R24 N7)**: the 10-minute ceiling is generous enough to absorb one forced venv recreation (~30 s) plus one in-flight pytest (~5 min) plus a safety margin. If `venv_version_drift=true` triggers a recreation on run A while run B is waiting at the flock, run B wakes up to a fresh venv and re-runs its own editable install — that is the intended path (version isolation). A second back-to-back drift-triggered recreation is vanishingly rare (drift is <5% of runs per the expected-frequency estimate above), but if it did occur, the ceiling still holds: two recreations + one pytest + overhead ≈ 6.5 min, well under 10 min. Runs that time out under this ceiling are the legitimate `install_failed` scored outcome and the study continues without the timed-out cell (its phase joins the partial-completion exclusion set per Phase 7). If the clone's tree contains a `setup.py` or `pyproject.toml` at the root, the runner does **`.venv-benchmark/bin/pip install --quiet -e <clone_path>` once per run** (editable install pointing at the clone path — **no `--no-deps`**; BR3's `pyproject.toml` declares its full runtime dependency list under `[project].dependencies` (verified 2026-04-16: includes fastapi, uvicorn, typer, rich, pyyaml, gitpython, supabase, anthropic, httpx, watchdog, filelock, psutil, PyJWT, opentelemetry-\*, and others). **`anthropic` import-time safety (resolves R24 W2)**: `import anthropic` does **not** require `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` at import time — the SDK only checks the key when a client method is called (`anthropic.Anthropic().messages.create(...)` raises `AuthenticationError` at call time, not import time). Contestants get `ANTHROPIC_*` stripped from env (per Phase 3 allowlist), so contestant-tree pytest runs that `import anthropic` succeed at collection time; any test that actually instantiates the client and makes an API call surfaces as a natural `status="fail"` (the correct scored outcome for a test that requires credentials the harness deliberately withholds). BR3's own `api/` code that imports `anthropic` is exercised during the editable-install smoke test (Phase 5 baseline sanity check runs `pytest --collect-only` before the first benchmark run) which catches any import-time regression. The pattern holds for all BR3 SDK deps that treat the API key as a call-time concern (openai, supabase, etc.) — these are stripped from contestant env but remain importable. These are **not all** duplicated in `requirements-api.txt` (which only covers the API server subset), so `--no-deps` would leave the clone's tests importing modules that aren't in `.venv-benchmark/`. Letting `pip install -e` resolve `pyproject.toml`'s declared deps is the correct path. The venv is monotonically widened by this install (Phase 1's `requirements-benchmark.txt` + `requirements-api.txt` + `pyproject.toml`'s project deps), which is consistent with the "union of deps, end-of-session reset" policy already specified above. Version drift against a pre-existing pinned dep is caught by the `venv_version_drift` check (see above) and triggers a full venv recreation). **Package-name discovery for teardown `pip uninstall`**: before the editable install, the runner parses `<clone_path>/pyproject.toml` (`project.name` or `tool.poetry.name`) or `<clone_path>/setup.py` (regex `name\s*=\s*['"]([^'"]+)['"]` with AST fallback via `ast.parse` when regex misses) to extract the distribution name. The extracted name is recorded on the `LocalTestResult` as `editable_package_name`. Teardown does `.venv-benchmark/bin/pip uninstall -y <editable_package_name>` keyed by that recorded name so the next run gets a clean editable install. If no `pyproject.toml`/`setup.py` exists at the root, the editable install is skipped entirely and the runner relies on `PYTHONPATH` alone; `editable_package_name` is `None`. If name parsing returns an empty string or a name that `pip show` cannot resolve after install (pip's sanitization of `-` vs `_`), the run flags `editable_install_leaked = true` and the venv is fully recreated at the next run's start to guarantee isolation — this recovery path trades one extra `install-benchmark-deps.sh` invocation (~20 s) for zero cross-run contamination. **Install-time code-execution note (resolves R54 Codex W2)**: `pip install -e <clone_path>` runs the project's PEP 517 build backend / `setup.py` hooks inside the shared host venv with no kernel-level sandboxing, and the plan explicitly accepts this risk with the following mitigations in force: (i) **contestant-trust boundary** — contestants are the two models under test (Claude Opus 4.7 + Codex 5.4) dispatched via `~/.buildrunner/scripts/dispatch-to-node.sh`, NOT arbitrary web input; the harness's threat model is "model-generated code that may be incorrect or undesirable", not "model-generated code that is actively adversarial against the host"; if a contestant's `setup.py` / `pyproject.toml` build-backend hook is found to mutate the host env in a way that breaks a subsequent run, the diff is preserved in the anchor ref `refs/heads/bench/<run_id>` for post-hoc audit and the run is scored as whatever outcome the mutated env produces (typically `install_failed` or a cascading `venv_version_drift` recovery); (ii) **`.venv-benchmark/` isolation** — the editable install writes into `.venv-benchmark/` which is outside the outer repo's source tree and is reset end-of-session (and mid-session on `venv_version_drift`), so any mutation a build backend inflicts on the venv's site-packages is bounded to at most the remainder of the current session; (iii) **environment stripping** — contestants get `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, `OPENROUTER_API_KEY`, `SUPABASE_*`, `GITHUB_TOKEN`, and other secrets stripped from env via Phase 3's dispatch-env allowlist, so a build-backend `os.environ[...]` read cannot exfiltrate credentials; (iv) **anchor-ref provenance** — every run's pre-run and post-run commit SHAs are preserved on the `refs/heads/bench/<run_id>` anchor ref (class (a) of Phase 3's `gc-anchors` classes), so any contestant that mutates the host during install leaves a permanent audit trail; (v) **deliberate non-sandbox choice** — running each install under a `firejail` / `bwrap` / Docker container would add 10–30 s per run × 360 runs ≈ 1–3 hrs to the study and add a significant engineering surface; the accepted risk trade is that the harness runs under the same Muddy orchestrator trust boundary that already trusts the dispatched runtimes (`claude` / `codex`) to produce commits on the parent repo. Runs that fail at the editable-install stage surface as `status="install_failed"` (a scored outcome, not a harness error). This is documented in the methods section of Phase 8's report alongside the `venv_version_drift` and `editable_install_leaked` covariates so a reader can reproduce the exact trust assumptions the study makes.
  - **Node / UI**: if `<clone_path>/ui/package.json` exists, the runner runs `(cd <clone_path>/ui && (if [ -f package-lock.json ]; then npm ci --ignore-scripts --prefer-offline --no-audit --no-fund || npm install --ignore-scripts --no-audit --no-fund; else npm install --ignore-scripts --no-audit --no-fund; fi))` **before** `npm test`. The `|| npm install` fallback covers **stale-lockfile** failures — when a contestant's `package.json` edit does not update `package-lock.json` in lock-step, `npm ci` aborts with a lockfile-sync error; falling back to `npm install` regenerates a consistent tree in the clone and the run proceeds to test. This keeps contestant-intent (the edited `package.json`) decisive rather than penalizing the model for an unrefreshed lockfile that the dispatcher's runtime did not regenerate. **`--ignore-scripts` is mandatory** and applies only to contestant-tree installs: the contestant can modify `package.json` scripts / `postinstall` hooks, and running those lifecycle scripts would be an uncontrolled code-execution vector against the shared host. `--ignore-scripts` suppresses `preinstall` / `install` / `postinstall` / `prepare` for all packages in the contestant's dependency tree. **Baseline-install sanity-check (guards against dependency-requires-postinstall false-positives — 2026-04-16 verification)**: before the benchmark starts, Phase 5's installer runs the same ci-or-install fallback used per-run against the current (pre-benchmark) `ui/` tree — `(cd <repo_root>/ui && (if [ -f package-lock.json ]; then npm ci --ignore-scripts --prefer-offline --no-audit --no-fund || npm install --ignore-scripts --no-audit --no-fund; else npm install --ignore-scripts --no-audit --no-fund; fi))` — and asserts that `npm test -- --run` then passes. The `|| npm install ...` fallback covers the **stale-lockfile** case where `npm ci` aborts because `package.json` and `package-lock.json` are out of sync (npm's exit is non-zero with `EUSAGE` / "can only install packages when your package.json and package-lock.json are in sync"); falling back to `npm install` regenerates a consistent tree without requiring an operator to hand-refresh the lockfile between benchmark runs. If both the ci and install paths still fail under `--ignore-scripts`, that means the project's current UI deps themselves require postinstall hooks to be usable — a state the harness cannot safely run against, so the benchmark refuses to start with a remediation message naming the failing package(s) (from the install stderr). The operator must then either pin alternative dep versions or accept a one-time harness change (outside the scope of this benchmark). Given BR3 currently uses Vite + vitest + React 20 — none of which require postinstall — the baseline check is expected to pass. This baseline assertion is how a contestant's introduction of a postinstall-requiring dep is distinguished from a pre-existing project requirement: the former surfaces as an installed `status="install_failed"` (scored as model failure — the contestant picked a dep that cannot be safely installed under `--ignore-scripts`), while the latter is caught at preflight and blocks the benchmark from running. Phase 1's / Phase 5's own `.buildrunner/benchmarks/tools/` install (for Prettier/ESLint/tsc/jscpd) uses a **harness-controlled, committed `package.json`** and therefore runs scripts normally — the `--ignore-scripts` flag is contestant-tree-only. `npm ci` is the reproducible path when the lockfile exists; the `npm install` fallback only fires if the contestant's edit removed the lockfile. Install timeout 3 min (kill on exceed, surface as `status="install_failed"`). The install step runs exactly once per run (not per test invocation).
  - The runner then executes (1) `.venv-benchmark/bin/pytest -q --tb=no -p no:cacheprovider` (**resolves R30 B4**: `--no-cov` is omitted because Phase 1's `requirements-benchmark.txt` does not pin `pytest-cov`; on a plain pytest install `--no-cov` is an unrecognized-argument error that aborts before tests run. `-p no:cacheprovider` disables the `.pytest_cache/` directory creation so test runs don't write stateful files into the clone that the scorer would then see in the diff) from the clone root if `<clone_path>/tests/` exists, and (2) the Node test invocation: **resolves R30 W5 — decouple from hardcoded `--run`**. The runner parses `<clone_path>/ui/package.json` via `_safe_parse_package_json(<clone_path>/ui/package.json)` — the same shared helper exported from Phase 1's `core/benchmark/deps.py` (resolves R52 B3 — helper was previously declared in Phase 5's `toolchain.py`, which did not exist when Phase 3 imported it under the `1 → 2 → 4 → 3 → 5` build order; relocating to `deps.py` ensures Phase 3's `setup_clone` and Phase 5's Node-scoring path both import from the same single source-of-truth location that exists at Phase 1 time) that wraps `json.loads(path.read_text())` in `try/except json.JSONDecodeError` (**resolves R51 B3 — a contestant whose diff produces invalid JSON in `package.json` (trailing comma, unquoted key, accidental truncation, deliberate sabotage) would otherwise crash the scorer at the `json.loads(...)` call before any verdict can be recorded, converting a scored contestant failure into an uncaught Python exception that aborts the run and contaminates the registry**). On any `JSONDecodeError`, `_safe_parse_package_json` returns the sentinel `{"__malformed__": True, "__error__": str(e), "__path__": str(path)}`; the Node test path detects the sentinel and short-circuits to a scored `status="install_failed"` outcome with `failing_tests=["ui_package_json_malformed"]` and `install_log_tail` populated with the `JSONDecodeError` message. The install step is skipped entirely (there is nothing safe to hand to `npm ci`/`npm install`), and the Node-surface verdict becomes `install_failed` — which the combined-status reducer promotes to an overall `fail` per the existing precedence rule, so the contestant is correctly penalized for producing a broken tree rather than the scorer crashing. The same sentinel check applies at `setup_clone` time for `pre_run_test_surfaces.ui` computation (Phase 3 deliverable): a pre-run malformed `package.json` in the checked-out historical commit yields `ui=False` (no detectable test surface), so the contestant's subsequent post-run malformed `package.json` does not hit the test-surface-deletion guard — this is the correct behavior because the pre-run surface was already absent from the scorer's perspective. Unit test `test_scorer.py::test_malformed_package_json_scored_install_failed` seeds a clone whose post-run `ui/package.json` contains a trailing comma, runs the Node test path, and asserts the verdict is `{status: "install_failed", failing_tests: ["ui_package_json_malformed"], ...}` with no raised exception and a populated `install_log_tail`. Companion unit test `test_safe_parse_package_json_returns_sentinel_on_malformed` validates the helper directly. Only on successful parse does the runner then inspect `scripts.test` to classify the runner: if the value is exactly `"vitest"`, starts with `"vitest "`, or contains `vitest` / ` vitest$` (token-boundary match against the full script string after shell-splitting on whitespace), the runner is classified as **vitest** and the invocation is `(cd <clone_path>/ui && npm test -- --run)` (passing `--run` so vitest exits after one pass instead of entering watch mode). For any other `scripts.test` value — including jest, mocha, a custom wrapper script, or a shell pipeline — the runner is classified as **non-vitest** and the invocation is `(cd <clone_path>/ui && npm test)` with **no positional args and no npm flags appended** (resolves R37 W1 — earlier drafts passed `--silent`, but npm's log-verbosity flag is interpreted as a literal arg by some custom wrapper test scripts via `npm_config_silent` and can break test invocation), letting the project's own test script decide its flags. The classification result is recorded on `LocalTestResult.node_runner_detected: Literal["vitest","other"]` so the report can surface what was invoked. This keeps a contestant whose legitimate change switches `scripts.test` to a non-vitest runner from being mis-scored because `--run` was passed to a tool that does not accept it. `npm test -- --run` is only invoked if `<clone_path>/ui/package.json` exists **and** the parsed JSON has a `scripts.test` key — the `--reporter` flag is omitted; vitest's default reporter writes to stdout and its per-test summary is sufficient for the scorer's pass/fail parse (the scorer reads vitest's JSON-on-stdout behavior via `--run` or, if needed in a future tweak, `--reporter=default` is the supported canonical name, not `basic`). Unit test `test_scorer.py::test_node_runner_detection` covers the four cases: `"vitest"`, `"vitest --coverage"`, `"jest --ci"`, `"node scripts/run-tests.mjs"` — asserts `--run` is appended only for the first two. If either surface is missing, the corresponding half returns `status="no_tests_discovered"` rather than crashing. **Test-surface deletion guard (resolves R29 W1)**: a contestant whose diff removes `<clone_path>/tests/` or `<clone_path>/ui/package.json` (or renames them to something the gate can't find) cannot silently collapse a required test surface into a `no_tests_discovered` free pass — the scorer captures **pre-run surface presence** at `setup_clone` time by recording `pre_run_test_surfaces: {python: bool, ui: bool}` on `CloneHandle` (python = `<clone_path>/tests/` exists AND contains at least one `test_*.py` file; ui = `<clone_path>/ui/package.json` exists AND its parsed JSON has `scripts.test`). At scorer entry, if `pre_run_test_surfaces[X] == True` but the post-run surface is missing/empty, the scorer returns `status="fail"` with `failing_tests=["<surface>_deleted_by_contestant"]` for that surface instead of `no_tests_discovered`. `no_tests_discovered` is reserved for the legitimate case where the surface was absent both before AND after — i.e. a phase whose clone genuinely has no tests. This closes the deletion-as-free-pass hole while keeping the "no tests exist" outcome intact for phases where it is accurate. Unit test `test_scorer.py::test_contestant_deletes_test_surface` seeds a clone with `tests/` and `ui/package.json` present, simulates a post-run diff that removes both, and asserts both surfaces return `fail` with the deletion reason. Test timeouts: 5 min Python, 5 min Node, kill on exceed. Per-surface verdict shape is `{status: Literal["pass","fail","timeout","no_tests_discovered","install_failed"], duration_ms: int, failing_tests: [str], install_log_tail: Optional[str]}`. **Combined-status rule (full 5×5 matrix, no undefined cells)**: `ObjectiveMetrics.local_test_result.combined_status` is computed by a precedence-ordered reducer — (1) if **either** surface is `timeout` → `timeout`; (2) else if **either** is `fail` or `install_failed` → `fail`; (3) else if **both** are `pass` → `pass`; (4) else if **both** are `no_tests_discovered` → `no_tests_discovered`; (5) else (exactly the mixed `pass`+`no_tests_discovered` case — one surface has tests and passed, the other has no tests at all) → `partial_pass`. The `partial_pass` state is added to the `combined_status` Literal (`Literal["pass","fail","timeout","no_tests_discovered","partial_pass"]`) and enters Phase 7's regression as a distinct level of the test-outcome categorical (not collapsed into `pass`, because a one-sided test suite is strictly weaker evidence than a two-sided one). `install_failed` is a scored outcome (contestant produced a tree whose deps can't install → test verdict = fail), not an error — this is how broken `package.json` edits or import breakages surface in the metric. Local-first scoring requires no remote push and no external-API contract, which is why it is the primary path.
- [ ] **Walter enrichment (optional, only if `WalterClient.is_verified()`)**: **does not pass the contestant's `post_run_commit_sha`.** Walter's verdict reflects Walter's own continuously-running test state against _its_ main-branch checkout; the contestant's commit is intentionally not pushed anywhere outside the local repo. The scorer simply calls `WalterClient.get_latest_results(project="BuildRunner3")` at the moment the run completes and records the returned overall pass/fail status on `ObjectiveMetrics.walter_cluster_snapshot = {status: Literal["pass","fail","unknown"], captured_at_utc: str}`. This is a pure **cluster-health snapshot** — it answers "was Walter green when this run finished?" — and does not depend on Walter knowing about the contestant's commit. If `is_verified()` is false, the field is `None`.
- [ ] **Lomax enrichment (optional, only if `LomaxClient.is_verified()` and the `br3-benchmark` project slug pre-exists)**: same snapshot-only contract as Walter. The scorer serializes through the single slug via `/tmp/br3-bench-lomax.lock` (fcntl.flock): acquire → `get_build_status("br3-benchmark")` → read status → release. Lomax's latest build status reflects whatever tree the slug's workspace contains (presumably main-branch), so this is also a **cluster-health snapshot**, not per-run. Recorded on `ObjectiveMetrics.lomax_cluster_snapshot = {status, captured_at_utc}`. `trigger_build` is **not** called from the scoring path; the operator (or a separate periodic cron) can keep the slug fresh if desired. If the slug does not exist or the client is unverified, the field is `None` and Lomax is skipped.
- [ ] **One-time ops procedure for `br3-benchmark` slug (documented, not automated, not required)**: since no Lomax provisioning endpoint has been verified (`POST /api/projects` is **not** in the verified contract), operators who want Lomax enrichment must create the `br3-benchmark` slug through Lomax's own admin workflow (UI or whatever mechanism Lomax exposes). The benchmark never attempts to create the slug. If the slug doesn't exist at preflight, Phase 9 surfaces a warning and proceeds Walter-only / local-only — the study is not gated on Lomax availability.
- [ ] Both enrichment fields enter the Phase 7 regression as cluster-health covariates; they do **not** enter the decision rule. This removes Walter/Lomax from the critical scoring path entirely.
- [ ] File precision/recall vs `phase_spec.declared_files`.
- [ ] Checklist item keyword-match counter (keyword extraction per item documented).
- [ ] Scope-creep LOC (diff lines outside declared files).
- [ ] Per-checklist-item score on a 3-way scale: `delivered` (all keywords present AND matching file touched), `partial` (some keywords OR file touched but not both), `missed` (neither). Scale and tie-breakers documented in `scorer.py` module docstring.
- [ ] Empty / ambiguous / no-keyword checklist items are tagged `unscorable` at parse time and excluded from the item denominator (counted separately in the report).

**Success Criteria:** Scorer handles a real past-phase diff and produces a complete `ObjectiveMetrics` (including `local_test_result`) for every run. Walter/Lomax enrichment fields populate when verified; the scorer never depends on either being available. Partial-credit rule covers every checklist item shape present in the current BR3 BUILD specs.

---

### Phase 6: Third-Party Judge + Blinding Protocol + Format Normalization

**Goal:** Blind pairwise judge dispatched to a non-contestant model. Double-pass with swap. Position-stability detection. Format normalization applied to _source files_, not diffs.

**Files:**

- `core/benchmark/judge.py` (NEW — **resolves R49 B3 Codex judge-export declaration gap**. Owns the `BenchmarkJudge` class used by `Runner.run_cell()`, `cli_judge.py`, and `cli_run.py`. **Declared API surface** (frozen in this phase; no later phase adds methods): (a) `class BenchmarkJudge(config: BenchmarkConfig)` — constructor takes a single `BenchmarkConfig` (matches the one-arg scorer/probe*scheduler pattern declared in `cli_run.py`'s R43 B2 resolution). Internally instantiates an `openrouter.OpenRouterClient(config)` (Phase 6's `openrouter.py` is additive to `openrouter_min.py` — same client type), a `formatter.DiffFormatter(config)`, and a `deblind_classifier.DeblindClassifier(config)`. (b) **`judge_pair(pair_key: PairKey) -> JudgeVerdict`** — the single primary method called by `Runner.run_cell()` and the `br benchmark judge` backfill command after a successful `registry.claim_judge(pair_key, worker_id, session_id)`. Reads the two `CompletedRow{stage="scored", pair_key==target}` rows from `benchmark_registry.jsonl` under `LOCK_SH`, normalizes each side's diff via `formatter.normalize_diff()`, assigns A/B labels via the `sha256(f"{phase_id}|{sub_study}|{replication_index}|{blind_salt}")` blinded-pair rule, dispatches two concurrent OpenRouter chat-completions (GPT-5 primary + Gemini 2.5 secondary) via the `openrouter` client's retry-wrapped helper, parses the structured JSON verdicts per the 5-dimension schema, applies the position-swap double-pass (second pass with A/B swapped; position-unstable pairs return a `JudgeVerdict` with `position_unstable=True`), computes the rater-disagreement flag per the judge-reduction rule, and returns a single `JudgeVerdict` pydantic model (declared in Phase 1's `models.py`) populated with GPT-5's verdict as the primary + Gemini's verdict in the `secondary*\*`fields.`judge_pair`raises`JudgeApiError`on exhausted OpenRouter retries (after the openrouter client's own backoff exhaustion) and`JudgeTimeoutError` on per-pair 90-second timeout — both caught by the caller (`Runner.run_cell()`) which then invokes `registry.release_judge(pair_key, worker_id, session_id, reason=...)`per the Phase 6 runner.py abandon-on-failure contract. (c)`class JudgeApiError(Exception)`and`class JudgeTimeoutError(Exception)`— the two named exception types the caller catches; declared here so`Runner.run_cell()`'s try/except is pinned to these two types exactly (no broad `except Exception:`in the judge-call path).`JudgeApiError.**init**(self, reason: Literal["openrouter_5xx","openrouter_rate_limit","openrouter_auth_error","openrouter_model_not_found"], detail: str)`carries a structured reason that`registry.release_judge`forwards as the`JudgeAbandonedRow.reason`field. (d)`judge_pair`is **side-effect-free against the registry** — it never appends rows; all row writes (JudgeDecisionRow + two CompletedRow{stage="judged"} rows per the three-row commit protocol) are performed by`Runner.run_cell()`under its`LOCK_EX`acquisition after`judge_pair`returns. This keeps the single-writer contract intact:`judge.py`computes verdicts,`runner.py`commits them. Unit tests live in`tests/benchmark/test_judge_blinding.py`(blinding-correctness + A/B assignment determinism) and`tests/benchmark/test_formatter.py`(normalization) already listed below; a new`tests/benchmark/test_judge.py`unit test pinning the`BenchmarkJudge`constructor signature +`judge_pair(pair_key)` return shape is added to Phase 6's test file list below.)
- `core/benchmark/formatter.py` (NEW)
- `core/benchmark/openrouter.py` (NEW — client + auth + retry)
- `core/benchmark/deblind_classifier.py` (NEW — logistic-regression classifier over TF-IDF features of normalized diffs, for the blinding success criterion)
- `core/benchmark/cli_judge.py` (MODIFY — replaces Phase 1's stub body with the real `br benchmark judge` command that dispatches pairs to GPT-5 + Gemini 2.5 via `openrouter.py`, normalizes formatting via `formatter.py`, and writes `JudgeVerdict` rows keyed by **`pair_key = (phase_id, sub_study, replication_index)`** — the pair-stable identifier that joins one Claude `cell_key` with its matched Codex `cell_key` on the same `(phase, sub_study, replication)`. `pair_key` is a top-level required field on every `CompletedRow` regardless of stage (**resolves R52 B1** — Phase 1's schema was updated in R50 B1 to make `pair_key: PairKey` non-optional and populated on `stage="run"`, `stage="scored"`, AND `stage="judged"` rows so the judge's `claim_judge(pair_key)` path can locate scored rows by `pair_key` without scanning by `cell_key` + inferring. The earlier text here that described `pair_key` as `Optional[PairKey]` populated only on judged rows was stale from the pre-R50 schema and contradicted Phase 1's current definition; it is now corrected so the single-source-of-truth for `pair_key`'s shape lives in Phase 1's `CompletedRow` declaration alone). Phase 7's aggregator reduces by `pair_key` for the judge verdict and by `cell_key` for the per-model metrics, so the Bradley-Terry pairwise fit reconstructs exactly one verdict per pair without double-counting. The command body imports from `core/benchmark/judge.py`; `core/benchmark/cli.py` is not touched — it already imports `cli_judge` and calls its `register(app)` hook from Phase 1.)
- `core/benchmark/probe.py` (NEW — **resolves R32 B1 probe-scheduler ownership gap AND R33 B1/B2 API-surface + trigger-contract gap**. Owns the full `ProbeScheduler` API surface used by every caller in the harness: `schedule(phase_id: str, model: str, expected_cell_count: int) -> None` (registers a `(phase_id, model)` pair with the total number of cells expected for it — `expected_cell_count = len(sub_studies) × replications`; called once per `(phase, model)` at session startup by `run_session`), `notify_cell_judged(phase_id: str, model: str) -> None` (**the R33 B1 method that was missing from the prior API listing; now declared here in Phase 6's canonical surface**; called by `Runner.run_cell()` every time a cell reaches `stage="judged"`; increments an internal per-`(phase, model)` counter), `notify_pair_judged(pair_key: PairKey) -> None` (**convenience wrapper that calls `notify_cell_judged(pair_key.phase_id, model)` for each model in the pair** — kept for backward-reference with Phase 6's `run_cell()` wiring, but internally just fans out two `notify_cell_judged` calls; documented as syntactic sugar, not a separate tracking primitive), **`notify_cell_scored(phase_id: str, model: str) -> None` (resolves R48 B1 + R48 W7 — declared here in Phase 6's canonical `probe.py` API surface, NOT in Phase 4. Called by `Runner.run_cell()` every time a cell reaches `stage="scored"` in single-model-run sessions where `len(session_state.selected_models) < 2`. Semantics mirror `notify_cell_judged` — increments an internal per-`(phase, model)` counter — but reads from the scored stage instead of judged. Internally, `notify_cell_scored` shares the same per-`(phase, model)` counter state as `notify_cell_judged`: the scheduler tracks a single `completed` counter per pair, and whichever `notify_*` method is appropriate for the session's mode increments it. `_maybe_fire(phase_id)` then applies its gate against the same counter regardless of mode, so the `expected_cell_count` watermark means "cells that have reached the session's terminal stage" (judged for two-model sessions, scored for single-model sessions). The "never primes" contract (Phase 4 Invariant 15) is preserved in both modes: the recognition probe fires strictly after the run's terminal stage completes — which is `scored` in single-model mode and `judged` in two-model mode. In single-model mode, scored IS the run's final output because no judging follows; the probe therefore cannot prime the run's own output, which is the exact non-priming invariant. Phase 7's regression includes a `session_mode: Literal["single_model","two_model"]` covariate so contamination effects can be analyzed per-mode without pooling the two populations, addressing R48 W7 by making the difference in trigger semantics an explicit analytical covariate rather than an implicit one)**, `run_pending() -> list[RecognitionRow]` (called at orchestrator shutdown and by `br benchmark probe` backfill to re-attempt any `ProbePendingRow`-flagged pairs), and internal `_maybe_fire(phase_id: str)` (fired from `notify_cell_judged`; checks whether **BOTH** `(phase_id, "claude")` AND `(phase_id, "codex")` completed-cell counters have reached their registered `expected_cell_count` values — i.e. the entire phase's 2×N×R cell matrix is fully judged across both models — and, only then, triggers the recognition probe for both models atomically (one probe per model, two probes per phase fired in sequence). **This is the R37 B3 fix reconciling Phase 4's phase-level trigger contract with the scheduler implementation**: Phase 4's Invariant 15 mandates the probe "never primes" by firing strictly after the scored+judged run — and Phase 4's precise trigger wording requires "every `(phase_id, any_model, sub_study, replication)` cell for this phase has a `CompletedRow` with `stage="judged"`", which is a **phase-level** gate across both models. Earlier drafts had `_maybe_fire` take a `(phase_id, model)` pair and fire per-model as soon as that one model's cells were judged, leaving a residual-taint window where the probe for model A could fire while model B's paired judgments were still outstanding (and those still-outstanding judgments could, in principle, be influenced by model A's probe output if any logging leaked). The corrected contract drops `model` from the `_maybe_fire` signature and gates on the both-models-complete condition: the scheduler tracks separate counters per `(phase_id, model)` via `notify_cell_judged(phase_id, model)` as before, but `_maybe_fire(phase_id)` is called after each notification and checks both counters; the `fired: bool` latch prevents double-firing once the watermark is reached. **Subset-aware gating (resolves R45 B3 — `--models` can be a subset of `{claude, codex}`, so the scheduler must not hardcode both-model completion)**: `_maybe_fire(phase_id)` gates on "every `(phase_id, model)` pair **that was registered via `schedule()`** for this phase has its `completed == expected` watermark reached" — i.e. the scheduler only waits on models that were actually scheduled. When `--models claude,codex` is passed (the default), `run_session` calls `schedule(phase_id, "claude", N)` + `schedule(phase_id, "codex", N)` and `_maybe_fire` waits on both; when `--models claude` is passed, only `schedule(phase_id, "claude", N)` fires and `_maybe_fire` waits only on that single model. The scheduler's in-memory state is keyed by the `(phase_id, model)` tuples actually registered, so iteration over `{(p, m) for (p, m) in self.counters if p == phase_id}` naturally yields the subset. Once every registered pair for a phase reaches its watermark, the scheduler fires the probe for each **registered** `(phase_id, model)` in sequence under a single latch. Unit test `test_probe.py::test_scheduler_fires_on_single_model_subset` seeds `schedule(P, "claude", 4)` only (no codex schedule call) and asserts the fourth `notify_cell_judged(P, "claude")` fires the claude probe exactly once and no codex probe is attempted. Unit test `test_probe.py::test_scheduler_fires_only_when_both_models_fully_judged` seeds `schedule(P, "claude", 4)` + `schedule(P, "codex", 4)` and asserts: four `notify_cell_judged(P, "claude")` calls fire no probe; three `notify_cell_judged(P, "codex")` calls still fire no probe; the fourth `notify_cell_judged(P, "codex")` call fires BOTH probes exactly once). The scheduler's state is a purely in-memory `dict[(phase_id, model), {expected: int, completed: int, fired: bool}]` plus a ring-buffer of pending `RecognitionRow`s for the backfill path; on kill/resume the counters are rebuilt by `Runner.resume()` from a registry scan (count `CompletedRow` rows at `stage="judged"` grouped by `(phase_id, model)` and initialize `completed` accordingly). In-process jittered-backoff retries (3 attempts: 2s/8s/32s) are driven from this module; exhausted retries emit a `ProbePendingRow` (Phase 1 schema) for the `br benchmark probe` backfill subcommand. Unit tests: `test_probe.py::test_scheduler_fires_only_when_all_cells_judged` seeds `schedule(P, M, expected=4)` + three `notify_cell_judged(P, M)` calls and asserts no probe fires; a fourth call fires the probe exactly once. `test_probe.py::test_scheduler_idempotent_on_extra_notifications` seeds `expected=2` + three `notify_cell_judged` calls and asserts the probe still fires exactly once (the `fired: bool` latch guarantees idempotence). `test_probe.py::test_notify_pair_judged_fans_out_to_both_models` asserts the pair-keyed convenience wrapper calls `notify_cell_judged` for both `model="claude"` and `model="codex"`. `test_probe.py::test_resume_rebuilds_counters_from_registry` seeds a synthetic registry with some judged rows and asserts the post-resume counters match the registry state.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_probe.py` (NEW — probe scheduler unit tests including pair-completion watermark, retry/backoff, `ProbePendingRow` emission on exhaustion, and idempotence on resume.)
- `core/benchmark/cli_probe.py` (MODIFY — **resolves R34 B2 cli_probe wiring gap**. Phase 4 created the initial `cli_probe.py` body that invoked the legacy in-Phase-4 probe dispatch path. Phase 6 now retargets this file to the canonical `ProbeScheduler` API: `from core.benchmark.probe import ProbeScheduler` at module scope; the `br benchmark probe` command body constructs `scheduler = ProbeScheduler(config)` (one-arg — matches `cli_run.py`/`cli_resume.py` and the canonical signature declared in `probe.py`'s file entry above; resolves R43 B2 — registry access is module-style, never `Registry(config)`), calls `scheduler.run_pending()` (which scans `benchmark_registry.jsonl` for `ProbePendingRow` entries without a matching `RecognitionRow` for the same **`(session_id, phase_id, model)`** triple — **resolves R45 B4** — using the `registry.scan_pending_probes(session_id, all_sessions)` helper declared in Phase 1 (R44 B2); by default scoped to the current `SessionState.session_id`, with `--all-sessions` CLI flag to widen the scan across every session. This matches Phase 4's `(session_id, phase_id, model)` dedup contract (R42 B2) exactly — a different session's `RecognitionRow` never suppresses this session's pending probe. Each un-fulfilled row is re-attempted with the scheduler's 3-retry jittered backoff), prints a summary (`<n_retried> retried, <n_recovered> recovered, <n_still_pending> still pending`), and exits. Phase 4's legacy dispatch helpers in `cli_probe.py` are removed in this MODIFY — the Phase 6 scheduler is now the sole owner of probe retry + backfill semantics. This closes the gap where Phase 6 introduced `ProbeScheduler` but left `br benchmark probe` wired to Phase 4's old path; after this MODIFY, every probe invocation (both the in-run scheduler path and the operator-invoked backfill path) flows through `ProbeScheduler`, guaranteeing consistent retry policy and `RecognitionRow` output shape. Unit test `tests/benchmark/test_cli_probe.py::test_backfill_retries_pending_rows` seeds a synthetic registry with 3 `ProbePendingRow` entries, runs the command body, and asserts 3 fresh probe attempts fire through the scheduler.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_cli_probe.py` (NEW — **resolves R35 B1**: Phase 4 owns `tests/benchmark/test_recognition_probe.py` (scheduler-level tests against the pre-Phase-6 trigger contract), not `test_cli_probe.py`. The CLI-level test file for `br benchmark probe` is a net-new Phase 6 artifact that pins the `ProbeScheduler`-backed backfill wiring introduced in the Phase 6 `cli_probe.py` MODIFY above. Asserts the command body (a) seeds a synthetic registry containing 3 `ProbePendingRow` entries with no matching `RecognitionRow`, (b) invokes the command body via Typer's CliRunner, (c) verifies 3 fresh probe attempts fire through `ProbeScheduler.run_pending()` (patched with a mock that records calls), (d) asserts the command exit code is 0 and the printed summary reports `3 retried, <n_recovered>, <n_still_pending>`. Also asserts the legacy Phase-4 dispatch helpers no longer exist in `cli_probe` via attribute checks on the imported module.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_runner.py` (MODIFY — **resolves R34 W2 (Phase 6 half)**. Phase 6 appends `test_run_cell_appends_two_judged_rows_per_pair` (asserts that when `run_cell()` triggers judge_pair, two stage="judged" CompletedRow rows are appended — one per model — both carrying the same pair_key and verdict) and `test_run_cell_claims_judge_before_judging` (asserts `registry.claim_judge` is called before `judge.judge_pair`, and that a concurrent orchestrator whose `claim_judge` was rejected does NOT call `judge_pair`). Listing the file here makes the test obligations enforceable against a concrete file mutation in Phase 6.)
- `core/benchmark/runner.py` (MODIFY — **resolves R32 B1 orchestrator wiring AND R33 B3 judge-data-model mismatch AND R34 B1 pair-level judge lock**. Phase 6 extends `Runner.__init__` with two new constructor-injected dependencies: `judge: Optional[BenchmarkJudge] = None` and `probe_scheduler: Optional[ProbeScheduler] = None`. `Runner.run_cell()` is extended so that after `self.scorer.score_run()` produces a `stage="scored"` row, the runner attempts to claim the judge slot for this pair via `registry.claim_judge(pair_key, worker_id, session_id)` (new registry method declared in Phase 1 schema addendum — see below). **`claim_judge` semantics (resolves R34 B1 concurrent-orchestrator duplicate-verdict hole)**: under `fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX)` on the registry, scan for any existing `JudgeClaimRow` with matching `pair_key`. If present AND its `lease_expires_at` is in the future → claim rejected, `run_cell` returns without judging (the claiming orchestrator will produce the two `stage="judged"` rows). If present but lease-expired → append `JudgeSupersededRow` and then a fresh `JudgeClaimRow`; claim succeeds. If absent → append a `JudgeClaimRow{row_type="judge_claim", session_id, pair_key, worker_id, claimed_at_utc, lease_expires_at}` and claim succeeds (default lease = 900 seconds = 15 min, configurable via `config.registry.judge_lease_seconds`). If ANY `JudgeDecisionRow` with the matching `pair_key` already exists → claim rejected (judging already complete; this side's `run_cell` just returns — **resolves R50 B2**: the "already judged" sentinel is the `JudgeDecisionRow` (the atomic commit point redefined by R47 B2 and used by `is_pair_judged`), NOT the derived `CompletedRow{stage="judged"}` rows. Keying the claim rejection on the same sentinel as `is_pair_judged` closes the crash-between-appends re-judge hole: after a crash between writing the JudgeDecisionRow and writing one or both CompletedRow{stage="judged"} convenience rows, a resuming orchestrator's `claim_judge` call sees the durable JudgeDecisionRow and rejects; the missing convenience rows are backfilled by `recover_missing_judged_rows` before resume-dispatch runs, not re-derived by a concurrent judge_pair call). **Single-model-run short-circuit (resolves R47 B3 — pair judging is undefined when only one model ran)**: before any judge-claim logic, `run_cell` reads `session_state.get_flag(session_id, "selected_models")` (the persisted subset from Phase 1's `SessionState.selected_models` field, resolving R46 B2). If `len(selected_models) < 2`, the judging step is **skipped entirely** — no `JudgeClaimRow`, no `judge_pair()` call, no `JudgeDecisionRow`, no `CompletedRow{stage="judged"}` rows. The `stage="scored"` CompletedRow from Phase 5 is the **terminal stage** for single-model runs: the cell-key reducer in `runner.resume()` (`_reduce_registry_by_cell_key`) treats `stage="scored"` as `terminal` when `len(session_state.selected_models) < 2`, and Phase 7's aggregator applies the same rule so the analysis dataset treats scored-only rows as complete observations. `ProbeScheduler.notify_cell_scored(phase_id, model)` fires the recognition probe in single-model runs (new method on `ProbeScheduler` — declared above in Phase 6's `core/benchmark/probe.py` file entry API surface, **NOT** in Phase 4 (Phase 4 owns `recognition_probe.py`, Phase 6 owns `probe.py` — resolves R48 W1 cross-reference).
