The method is triggered on scored rows instead of judged rows when session state indicates single-model mode; when `len(selected_models) == 2` the existing `notify_cell_judged` path is used). Phase 8's report marks single-model sessions with a "no-judge-run" caveat: no Bradley-Terry ratings are produced (BT requires pairwise comparisons), only per-phase objective/adherence metrics. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_single_model_run_skips_judge` constructs `run_session(models=["claude"])`, runs one cell through completion, and asserts (a) no `JudgeClaimRow` / `JudgeDecisionRow` / `CompletedRow{stage="judged"}` rows are written, (b) the `stage="scored"` row is the terminal state for the cell, (c) `probe_scheduler.notify_cell_scored()` was called with `(phase_id, "claude")`. Unit test `test_aggregator.py::test_single_model_run_uses_scored_as_terminal` seeds a registry with only `stage="scored"` rows from a `selected_models=["claude"]` session and asserts the aggregator yields per-phase metrics without errors about missing judged rows. **Two-model-run path (unchanged)**: when `len(selected_models) == 2`, the existing judge-claim → judge_pair → three-row commit protocol applies as specified below. Only after a successful claim does the runner proceed to call `self.judge.judge_pair(pair_key)` **iff** the companion cell for that `pair_key` is already at `stage="scored"` in the registry (checked via the same `LOCK_SH` registry read before claim); otherwise the claim is immediately released (`JudgeAbandonedRow{row_type="judge_abandoned", session_id, pair_key, worker_id, reason="companion_not_scored"}` appended under the same lock) and the judge call is deferred — the next-completing companion cell's `run_cell` will re-attempt the claim. This replaces the earlier unlocked "check scored → call judge" read-then-write race with a claim-first, call-second protocol that mirrors the cell-level claim protocol. **After `judge_pair()` returns a single `JudgeVerdict` keyed by `pair_key = (phase_id, sub_study, replication_index)` (symmetric — it names the winner, not the side that appended the row), the runner appends the pair's judged state as a **three-row commit protocol under a single `LOCK_EX` acquisition** (resolves R47 B2 — crash-between-appends atomicity): **(1)** append one `JudgeDecisionRow{row_type="judge_decision", session_id, pair_key, verdict, worker_id, decided_at_utc}` — this single JSONL append is the atomic commit point for the pair's judged state; (2) append `CompletedRow{stage="judged", model="claude", pair_key, verdict: JudgeVerdict (copied by value), run_id, cell_key, RunResult + ObjectiveMetrics + AdherenceMetrics from claude's prior stage="scored" row}`; (3) append `CompletedRow{stage="judged", model="codex", pair_key, verdict, ...}` with codex's payload. All three rows land under the same `LOCK_EX`, so no concurrent orchestrator reader observes a half-committed pair. A **crash between (1) and (2)** or between (2) and (3) is recovered on next orchestrator start: `runner.resume(session_id)` calls `registry.recover_missing_judged_rows(session_id)` which rebuilds the missing CompletedRow{stage="judged"} rows from the durable `JudgeDecisionRow.verdict` + the prior CompletedRow{stage="scored"} rows. `registry.is_pair_judged(pair_key)` now keys off the `JudgeDecisionRow`, not the CompletedRow, so a resumed orchestrator does NOT short-circuit the pair as "already judged" when only one convenience row is on disk. This resolves R33 B3 (both cells reach terminal stage="judged") AND R47 B2 (crash safety): both underlying cells reach the terminal `stage="judged"` state in the registry, the progressive-fill reducer finds one judged row per cell (two per pair), the cell-level reducer selects the correct judged row per model, and the crash-recovery path self-heals before any resume-dispatch decision is made. After the two rows are appended, the runner calls `self.probe_scheduler.notify_cell_judged(phase_id, "claude")` and `self.probe_scheduler.notify_cell_judged(phase_id, "codex")` (two calls — one per model whose cell just reached judged); the scheduler accumulates these and fires the recognition probe only when every cell for each `(phase, model)` pair has reached judged (per the updated Phase 6 B2 trigger contract — see `probe.py` file entry above). The null-coalescing `is None` branches on both dependencies are preserved exclusively for the unit-test constructor path. **Every method added here is net-new in Phase 6 and owned by Phase 6**; Phase 3's existing `Runner` API surface (`run_cell`, `run_session`, `resume`, `dispatch_run`, `setup_clone`, `teardown_clone`) and Phase 5's additions are unchanged in signature — `run_cell`'s body grows two new call sites but its input/output contract does not change. **`run_session` body extension (resolves R36 B4 probe-scheduler initialization gap)**: Phase 6's same `runner.py` MODIFY **also extends `run_session`'s body** so the scheduler's per-`(phase, model)` counters are seeded at session startup before any `run_cell` fires. Immediately after `run_session` resolves its selected phases via `selector.selected_phase_ids` + `selector.get_phase(phase_id)`, the new body adds a nested loop (pseudocode) `if self.probe_scheduler is not None: for phase_id in selector.selected_phase_ids: for model in models: self.probe_scheduler.schedule(phase_id, model, expected_cell_count=len(sub_studies) * replications)` — where `models`, `sub_studies`, and `replications` are the parameters passed to `run_session(selector, replications, models, sub_studies)` (i.e. the CLI-scoped `--models` subset, not the full `("claude", "codex")` tuple). **Resolves R46 B2**: a `--models claude` run registers only claude `(phase, model)` pairs, and `_maybe_fire`'s subset-aware iteration (see Phase 4's `_maybe_fire` contract — iterates only pairs actually registered via `schedule()`) correctly fires recognition probes when the claude-only cell matrix completes. `Runner.resume(session_id)` receives the identical extension but **reads `models` from session-state** via `models = session_state.get_flag(session_id, "selected_models")` (the Phase 1 `SessionState.selected_models` field) before the scheduler loop runs; the same loop body then iterates that persisted subset. This preserves the kill/resume contract: a `--models claude` session killed mid-run and resumed continues to register only claude pairs, not both models. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_run_session_schedules_only_selected_models` constructs `run_session(models=["claude"], sub_studies=[...], replications=5)` with a mock `probe_scheduler` seeded with 3 phases and asserts `probe_scheduler.schedule()` is called exactly 3 times (3 phases × 1 model), never 6 times. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_resume_schedules_only_selected_models_from_session_state` seeds a session-state file with `selected_models=["codex"]`, runs `Runner.resume(session_id)`, and asserts the mock `probe_scheduler.schedule()` is called only with `model="codex"`. **`_resume_scheduler_counters_from_registry(session_id)` helper (resolves R49 W4 — single-model resume dispatches on the session's actual terminal stage)**: `resume` additionally calls this helper immediately after the `schedule()` loop. The helper first reads `models = session_state.get_flag(session_id, "selected_models")` (same persisted subset the `schedule()` loop just iterated) and **dispatches on `len(models)`** to pick the correct terminal-stage scan: **(a) if `len(models) < 2` (single-model session)** — the terminal stage is `scored`, so the helper calls `registry.scan_for_scored_rows(session_id)` (Phase 1 API — see Phase 1's scan-helpers deliverable), groups the returned rows by `(phase_id, model)`, and calls `probe_scheduler.notify_cell_scored(phase_id, model)` once per matching row so single-model counters rebuild against the same stage the in-run path increments against; **(b) if `len(models) == 2` (two-model session)** — the terminal stage is `judged`, so the helper calls the existing `registry.scan_for_judged_rows(session_id)` path, groups by `(phase_id, model)`, and calls `probe_scheduler.notify_cell_judged(phase_id, model)` once per row. The two branches never run together: a session is fixed to one terminal stage for its entire lifetime by the persisted `selected_models` field, so a resumed `--models claude` session never rebuilds counters from `stage="judged"` rows that cannot exist for that session (the in-run path never wrote any), and a resumed two-model session never rebuilds from `stage="scored"` rows (which would double-count, since the cells also have `stage="judged"` rows). This guarantees the scheduler's in-memory `completed` counters match the registry's ground truth under **both\*\* session modes and the scheduler does not re-fire probes that already fired pre-kill. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_resume_single_model_rebuilds_from_scored_rows` seeds a session-state file with `selected_models=["claude"]` and a registry containing 3 `CompletedRow{stage="scored", model="claude"}` rows (no judged rows), invokes `Runner.resume(session_id)`, and asserts `probe_scheduler.notify_cell_scored` is called 3 times with `model="claude"` and `notify_cell_judged` is never called. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_resume_two_model_rebuilds_from_judged_rows` seeds `selected_models=["claude","codex"]` and 4 `stage="judged"` rows (2 per model), asserts `notify_cell_judged` is called 4 times and `notify_cell_scored` is never called. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_run_session_schedules_every_phase_model_pair` seeds 3 phases × 2 models = 6 pairs, asserts `probe_scheduler.schedule()` was called exactly 6 times with `expected_cell_count = sub_studies × replications`. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_resume_rebuilds_scheduler_counters` seeds a registry with some judged rows pre-kill, runs `Runner.resume(session_id)`, and asserts the scheduler's post-resume `completed` counters match the judged-row count per `(phase, model)` pair. Unit test `test_runner.py::test_run_cell_appends_two_judged_rows_per_pair` seeds a synthetic scored pair of cells and asserts the judge call produces exactly two `stage="judged"` `CompletedRow` rows with the same `pair_key` and verdict.)
- `core/benchmark/cli_run.py` (MODIFY — **resolves R32 B1 CLI-side wiring, R42 B3 ProbeScheduler constructor consistency, AND R43 B2 Registry-class fabrication**. Phase 5 already updated `cli_run.py` to construct `Runner(scorer=BenchmarkScorer())`; Phase 6 extends the same constructor call to `Runner(config=config, scorer=BenchmarkScorer(config), judge=BenchmarkJudge(config), probe_scheduler=ProbeScheduler(config))` — **the canonical `ProbeScheduler` constructor signature is `ProbeScheduler(config: BenchmarkConfig)`** (one required positional argument, matching the declaration in `probe.py`'s file entry above). **Registry is a MODULE, not a class** (resolves R43 B2 — Phase 1's `core/benchmark/registry.py` exports module-level functions like `registry.claim(cell_key, worker_id, session_id)`, `registry.claim_judge(pair_key, worker_id, session_id)`, `registry.is_pair_judged(pair_key)`, `registry.is_phase_dropped(phase_id)`, `registry.append_row(row)`, `registry.scan_pending_probes(session_id)`, etc. — there is NO `Registry` class or constructor anywhere in the plan. Every module that needs registry access uses `from core.benchmark import registry` at module scope and calls the functions directly; the registry module reads its own config via an internal `_get_config()` helper that calls `load_config()` lazily on first use and caches the result, so callers never thread a Registry instance through the dependency graph). `ProbeScheduler(config)` therefore takes config only; its internal `_resume_scheduler_counters_from_registry` path and `ProbePendingRow` append path use `from core.benchmark import registry as _registry_module` at module scope and call `_registry_module.scan_for_judged_rows(session_id)` / `_registry_module.append_row(...)` directly. `BenchmarkJudge(config)` and `BenchmarkScorer(config)` follow the same one-arg constructor pattern. `config = load_config()` is constructed at the top of `cli_run.py`'s command body; the `from core.benchmark import registry` import is added at module scope. **Every call site that instantiates `ProbeScheduler` uses the same one-arg signature** — `cli_run.py`, `cli_resume.py`, `cli_probe.py` (see below) — so the class has exactly one constructor contract across the codebase. The imports for `BenchmarkJudge`, `ProbeScheduler`, `BenchmarkConfig`/`load_config`, and the `registry` module are added at module scope. `br benchmark run --pilot` (Phase 9) and `br benchmark run` (Phase 10) inherit this wiring — they call the same `cli_run.py` entry point and get judging + probing integrated into `run_cell()` automatically. No Phase 9 / Phase 10 file change is required to pick up the wiring.)
- `core/benchmark/cli_resume.py` (MODIFY — same dependency extension as `cli_run.py`: construct `Runner(config=config, scorer=BenchmarkScorer(config), judge=BenchmarkJudge(config), probe_scheduler=ProbeScheduler(config))` using the canonical one-arg `ProbeScheduler(config)` signature so resumed sessions continue to judge + probe their in-flight cells. Imports the `registry` module at module scope (not `Registry(config)` — module-style access per R43 B2).)
- `core/benchmark/prompts.py` (MODIFY — judge prompt template)
- `tests/benchmark/test_cli_judge.py` (NEW — **resolves R41 B3 (Codex)**: pins the two unit tests named in the "JudgeVerdict single-writer rule" deliverable below (`test_backfill_skips_already_judged_pairs` and `test_backfill_and_runner_race_single_judgment`). Both tests exercise the `br benchmark judge` backfill command body against a synthetic `benchmark_registry.jsonl` and assert (a) the backfill skips pairs already at `stage="judged"` (does not re-judge, does not double-append) and (b) a concurrent race between `Runner.run_cell()` and `br benchmark judge` on the same `pair_key` resolves to exactly one `judge_pair` call and one pair of `stage="judged"` rows — no duplicate verdicts. This file is listed explicitly because the two test names are referenced by the JudgeVerdict single-writer deliverable below; without the explicit file declaration here the plan would depend on a test file it never creates.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_judge.py` (NEW — **resolves R51 W3**: pins the `BenchmarkJudge` API surface declared in `judge.py`'s Phase 6 file entry. Hosts `test_benchmark_judge_constructor_one_arg_config` (asserts `BenchmarkJudge(config)` is the only legal constructor signature and rejects a zero-arg or two-arg call), `test_judge_pair_returns_verdict_on_scored_pair` (seeds a synthetic registry with two matching `CompletedRow{stage="scored", pair_key==target}` rows, mocks the openrouter chat-completion path, invokes `judge.judge_pair(pair_key)`, and asserts the returned `JudgeVerdict` pydantic model carries GPT-5 primary + Gemini secondary + `position_unstable` populated), `test_judge_pair_raises_judge_api_error_on_openrouter_exhausted` (asserts the named `JudgeApiError` bubbles up to the caller after retry exhaustion, not a raw `HTTPError`), and `test_judge_pair_raises_judge_timeout_error_on_90s_ceiling` (asserts per-pair timeout). Referenced throughout Phase 6's judge.py declaration; without this explicit file the declared API surface would have no scheduled test.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_judge_blinding.py` (NEW)
- `tests/benchmark/test_formatter.py` (NEW)
- `tests/benchmark/test_deblind_classifier.py` (NEW)
- `tests/benchmark/test_openrouter_min_contract.py` (NEW — moved here from Phase 4 because the test can only run once both `openrouter_min.py` (Phase 4) and `openrouter.py` (this phase) exist. Pins the additive-only re-export contract described in Phase 4's `openrouter_min.py` declaration: asserts `set(openrouter_min.__all__) ⊆ set(dir(openrouter))` AND that every attribute in `openrouter_min.__all__` has a compatible `inspect.signature` in `openrouter`. The **invariant** is owned by Phase 4; the **test** is owned by Phase 6 because this is the first phase where both modules coexist. If either module goes missing at test-collection time, the test is skipped with a pytest `skip` marker and a remediation message pointing at the owning phase.)
- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/results/<run_id>/format_coverage.json` (NEW — per-run artifact written by `formatter.normalize_diff()`. Schema: `{run_id: str, files: list[{path: str, extension: str, formatter: Literal["prettier","black","ruff","passthrough"], format_status: Literal["ok","format_failed","unsupported_ext"], reason: Optional[str]}], total_files: int, format_failed_count: int, unsupported_ext_count: int, recovered: bool, format_unrecoverable: bool}`. `recovered=true` means at least one file fell back to raw unformatted content but the run remained scorable; `format_unrecoverable=true` means every file failed to format (the run is excluded from judge analysis per Phase 6's fallback rule). Written via `tmp+fsync+rename`. Read by Phase 7's aggregator (format-failure covariate) and Phase 8's report. Listed here so the owning phase is explicit.)

**Blocked by:** Phase 3, Phase 5 (Phase 6's format normalization requires `toolchain.ensure_installed()` from Phase 5 to be green; this is a hard dependency, not a soft "After:").

**Deliverables:**

- [ ] OpenRouter client with `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` auth, jittered-backoff retries, and structured error surfacing.
- [ ] Judge models: GPT-5 (primary), Gemini 2.5 (secondary). Both run on 100% of pairs.
- [ ] Format normalization: apply Prettier to all source files whose extensions are in `{.ts, .tsx, .js, .jsx, .mjs, .cjs, .json, .md, .css, .scss, .html, .yaml, .yml}` (parser auto-selected by Prettier from extension); Black to all `.py` files; `ruff --fix --select I` for Python import ordering after Black. Apply to **both pre- and post-edit trees**, then regenerate the diff. Files with extensions outside the supported set are passed through unchanged and flagged in `format_coverage.json`. Judge sees the normalized diff only. Requires `toolchain.ensure_installed()` from Phase 5 to be green.
- [ ] **Format-failure fallback (per-file, not per-run)**: when Prettier/Black/ruff exits non-zero on a specific file (typical causes: syntax error in contestant output, truncated JSON, invalid Python), the formatter catches the non-zero exit, tags that file `format_failed: true, reason: <stderr_snippet>` in `format_coverage.json`, and uses the **raw unformatted content** for that file when regenerating the diff. This preserves the run as scorable (the judge sees the raw file, which is a correct representation of broken output — broken output SHOULD score low), prevents a single malformed file from crashing the pipeline, and produces a log artifact for post-hoc review. A run is only aborted if **every** file in its diff fails to format (extreme corruption case), in which case the run is marked `format_unrecoverable` and excluded from judge analysis. Unit test: feed a known-broken Python file alongside a valid one and verify the pipeline continues and the coverage map is accurate.
- [ ] Metadata stripping: no commit messages, no git log, no model identifiers, no file timestamps.
- [ ] Deterministic A/B label assignment via **`sha256(f"{phase_id}|{sub_study}|{replication_index}|{blind_salt}")`** — seeded on the `pair_key` (stable across both sides of the judged pair and across re-judging passes / implementations), **not** on attempt-scoped `run_id`. `blind_salt` is read from `.buildrunner/benchmarks/config.yaml:blinding.blind_salt` via `load_config()`. This guarantees the same judged pair gets the same A/B labels every time — across the primary pass, the swap pass, re-runs from registry state, and independent reimplementations — so Phase 7's aggregation never sees label-drift artifacts.
- [ ] Double-pass: each pair judged twice with A/B positions swapped.
- [ ] Position-unstable pairs (winner flips on swap) flagged and excluded from primary analysis.
- [ ] `JudgeVerdict` parsed into structured JSON (5 dimensions + overall winner).
- [ ] **JudgeVerdict single-writer rule (resolves R40 W3 — two call paths can produce `stage="judged"` CompletedRow rows for the same `pair_key`: (a) `Runner.run_cell()` automatically post-scoring when both halves of a pair reach `stage="scored"` in the same session; (b) the standalone `br benchmark judge` operator-invoked backfill subcommand scanning the registry for un-judged scored pairs. Without an explicit rule, both paths could produce duplicate/conflicting verdicts for the same pair, double-counting in Phase 7's Bradley-Terry aggregator)**: the single-writer invariant is keyed on `pair_key` and enforced by the pair-level `registry.claim_judge(pair_key, worker_id, session_id)` lock (declared in Phase 1's registry API surface). The canonical policy is:
  - **`Runner.run_cell()` is the PRIMARY writer** for in-session pairs. When both halves of a `pair_key` reach `stage="scored"` inside the same live benchmark session, the runner holding the second half's `cell_key` claim attempts `registry.claim_judge(pair_key, worker_id, session_id)`. On success (no prior `JudgeClaimRow` active AND `registry.is_pair_judged(pair_key) == False` — i.e. no `JudgeDecisionRow{pair_key==target}` exists; **resolves R54 Codex B2**: the "already judged" sentinel in `claim_judge`'s success-gate is the durable `JudgeDecisionRow`, NOT the derived `CompletedRow{stage="judged"}` convenience rows, matching the post-R47-B2 `is_pair_judged` commit-point redefinition and the `br benchmark judge` backfill's skip predicate at line 443. This alignment guarantees that after a crash between the `JudgeDecisionRow` append and the two `CompletedRow{stage="judged"}` convenience-row appends, a resuming orchestrator's `claim_judge` call sees the same sentinel as `is_pair_judged` and correctly rejects the claim as `rejected_already_judged`, closing the re-judge hole) it calls `judge.judge_pair(pair_key)` and appends the two `stage="judged"` rows under `LOCK_EX`, then calls `registry.release_judge(pair_key, worker_id, session_id, reason=...)` if it elected to abandon. **This path writes for every pair whose both halves score successfully during the run.**
  - **`br benchmark judge` is the BACKFILL writer only.** Its command body scans `benchmark_registry.jsonl` for `pair_key` values where both sides have a `CompletedRow{stage="scored"}` AND `registry.is_pair_judged(pair_key) == False` (**no `JudgeDecisionRow{pair_key==target}` exists — resolves R48 W11 by matching Phase 1's post-R47 B2 `is_pair_judged` semantics exactly: the commit point is the `JudgeDecisionRow` sentinel, NOT the `CompletedRow{stage="judged"}` convenience rows; earlier draft text here referenced the stale `CompletedRow{stage="judged"}` semantics and would mis-skip pairs whose decision row exists but whose convenience rows are still being rebuilt by `recover_missing_judged_rows`**) AND no live `JudgeClaimRow` holds the pair. For each such pair, it invokes the same `registry.claim_judge(pair_key, worker_id, session_id)` path as `run_cell`; a successful claim produces the two `stage="judged"` rows via the same code path. **If `is_pair_judged(pair_key) == True` — i.e. `Runner.run_cell()` already judged the pair in-session — the backfill subcommand skips the pair silently and prints it in the "already judged" summary count.** The backfill never overwrites an existing `stage="judged"` row, never appends a second `stage="judged"` row for a `pair_key` that already has one, and never attempts to "re-judge" a position-unstable pair (those are excluded at the primary analysis level, not re-processed by backfill).
  - **Operator use cases for backfill, all covered by the "no existing judged row" guard**: (i) a pair whose second-half scoring completed after the orchestrator was killed, so `run_cell()` never got to claim the judge slot; (ii) a pair whose in-session `claim_judge` succeeded but `judge_pair()` raised (network error, API timeout) and the claimer emitted a `JudgeAbandonedRow` before release; (iii) a past session whose operator elected to run judging offline rather than in-session (e.g. to batch judge costs across multiple completed sessions). All three paths funnel through the same `claim_judge → judge_pair → two-row append under LOCK_EX → release_judge` sequence.
  - **Concurrency across orchestrators**: the `claim_judge` lease is a pair-scoped lock (per the Phase 1 registry API declaration); two concurrent processes (one `br benchmark run` orchestrator + one `br benchmark judge` backfill) that race on the same `pair_key` both attempt `claim_judge`; exactly one claim succeeds under `LOCK_EX`, the other sees either `rejected_active_lease` (claim held by the other) or `rejected_already_judged` (the other completed before this one's claim attempt). No duplicate `stage="judged"` rows can be appended for the same `pair_key` even under worst-case concurrency.
  - **Unit test `test_cli_judge.py::test_backfill_skips_already_judged_pairs`**: seeds a synthetic registry with two pairs — pair A has both sides scored AND a `stage="judged"` row for both models from `Runner.run_cell()`; pair B has both sides scored AND no judged row; runs the backfill command body; asserts `judge.judge_pair` was called exactly ONCE (for pair B) and NOT for pair A, and asserts the final registry has exactly two `stage="judged"` rows per pair (pair A unchanged, pair B newly judged) — no double-appending for pair A.
  - **Unit test `test_cli_judge.py::test_backfill_and_runner_race_single_judgment`**: seeds a pair at `stage="scored"` on both sides and simulates two concurrent `claim_judge` calls (one from `Runner.run_cell()`, one from backfill); asserts exactly ONE of the two proceeds to `judge_pair`, the other gets `rejected_active_lease`, and the final registry has exactly two `stage="judged"` rows (one per model) — no duplicate verdicts.
  - **Aggregator guard (defensive; should be unreachable given the lock)**: Phase 7's cell-key reducer (see Phase 1 deliverable "Attempt → cell reducer") emits a `duplicate_cell_completion` warning if it ever observes two non-superseded `stage="judged"` rows for the same `cell_key`; the guard exists purely as a safety net for a clock-skew or filesystem-corruption edge case. Under normal operation the single-writer rule above guarantees the warning never fires.
- [ ] **Judge reduction rule (resolves R20 B14 / R16 C2 "how two judges reduce to one verdict")** — every pair is scored by both GPT-5 and Gemini 2.5; the single `JudgeVerdict` row that enters Phase 7's Bradley-Terry fit is computed as follows: (1) **GPT-5 is the verdict-of-record** — its `overall_winner` and per-dimension scores are what land in the canonical `JudgeVerdict` that the aggregator consumes for the primary BT fit. (2) **Gemini is the inter-rater reliability signal** — its verdict is stored alongside (as `JudgeVerdict.secondary_*` fields) and used to compute an overall agreement rate, per-dimension Cohen's κ, and per-pair disagreement flags, but does not change the primary winner. (3) **Rater-disagreement flag**: a pair is flagged `rater_disagreement = true` when (a) the two judges' `overall_winner` fields disagree, OR (b) on 3 or more of the 5 dimensions the absolute score difference between GPT-5 and Gemini exceeds 2 points on the 1–5 Likert scale (i.e. `sum(abs(gpt5_dim[i] - gemini_dim[i]) > 2 for i in dimensions) ≥ 3`). (4) **Primary vs sensitivity analysis (R16 C2 explicit)**: rater-disagreement pairs are **included** in the primary BT fit using GPT-5's verdict (Phase 7's primary analysis consumes all non-position-unstable pairs, period — excluding 10–15% of pairs because Gemini disagreed would bias the sample toward "easy" pairs and distort the BT ratings). They are additionally fed into a **sensitivity analysis** that re-fits BT on the subset of pairs where the two judges agree on `overall_winner`; if the two BT fits produce winners with overlapping 95% bootstrap CIs and consistent sign of the rating delta, the verdict is reported as robust. If the sensitivity fit flips the winner or widens CIs to include zero, the report's caveats section flags the result as "judge-sensitive" and the decision rule in `decision-rule.md` is applied with the rater-disagreement flag surfaced to the operator. (5) **Position-unstable pairs are excluded from BOTH fits** — they are a separate failure mode handled by the double-pass swap logic, not merged into the judge-disagreement bucket.
- [ ] Inter-judge agreement (GPT-5 vs Gemini) logged; reported but not gating.
- [ ] **De-blinding classifier (blinding-success check)**: `deblind_classifier.py` implements a scikit-learn `Pipeline([TfidfVectorizer(analyzer="char_wb", ngram_range=(3,5)), LogisticRegression(max_iter=1000, class_weight="balanced")])` that tries to predict which model produced a given normalized diff. **Evaluation is 5-fold stratified GROUP cross-validation over the full 84-row pilot with `phase_id` as the grouping key** (not plain `StratifiedKFold`, which would leak replication-level similarity across folds because the 3 replications per `(phase, model, sub_study)` cell are near-duplicates of the contestant's work on the same spec — training on rep 1 and testing on rep 2 of the same phase/model inflates accuracy). The correct primitive is `sklearn.model_selection.StratifiedGroupKFold(n_splits=5, shuffle=True, random_state=<blind_salt_int>)` with `groups = phase_id_column` — this keeps every replication/sub_study row for one phase inside a single fold (so no two rows sharing a phase ever span train and test) while still stratifying the class balance across folds. Invocation: `cross_val_score(pipeline, X, y, groups=phase_ids, cv=StratifiedGroupKFold(n_splits=5, shuffle=True, random_state=<blind_salt_int>))`. With 7 phases and 12 rows per phase (`2 models × 3 reps × 2 sub-studies`), each fold holds out 1 or 2 phases (≈ 12 or 24 rows) and trains on the remaining 5-6 phases; the 84-row OOF prediction set is still complete and the `k_observed / n` gate below is unchanged. If the pilot runs at reduced N (5-6 surviving phases) `StratifiedGroupKFold` still applies — `n_splits` is clamped to `min(5, n_phases)` with the clamp logged in `pilot_deblind.md`. `scikit-learn >= 1.4` ships `StratifiedGroupKFold` (added in 0.24), so the existing `requirements-benchmark.txt` pin is sufficient — no new dependency is needed. Each of the 84 rows is held out exactly once, yielding a single 84-prediction out-of-fold vector; the **accuracy statistic** reported is `(correct predictions across all 84 OOF predictions) / 84`, which is a single binomial outcome with `n = 84` (not a per-fold average). The gate is computed from the exact one-sided binomial upper 95% CI for `p = 0.5` at `n = 84`: using `scipy.stats.binomtest(k=k, n=84, p=0.5, alternative="greater")`, the smallest integer `k_crit` such that `p_value(k_crit) ≤ 0.05` is **51** (verified: `binomtest(50, 84, 0.5, alternative="greater").pvalue = 0.0506 > 0.05`; `binomtest(51, 84, 0.5, alternative="greater").pvalue = 0.0315 ≤ 0.05`). So the **chance-ceiling gate is 50/84 ≈ 0.5952 (59.5%), rejecting only at ≥ 51/84 ≈ 60.71%**. Classifier accuracy must be `≤ 50/84` to pass; `≥ 51/84` is a blinding failure. The exact `k_crit` for the achieved `n` (if `n` ever deviates from 84 because of pilot attrition) is recomputed from `binomtest` at runtime — no hardcoded fractions — and the computed `k_crit`, the achieved `n`, and the observed accuracy are all written to `pilot_deblind.md`. The previous "80/20 split → n=16 → 62.5% threshold" formulation was a statistical miscalibration (binomial CI with n=16 is much wider than with n=84; the same α=0.05 one-sided gate at n=16 is actually ≈68.75%, and holding out only 16 rows wastes 68 rows of evaluable signal). This deliverable supersedes any earlier numerics elsewhere in the spec; Phase 9's remediation ladder references this formula, not a fixed percent. `scikit-learn>=1.4` and `scipy>=1.11` are in `requirements-benchmark.txt`.

**Success Criteria:** A pair is judged end-to-end, blinded correctly. The de-blinding classifier scores at or below the size-adjusted chance threshold (see the deliverable above: 5-fold stratified CV over all 84 pilot rows, `k_crit = 51`, pass region `accuracy ≤ 50/84 ≈ 59.5%`, reject region `accuracy ≥ 51/84 ≈ 60.71%`; both values recomputed exactly from `scipy.stats.binomtest(..., alternative="greater")` at the actual achieved `n`).

---

### Phase 7: Statistical Analysis Engine + Pre-Registered Hypothesis List

**Goal:** Aggregator produces Bradley-Terry ratings, mixed-effects coefficients, clustered bootstrap CIs, BH-corrected p-values, pre/post-cutoff strata — all against a hypothesis list frozen before Phase 10 runs.

**Files:**

- `core/benchmark/aggregator.py` (NEW)
- `core/benchmark/stats.py` (NEW)
- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/hypotheses.md` (NEW — pre-registered hypothesis list, frozen before Phase 10)
- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/decision-rule.md` (NEW — `runtime.json` update rule, frozen before Phase 10)
- `tests/benchmark/test_stats.py` (NEW)
- `tests/benchmark/test_aggregator.py` (NEW — includes **`test_single_model_run_uses_scored_as_terminal`** (resolves R48 W2 + W3 orphan-test reference): seeds a registry with `stage="scored"` CompletedRows from a `session_state.selected_models=["claude"]` session plus no JudgeDecisionRows, invokes the Phase 7 aggregator, and asserts (a) no crash about missing judged rows, (b) per-phase objective/adherence metrics are returned, (c) Bradley-Terry fitting is **skipped** (not attempted with degenerate pairwise data), (d) the aggregator's output pydantic model's `single_model_mode` field is `True` and `bt_ratings` is `None`. Companion test `test_two_model_run_requires_judged_terminal` seeds a two-model session whose registry has only `stage="scored"` rows and asserts the aggregator raises `IncompleteRunsError` (two-model runs without judged rows are incomplete and must not be aggregated). Additional coverage: `test_aggregator_respects_session_mode_covariate` asserts Phase 7's regression includes `session_mode: Literal["single_model","two_model"]` as a covariate per the R48 W7 resolution in Phase 6's probe.py API surface declaration.)

**Note:** `requirements-benchmark.txt` and the `.venv-benchmark/` installation are owned by **Phase 1** (Phase 5 delegates to Phase 1's installer for the Python side and only adds the Node toolchain). Phase 7 consumes them; it does not re-create them.

**Blocked by:** Phase 5, Phase 6

**Deliverables:**

- [ ] **Single-model-mode aggregator path (resolves R48 W3)**: the aggregator's entry point reads `session_state.get_flag(session_id, "selected_models")` as its first step. If `len(selected_models) < 2`, the aggregator **short-circuits the Bradley-Terry fit and the mixed-effects pairwise-comparison regressions** (both require pairwise data that does not exist in single-model runs) and produces a per-model descriptive report only: per-phase `ObjectiveMetrics` + `AdherenceMetrics` summary tables, per-sub-study pass rates, and the recognition-probe covariate still enters as a per-phase descriptor. The aggregator's output pydantic model carries `single_model_mode: bool` (True when `len(selected_models) < 2`) and `bt_ratings: Optional[BradleyTerryRatings]` (None in single-model mode; populated in two-model mode). The reducer treats `stage="scored"` as the terminal stage when `single_model_mode=True` (no judged rows required; their absence is expected). A two-model session that encounters only `stage="scored"` rows for any cell raises `IncompleteRunsError` — the two-model-mode rule still requires judged as terminal. Phase 8's report template reads `single_model_mode` and switches its narrative: the single-model template omits the "Bradley-Terry comparison" section, prints a "single-model run caveat" headline, and formats the per-model descriptive tables. Phase 10's decision rule in `decision-rule.md` is a no-op in single-model mode: `runtime.json` is explicitly NOT touched (the study cannot decide between two models if only one ran); the report prints "single-model run: default preserved; no cross-model decision produced." Unit test coverage in `test_aggregator.py::test_single_model_run_uses_scored_as_terminal` + `test_two_model_run_requires_judged_terminal` + `test_single_model_mode_skips_bt_fit` (declared in the Files-list entry above).
- [ ] `hypotheses.md` enumerates every BH-corrected comparison (overall BT gap, per sub-study, per cutoff stratum, per layer, per-dimension judge scores). BH is applied across this frozen list only.
- [ ] `decision-rule.md` codifies the **single canonical decision rule used by both Phase 9 and Phase 10** (all rules pre-registered before Phase 10 execution — any later section of this spec that appears to state degraded-N thresholds explicitly defers to this document):
  - **Primary rule (`N ≥ 30`, full target):** "Change `runtime.json` default to X iff the lower bound of the 95% clustered-bootstrap CI on the Bradley-Terry rating gap favors X on both the native and neutral sub-studies, AND the cost-veto condition (>2× token cost OR >2× wall-clock at the median) does not apply."
  - **Degraded-sample rule (pre-registered, used whenever achieved N < 30):** If the achieved N (phases that passed all filters after paraphrase-equivalence exclusions) is `25 ≤ N < 30`, the CI gate stays at 95% **and** the BT gap effect size must exceed 0.15 Bradley-Terry logits. If `20 ≤ N < 25`, tighten the CI gate to a **99% lower bound** (and the effect-size gate is dropped — the wider CI at the tighter level does the same work). If `N < 20`, the full study is declared inconclusive, `runtime.json` is **not touched**, and the report states "insufficient phases passed filters; default preserved."
  - **Phase 10's summary wording in its deliverables section is a paraphrase, not a competing rule** — the canonical source is `decision-rule.md` written in Phase 7 and committed before Phase 10 launches. Any apparent discrepancy between Phase 10's prose and `decision-rule.md` is resolved in favor of `decision-rule.md`; this precedence is stated inline in both places.
  - **Deviation handling:** Any deviation from the above is documented as an exception with written justification in the report.
- [ ] Bradley-Terry pairwise rating via pure-Python minorization-maximization (MM) algorithm (Hunter 2004) implemented in `stats.py` — no external `choix` dependency. Unit-tested against the 4-team worked example from Hunter's paper; tolerance 1e-6 on returned ratings. Clustered bootstrap CI on rating gap.
- [ ] Mixed-effects logistic regression (binary outcomes, phase as random intercept) controlling for `recognition_score`, `node_name`, `equivalence_validator`, `walter_cluster_snapshot.status`, and `lomax_cluster_snapshot.status`. **Implementation path**: `statsmodels.genmod.bayes_mixed_glm.BinomialBayesMixedGLM` is the supported random-intercept binomial GLMM in statsmodels 0.14; it is listed in `requirements-benchmark.txt` (`statsmodels>=0.14,<0.15`). The fit uses the variational Bayes posterior (`fit_vb()`) with random intercept on `phase_id`; fixed effects are the covariates listed above. **VB-posterior caveat (methods-section note)**: `fit_vb()` returns a variational approximation, not exact posterior samples; VB can underestimate variance on skewed binomial data. The report's methods section explicitly labels any BBMGLM result as "variational approximation; coefficients are MAP-adjacent, uncertainty intervals may be anticonservative" so downstream readers interpret CIs appropriately. This caveat is cited alongside every BT / CI number that derives from a BBMGLM fit. Fallback: if BBMGLM fails to converge within 200 iterations on a given dataset, the aggregator falls back to a cluster-robust fixed-effects logit (`statsmodels.discrete.discrete_model.Logit` with `cov_type='cluster', cov_kwds={'groups': phase_id}`) which collapses the random intercept into clustered standard errors. Both paths yield phase-clustered inference; the fallback is logged as a caveat. `equivalence_validator` enters as a categorical fixed effect (`below` / `deepseek` / `both` / `na`) so heterogeneous validation does not become hidden variance, consistent with Phase 4's promise. Walter/Lomax cluster-health covariates enter as categorical controls and are **automatically dropped** (not an error) under three conditions: (a) all observations share the same value (single-level factor not estimable); (b) the covariate column is entirely `None`/`NaN` (e.g. Walter unverified for the whole run — this is the all-missing case); (c) <2 observations per level after filtering. **Single-node fallback**: if the session-state flag `preflight_single_node` is true, or if the observed number of distinct `node_name` values in the dataset is 1, the `node_name` covariate is dropped the same way. All auto-drops are logged in the report's methods section and flagged as caveats. Unit test `test_aggregator.py` covers all four auto-drop paths with synthetic data.
- [ ] Linear mixed model for continuous scores (item nested in phase).
- [ ] Clustered bootstrap — resample phases not items, 10k iterations.
- [ ] **Partial-completion exclusion rule**: a phase is "complete" iff all `model × sub_study × replication` cells have a `CompletedRow` AND (if the phase's pair got a `RecognitionRow`, it is present — otherwise the phase is treated as probe-missing and its `recognition_score` column is NaN). A phase missing ≥1 completed cell (run crashed, killed, or never dispatched) is flagged `partial` in the aggregator and **excluded from the primary Bradley-Terry fit and the decision rule**; it is included in a separate sensitivity analysis that pools pairwise-complete cells only. The exclusion rule keeps the BT rating comparison balanced (equal cell counts per model) which is the assumption underlying the CI bounds. Partial phases and their cell-counts are listed explicitly in the report's caveats section.
- [ ] Benjamini-Hochberg correction applied across the pre-registered hypothesis list.
- [ ] Hodges-Lehmann effect size estimator with CI.
- [ ] Pre-cutoff vs post-cutoff stratified fits with coefficient comparison.
- [ ] Power analysis report for the achieved sample size.

**Success Criteria:** Given synthetic input with a known effect, aggregator recovers it within the reported CI. Hypothesis list is committed and frozen before Phase 10 execution begins.

---

### Phase 9: Pilot Run (N=7, full pipeline dry run)

**Goal:** Execute a 7-phase dry run to shake out harness bugs, profile performance, and confirm API costs.

**Files:**

- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/results/pilot/` (NEW)
- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/reports/pilot_report.md` (NEW)
- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/reports/pilot_deblind.md` (NEW — de-blind gate outcome artifact. Schema (markdown with front-matter YAML): front-matter `{n: int, k_observed: int, k_crit: int, pass_ceiling: float, outcome: Literal["pass","fail"], remediation_applied: bool, remediation_details: Optional[str], measured_at_utc: str}`, followed by a human-readable narrative section. Written by `core/benchmark/deblind_classifier.py` after the pilot run's blinding-success gate is evaluated. Consumed by Phase 9's `pilot_report.md` (included as a sub-section) and by Phase 10's preflight (which refuses to launch if `outcome == "fail"` and `remediation_applied == false`). This is the single source of truth for the de-blind gate's pass/fail decision; Phase 6's reject region and Phase 9's reject region are byte-identical in `k_observed` space by construction (both read the same `k_crit` formula at runtime).)
- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/pilot_contention.json` (NEW — written by `core/benchmark/pilot_contention.py` during Phase 9; read by Phase 10's `deps.py`. **Path and schema are the single source of truth defined here and must match Invariant 14 byte-for-byte.** Schema: `{"drop_lomax": bool, "ratio": Optional[float], "otis_median_ms": Optional[int], "lomax_median_ms": Optional[int], "observed_scoring_serial_p95_seconds": Optional[float], "p95_sample_size": Optional[int], "measured_at_utc": str}` (**resolves R53 B4 — `p95_sample_size` present in producer schema, Phase 1 pydantic model, and Phase 10 consumer; all three aligned on one JSON shape**) (**resolves R50 B3** — the `observed_scoring_serial_p95_seconds` field is now declared on both producer (this artifact + `pilot_contention.py`) and consumer (Phase 10's `deps.read_pilot_contention()` + venv-lock budget-revalidation gate) sides, matching Phase 1's `PilotContention` pydantic model exactly). `ratio`, `otis_median_ms`, `lomax_median_ms`, and `observed_scoring_serial_p95_seconds` are nullable (JSON `null`) because the insufficient-sample path explicitly writes nulls when either bucket has fewer than 8 samples and the serial-scoring path writes null when the pilot produced no `stage="scored"` rows; pydantic `Optional[...]` is the correct type for both producer and consumer so no validation fails on the fallback path. `drop_lomax` is always bool; `measured_at_utc` is always string.)
- `core/benchmark/pilot_contention.py` (NEW — the contention measurement implementation. Phase 9 is the sole writer of this module; Phase 10 consumes only the JSON artifact. Responsibilities: scan `.buildrunner/benchmarks/benchmark_registry.jsonl` (canonical path; the registry file Phase 1 creates) for `CompletedRow` entries and apply **two filters in order (resolves R31 B8)**: (a) **session filter** — keep only rows whose `CompletedRow.session_id` equals the pilot `session_id` passed in via `--session-id <id>` (a new required CLI flag on `python -m core.benchmark.pilot_contention`); rows from concurrent non-pilot `br benchmark run` invocations are dropped; (b) **stage-dedupe** — reduce each `(run_id)` group using the progressive-fill stage precedence `judged > scored > run` (same rule as `runner._reduce_registry_by_cell_key`) so each run_id contributes exactly one row to the bucket, eliminating the triple-count across `stage="run"` + `stage="scored"` + `stage="judged"` copies of the same run. After both filters, split the deduplicated set by `CompletedRow.node_name` into Otis and Lomax buckets, compute each bucket's median wall-clock as `median([row.run_result.wall_clock_ms for row in bucket])` — **wall-clock lives on the nested `RunResult`, not on `CompletedRow` top-level**, per Phase 1's dataclass schema; there is no `CompletedRow.wall_clock_ms` field and the module must never read that name — compute `ratio = max(lomax_median, otis_median) / min(lomax_median, otis_median)` (per Invariant 14's definition), load `threshold = config.pilot.contention_ratio_threshold` and `min_samples = config.pilot.contention_min_samples_per_bucket` (both declared in Phase 1's `BenchmarkConfig`; canonical defaults 1.10 and 8), and decide `drop_lomax = (ratio is not None AND ratio > threshold AND len(otis_bucket) >= min_samples AND len(lomax_bucket) >= min_samples)`. **No numeric literal is hardcoded in this module** — the threshold and sample floor are both config-loaded so the operator can tune them via `config.yaml` without editing Python, and the unit test seeds both fixtures with a known config to exercise the threshold-at-boundary cases. Registry field names used: `CompletedRow.node_name`, `CompletedRow.run_result.wall_clock_ms`, `CompletedRow.created_at_utc` — all per Phase 1's pydantic row definitions, no aliases. If either bucket has <8 samples the runner writes `drop_lomax=false, ratio=null, otis_median_ms=null, lomax_median_ms=null` (all three nullable fields go null together so a partial read is impossible), and Phase 10's deps.py falls back to the live-node-count-only path per Invariant 14's fallback rule. **Serial-scoring measurement (resolves R50 B3)**: additionally, the module computes `observed_scoring_serial_p95_seconds` by iterating the pilot's deduplicated rows that reached `stage="scored"` (i.e. at least one `scored` row per cell after the stage-dedupe filter) and for each such row computing `scoring_duration_ms = scored_row.created_at_utc - matching_run_row.created_at_utc` (the elapsed time between the `stage="run"` append and the `stage="scored"` append, which bounds the `install → pytest → npm test → uninstall` venv-lock-held wall-clock). Takes the 95th percentile of those durations using a sample-size-aware selector (**resolves R52 W3 — `statistics.quantiles(data, n=20)` requires `len(data) >= 2` to return any quantiles at all AND returns a list of exactly `n-1 = 19` cut points; indexing `[18]` on a partial-pilot bucket with 1 scored row raises `StatisticsError("must have at least two data points")` and on 2–19 scored rows returns a degraded 19-cut interpolation whose `[18]` index is the max of the tiny sample — neither failure mode is the documented `null` artifact schema the rest of the plan expects, so the module would crash or silently mis-report p95 for partial pilots**): `if len(scoring_durations) == 0: p95 = None; elif len(scoring_durations) == 1: p95 = scoring_durations[0] / 1000.0 (single-sample degenerate — the one observation IS the p95 estimate, recorded with a `p95_sample_size=1`companion field so Phase 10 can detect and widen its tolerance); elif len(scoring_durations) < 20: p95 = max(scoring_durations) / 1000.0 (small-sample fallback —`statistics.quantiles(..., n=20)[18]`is not meaningful below 20 samples, so the module reports the sample maximum as a conservative upper-bound estimate AND records`p95_sample_size=len(scoring_durations)` alongside the value so Phase 10's budget revalidation can treat small-sample p95s with reduced confidence); else: p95 = statistics.quantiles(scoring_durations, n=20)[18] / 1000.0 (canonical p95 path, only taken with ≥20 samples)`. The `PilotContention` pydantic schema (Phase 1 + Phase 9 file schema) is extended with a new field `p95_sample_size: Optional[int]` set to `None` when `observed_scoring_serial_p95_seconds is None`, and to the actual count (1, 2–19, or ≥20) otherwise; Phase 10's budget revalidation reads this field and applies a small-sample widening factor when `p95_sample_size < 20`. Unit test `test_pilot_contention.py::test_observed_scoring_serial_p95_single_sample` seeds 1 scored row and asserts `p95 == that row's duration` with `p95_sample_size == 1`; `test_observed_scoring_serial_p95_small_sample_fallback` seeds 10 scored rows with durations 30s–300s and asserts `p95 == 300.0` (the max) with `p95_sample_size == 10`; `test_observed_scoring_serial_p95_canonical_path` seeds 25 scored rows and asserts the canonical quantile formula fires with `p95_sample_size == 25`; `test_observed_scoring_serial_p95_zero_rows` seeds zero scored rows and asserts `p95 is None` with `p95_sample_size is None`. If the pilot produced zero scored rows (pilot aborted before any scoring completed), writes `null`; Phase 10's budget gate then skips the p95 comparison and proceeds with the baseline 5–6 min budget. Unit test `test_pilot_contention.py::test_observed_scoring_serial_p95` seeds a synthetic registry with 20 run+scored row pairs spanning 60s to 300s scoring durations and asserts the written p95 matches the expected 95th percentile within 1s. **Module entrypoint**: the file ends with `if __name__ == "__main__": main()` where `main()` is a small Typer or argparse wrapper parsing `--registry`, `--out`, AND `--session-id <id>` (required — the pilot session whose rows to analyze) CLI args, so `python -m core.benchmark.pilot_contention --registry ... --out ... --session-id <pilot_session>` (the invocation Phase 9's deliverable uses) dispatches into the measurement logic. Without this idiom the module would be import-only and the Phase 9 deliverable's CLI invocation would fail.)
- `tests/benchmark/test_pilot_contention.py` (NEW — unit tests over synthetic registry fixtures that exercise the overlap classifier and the ratio computation; includes edge cases for empty parallel set, empty serial set, and single-node dispatch.)

**Blocked by:** Phase 8

**Deliverables:**

- [ ] `br benchmark run --phases 7 --replications 3 --sub-studies native,neutral --pilot` completes.
- [ ] **Per-cell result targets** (every successfully-dispatched cell produces exactly one `RunResult`): `achieved_phases × 2 models × 3 replications × 2 sub-studies` runs complete with valid `RunResult` rows. The **target** `achieved_phases` is 7 (yielding 84 runs); the **minimum acceptable** `achieved_phases` is 5 (yielding 60 runs). To protect against paraphrase/equivalence failures shrinking the pool below the minimum, Phase 9 invokes Phase 2's `selector.select_with_buffer(target=7, buffer=3)` (declared explicitly in Phase 2's API surface). If after paraphrase + equivalence filtering at least 7 candidates survive, the pilot uses the first 7 in deterministic selector order and the run target is 84. If 5–6 survive, the pilot runs at that reduced N (60–72 runs) and its success criterion adjusts proportionally — the de-blinding binomial gate, judge-human agreement, and harness-bug-free criteria all apply at the actual `n` achieved via the runtime-recomputed `k_crit` formula in Phase 6. If fewer than 5 survive, the pilot is aborted and the harness surfaces the paraphrase-failure rate — this is a Phase 9 failure mode that must be resolved before Phase 10 (likely by revisiting the paraphraser model or tightening the BUILD-spec filters). The report logs the actual achieved N and run count.
- [ ] Scorer produces complete metrics for every run.
- [ ] Both judges produce verdicts for every pair.
- [ ] Human validation step produces an agreement rate on ≥ 30 pilot items.
- [ ] Pilot report generated end-to-end.
- [ ] Any high-severity harness bugs (crash, data loss, missing metric) are logged and fixed before Phase 10.
- [ ] **De-blinding classifier gate (remediation step)** — **single source of truth is Phase 6's formula.** Phase 6 defines the classifier as 5-fold stratified CV over all 84 pilot rows, with `k_crit` = smallest integer `k` such that `scipy.stats.binomtest(k, n, 0.5, alternative="greater").pvalue ≤ 0.05`. At `n = 84`, `k_crit = 51`; pass region is `k_observed ≤ k_crit - 1 = 50` (accuracy ≤ 50/84 ≈ 59.5%); reject region is `k_observed ≥ k_crit = 51` (accuracy ≥ 51/84 ≈ 60.71%). Phase 9 uses that same formula at Phase 9's actual achieved `n`; it does not hardcode percents. Let `pass_ceiling = (k_crit - 1) / n` computed at runtime (at `n=84`, `pass_ceiling = 50/84 ≈ 0.5952`). **The pass test is strict-inequality on `k_observed`, not on the fraction** to avoid float-rounding off-by-one: the classifier passes iff `k_observed ≤ k_crit - 1` (equivalently `k_observed < k_crit`); the literal fraction `pass_ceiling` is used for reporting only. The remediation ladder, phrased in `k_observed` terms to stay exactly consistent with Phase 6:
  - `k_observed ≤ k_crit - 1` (accuracy ≤ `pass_ceiling`) → blinding succeeded, proceed to Phase 10.
  - `k_crit ≤ k_observed ≤ k_crit - 1 + ceil(0.06 × n)` (a ~one-σ buffer at n=84; `sqrt(0.25/84) ≈ 0.055`, rounded up; at n=84 the buffer is ≤ 56/84 ≈ 0.667) → tighten the format normalization (uniformize quote styles, strip trailing-whitespace-only diffs, widen parser coverage to `.mdx` if present in training rows) and re-run the pilot normalization step once; retest. If the re-test is `≤ k_crit - 1`, proceed; otherwise, abort.
  - `k_observed > k_crit - 1 + ceil(0.06 × n)` → abort immediately — do not proceed to Phase 10; log the de-blinding failure, surface identified leakage features (top-weighted TF-IDF tokens from the trained LogisticRegression), and schedule a harness redesign.
  - The remediation attempt and its outcome are committed to `.buildrunner/benchmarks/reports/pilot_deblind.md`, along with the exact `k_crit`, `n`, `k_observed`, and `pass_ceiling = (k_crit - 1) / n` values computed at runtime. Phase 9's reject region and Phase 6's reject region are **byte-identical** in `k_observed` space (no contradiction possible).
- [ ] Runtime + cost measurements used to re-budget Phase 10 (see Phase 10 budget math, which includes per-run overhead for paraphrase + equivalence + judge + probe).
- [ ] **Contention measurement artifact written** — at the end of the pilot, Phase 9 invokes `python -m core.benchmark.pilot_contention --registry .buildrunner/benchmarks/benchmark_registry.jsonl --out .buildrunner/benchmarks/pilot_contention.json --session-id <pilot_session_id>` (the `<pilot_session_id>` is the UUID minted by the pilot's `br benchmark run --pilot` invocation, passed through from the pilot's Typer context; resolves R31 B8 so only this session's rows are analyzed). The module scans `CompletedRow` entries in the canonical registry, filters by `session_id == <pilot_session_id>`, deduplicates each `run_id` group via the `judged > scored > run` stage precedence, then groups each deduplicated row by `CompletedRow.node_name` into `otis` and `lomax` buckets, computes `otis_median_ms = median([row.run_result.wall_clock_ms for row in otis_bucket])`, `lomax_median_ms = median([row.run_result.wall_clock_ms for row in lomax_bucket])` — **the wall-clock reads go through the nested `RunResult.wall_clock_ms` only, never a non-existent `CompletedRow.wall_clock_ms` field, per Phase 1's dataclass schema** — `ratio = max(otis_median_ms, lomax_median_ms) / min(otis_median_ms, lomax_median_ms)`, loads `threshold = config.pilot.contention_ratio_threshold` and `min_samples = config.pilot.contention_min_samples_per_bucket` (Phase 1's `BenchmarkConfig`; canonical defaults 1.10 and 8 — `pilot_contention.py` reads both via `load_config()` and does not hardcode either literal), and sets `drop_lomax = (ratio > threshold AND len(otis_bucket) >= min_samples AND len(lomax_bucket) >= min_samples)` — exactly Invariant 14's rule. Writes the JSON artifact at `.buildrunner/benchmarks/pilot_contention.json` with the schema `{drop_lomax, ratio, otis_median_ms, lomax_median_ms, measured_at_utc}`. If either bucket has fewer than `min_samples` samples, writes `drop_lomax=false, ratio=null`, and Phase 10's deps.py falls back to the live-node-count-only path per Invariant 14's final sentence. **Phase 9 is the sole writer of `pilot_contention.json`; Phase 10's `deps.py` is the sole reader. The artifact's path and field names are identical in Invariant 14, the Phase 9 Files list, and this deliverable — no duplication, no drift.**

**Success Criteria:** Pilot report complete, judge-human agreement ≥ 70%, zero high-severity open harness bugs. Achieved N meets the over-draw rule above (≥5 surviving phases with proportionally-adjusted run count, not strictly 84). Low-severity bugs are permitted but logged.

---

### Phase 10: Full Benchmark Run (360 runs) + Public Report

**Goal:** Execute the full 30-phase study and publish the trustworthy result.

**Budget math:** 30 phases × 2 models × 3 replications × 2 sub-studies = **360 runs**. Per-run wall clock breaks down into: dispatch + contestant generation ~4–5 min (measured at pilot), plus paraphrase ~20s (Llama-3.1-405B via OpenRouter), plus equivalence check ~15s (Below NLI + DeepSeek cross-check), plus format normalization ~10s, plus **local scorer install → pytest → npm test → teardown ~5–6 min** (the dominant serialized step — see venv-lock reconciliation below), plus two-judge double-pass ~45s (GPT-5 + Gemini 2.5 each twice), plus recognition probe ~10s (run post-scoring, fresh process) = **~11–13 min per run end-to-end**. **Venv-lock reconciliation (resolves R49 W5 — the earlier "~6–7 min per run, ~20 runs/hour" estimate was materially optimistic because it did not reconcile the shared `/tmp/br3-bench-venv.lock` serialization with multi-node parallelism)**: Phase 5's `run_local_tests` holds `fcntl.flock(LOCK_EX)` on the shared venv for the full `install → pytest → npm test → uninstall` sequence (~5–6 min worst case including mid-run recreate paths — see Phase 5 deliverable's 10-min ceiling). This single flock is **process-wide across Muddy** and is acquired by every orchestrator worker regardless of which node it was dispatched to, so two orchestrator workers on Otis + Lomax cannot overlap their scoring sections — worker B waits at the flock until worker A releases. The **parallelism ceiling for the end-to-end pipeline is therefore bounded by the scoring step**, not by dispatch or generation: at ~5–6 min/run serialized scoring time, the theoretical maximum throughput is ≈ 10–12 runs/hour even with infinite dispatch-side parallelism. With Otis + Lomax dispatch overlap hiding the ~4–5 min generation step behind concurrent scoring on the contra-node, effective observed throughput is **~10 runs/hour (two-node path)**, not the 20 runs/hour the earlier estimate assumed. Revised budget: **360 runs ÷ 10 runs/hour = ~36 hours of cluster time across five to six overnight windows**. **Single-node fallback budget:** if Invariant 14 collapses the pool to Otis only (Lomax too contended or offline), dispatch parallelism disappears entirely and the pipeline becomes fully serial at ~11–13 min/run ⇒ ~5 runs/hour ⇒ ~72 hours across ten overnight windows. **Alternative path (per-clone venv, not taken)**: switching to a per-clone venv (each run gets its own `.venv-benchmark-<run_id>/`) would eliminate the flock but adds ~30 s of venv-creation cost per run (~3 hours total over 360 runs) AND breaks the baseline-drift isolation contract that motivates the shared-venv design (no baseline to drift against when each run starts fresh). The plan keeps the shared-venv + flock design and accepts the 10 runs/hour ceiling; operators who want faster wall-clock can run Phase 10 across more overnight windows rather than restructure the venv contract. Either path is acceptable; the schedule is re-validated against the Phase 9 pilot's **measured serialized-scoring time** and measured throughput **before** Phase 10 launches, and a written budget-revision note is committed before the full run begins (covering either the two-node path, the single-node fallback path, or a measured-throughput adjustment, whichever the pilot observed). The Phase 9 pilot includes an explicit `pilot_contention.json` field `observed_scoring_serial_p95_seconds` that is compared against the 5–6 min budget — a p95 above 8 min triggers a budget-revision note before Phase 10 starts.

**Files:**

- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/results/full-n30/` (NEW)
- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/reports/full-n30_report.md` (NEW)
- `.buildrunner/benchmarks/reports/full-n30_data.jsonl` (NEW)
- `.buildrunner/runtime.json` (MODIFY — only if the pre-registered decision rule is satisfied)
- `core/benchmark/deps.py` (MODIFY — Phase 10 adds a `read_pilot_contention()` helper that loads `.buildrunner/benchmarks/pilot_contention.json` (Phase 9's artifact), returns a typed `PilotContention` pydantic model matching Phase 9's schema, and is called by `deps.execution_preflight()` to gate Phase 10's node-pool decision per Invariant 14. Phase 1 owned `deps.py` for all preflight/dependency logic; Phase 10's one-helper addition is the single Phase 10-scoped read path for Phase 9's forward-referenced artifact. **The `PilotContention` pydantic model is pre-declared in Phase 1's `models.py`** — its schema matches Phase 9's `pilot_contention.json` byte-for-byte, so Phase 10's MODIFY adds only the reader helper, not any schema type. This keeps Phase 1's "every schema declared up-front" invariant intact.)

**Blocked by:** Phase 9

**Deliverables:**

- [ ] Hypothesis list (`hypotheses.md`) and decision rule (`decision-rule.md`) are committed _before_ Phase 10 execution starts.
- [ ] `br benchmark run --phases 30 --replications 3 --sub-studies native,neutral` completes all **achieved** runs (resumable). "Achieved runs" = `achieved_phases × 2 models × 3 replications × 2 sub-studies`, where `achieved_phases = selector.surviving_phase_count` — a single read-only property on the Phase 2 selector instance (see Phase 2's Selector API surface deliverable). **`surviving_phase_count` is the single source of truth for "how many phases actually made it into the final scored pool" (resolves R33 W1)**: it counts only phase_ids whose paraphrase AND equivalence filters passed (i.e. phases for which at least one `CompletedRow` with `stage="scored"` or `stage="judged"` exists in the registry, filtered to the current session_id) — replacement phases enqueued by `redraw()` that themselves subsequently fail paraphrase or equivalence are NOT counted (they appear in `redraw_map` as reservations but produce no `CompletedRow` rows, so they are excluded from `surviving_phase_count`). This replaces the earlier additive formula `pool_survivors_after_paraphrase_equivalence + replacement_phases_enqueued_by_redraw` which was shown to over-count because the second term measured reservations, not successes. The two earlier properties remain on the selector for diagnostic/reporting purposes (they appear in the caveats section for transparency) but are **not** used to compute `achieved_phases`. The **target** is 360 runs at `achieved_phases == 30`; the **accepted floor** is `achieved_phases >= 24` (288 runs) with all fewer-run outcomes governed by `decision-rule.md` (see next deliverable). This reconciles the earlier "360 runs" with the candidate-pool safeguard: "completes all 360" applies when no phase drops force a redraw pool exhaustion; otherwise the run completes `achieved_phases × 12` cells and the decision-rule.md thresholds apply. The success criterion at the bottom of this phase is stated in `achieved_phases`, not a fixed run count.
- [ ] **Candidate-pool exhaustion safeguard**: the selector returns `min(30, available)`. If paraphrase-fail exclusions (Invariant 16) bring the pool below 30 mid-run, `selector.redraw(dropped_phase_id)` (Phase 2 deliverable) is called with the stratified replacement rule. Any `stratum_violation` entries logged by `redraw` are surfaced in the report's caveats. **Degraded-sample-size handling is governed by `.buildrunner/benchmarks/decision-rule.md` (canonical source, committed in Phase 7, frozen before Phase 10).** Phase 10 does NOT restate the thresholds here — any paraphrase of the rules earlier in this spec was a source of contradiction and is removed. At Phase 10 run time, the achieved N is measured after filters, the decision-rule.md thresholds are applied mechanically, and the achieved N plus any stratum violations are recorded verbatim in the report's caveats section.
- [ ] All objective, adherence, and judge metrics collected across both sub-studies.
- [ ] Byron completes the human-validation step (target 60, floor 30).
- [ ] Final report with the caveats section prominent at the top.
- [ ] Bradley-Terry ratings with clustered-bootstrap CIs published.
- [ ] Pre/post-cutoff stratification reported.
- [ ] Raw JSONL archived for future re-analysis.
- [ ] `runtime.json` edit contract: read the current file `{"schema_version": "br3.runtime.config.v1", "default_runtime": <current>}`, set `default_runtime` to the winner per `decision-rule.md`, preserve `schema_version` and any other keys. Write atomically (`tmp + fsync + rename`). Pre-flight asserts `schema_version == "br3.runtime.config.v1"`; if the schema version has changed, the harness refuses to write and surfaces a manual-intervention report entry.
- [ ] If the decision rule is not satisfied, `runtime.json` is left untouched and the report records "no change: decision rule not satisfied, default preserved".

**Success Criteria:** Report passes internal review. `runtime.json` state (changed or preserved) matches the pre-registered decision rule mechanically.

## Parallelization Matrix

| Phase | Key Files                                                                      | Can Parallel With | Blocked By     |
| ----- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ----------------- | -------------- |
| 1     | `core/benchmark/{models,cli,registry,deps}.py`, `cli/main.py`                  | —                 | —              |
| 2     | `core/benchmark/{selector,training_cutoffs,api_clients,lockres}.py`            | —                 | 1              |
| 4     | `core/benchmark/{paraphraser,equivalence,recognition_probe,openrouter_min}.py` | —                 | 2              |
| 3     | `core/benchmark/{runner,node_allocator,prompts}.py`                            | —                 | 1, 2, 4        |
| 5     | `core/benchmark/{scorer,pass_at_k,toolchain}.py`                               | —                 | 2, 3           |
| 6     | `core/benchmark/{judge,formatter,openrouter,deblind_classifier}.py`            | —                 | 3, 4, 5 (hard) |
| 7     | `core/benchmark/{aggregator,stats}.py`, `hypotheses.md`, `decision-rule.md`    | —                 | 5, 6           |
| 8     | `core/benchmark/{human_validator,reporter}.py`                                 | —                 | 7              |
| 9     | `.buildrunner/benchmarks/results/pilot/`                                       | —                 | 8              |
| 10    | `.buildrunner/benchmarks/results/full-n30/`                                    | —                 | 9              |

**Build order:** `1 → 2 → 4 → 3 → 5 → 6 → 7 → 8 → 9 → 10`. Phase 4 moves before Phase 3 because the runner imports `paraphraser.paraphrase_spec()` and `equivalence.check_equivalence()` — paraphrasing must happen before dispatch, so the paraphraser module must land before the runner that calls it. This ordering also eliminates the previously-claimed (4, 5) parallel pair; empirically that pair was never worth chasing given each is ≤1 day of work and they share the same reviewer. Phase 6 depends on Phase 4's `openrouter_min.py` (re-exported and extended). Note on `prompts.py`: Phases 3, 6, and 8 all modify this file sequentially (per the build order above), so no cross-worktree merge is needed — the original namespaced-sections convention is kept only as a coding-style guideline.

## Out of Scope (Future)

- Harness-diversity study (aider vs Cursor vs Cline) — single harness now.
- Third model comparison (Gemini, Qwen, local) — two-model focus first.
- Continuous re-benchmarking on every model release — manual re-run.
- Public leaderboard publication — internal use first.
- Held-out test set beyond 10 phases — current set only.
- Languages beyond Python + TypeScript — BR3-specific.
- UI dashboard for results — markdown reports only.
- Automated per-task runtime routing — manual toggle based on report.

---

## Risks

| Risk                                                 | Mitigation                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| ---------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| OpenRouter access to GPT-5/Gemini lapses mid-run     | **Pause + resume**; the pre-registered dual-judge protocol requires **both** judges to score every pair (Phase 6), so single-judge fallback is explicitly disallowed — it would change the analysis population and invalidate the inter-judge-agreement statistic. If one judge is permanently unavailable, Phase 10 is paused (not restarted), the `resume` checkpoint preserves already-scored rows, and execution continues once the judge is restored. If both are unavailable, pause and retry. |
| Walter flakes inflate test-pass variance             | pass@k averages across replications; flakes logged and reported separately.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| Paraphraser changes semantic difficulty accidentally | Symmetric NLI equivalence check via Below; fail the run on non-equivalence rather than continuing.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| Judge-human agreement below 70% on pilot             | Rubric revision required before Phase 10.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| Cluster contention during the long run               | Schedule four overnight windows; Otis + Lomax dedicated during windows; resume handles interruptions.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| Byron doesn't have time for 60-item validation       | Floor is 30; report carries a reduced-calibration caveat between 30 and 60.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| Two sub-studies disagree on winner                   | Decision rule requires both to favor challenger; otherwise default is preserved.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| Result is "no clear winner"                          | Valid outcome — default stays, report produces cost/speed breakdown for per-task routing.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| Node hardware confound                               | `NodeAllocator` balances every (model, node) cell within each phase; `node_name` enters the regression as a covariate.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| Training-cutoff metadata wrong                       | Cutoffs are plan constants; cutoff-stratified analysis is sensitivity analysis, not the headline number.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
